Dishonest use of these monies therefore is not stealing from a private person but <i>me`ilah</i> from Heaven’s property.</i>. If somebody pays his <i>sheqel</i> from Temple money, if the sums were disbursed and the animal sacrificed he committed <i>me`ilah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">Temple money in general is money intended for the upkeep of the Temple. <i>Sheqalim</i> are mainly used to buy sacrifices. Using one for the other is alienation from the original intent but not <i>me`ilah</i>, which is committed only if <i>sancta</i> are used for profane purposes. If the money which he took from Temple money is actually used to buy a sacrifice, he does not have to take from his profane money to pay the <i>sheqel</i>; using the corresponding profane money makes the act larceny.</i>. From Second Tithe or Sabbatical money, he shall eat correspondingly<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">Second Tithe is produce to be eaten in Jerusalem in purity. The produce may be redeemed and the money taken to Jerusalem (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 14:22-27" href="/Deuteronomy.14.22-27"><i>Deut</i>. 14:22–27</a>). Similarly, Sabbatical produce has to be eaten, not used in industry. If such produce was sold, the proceeds are to be used to buy produce of the Land to be consumed in the Land. If such money was alienated from its original use, the situation can be repaired in replacing it with new money to be used for the original purpose.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “He who pays the <i>sheqel</i>,” etc. We have stated, “if the sums were disbursed.” In the House of Rebbi it was stated, “if the animal was sacrificed.<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">Even in the first sentence of the Mishnah.</i>” Rebbi Eleazar said, who is the Tanna of “if the animal was sacrificed”? Rebbi Simeon, since Rebbi Simeon said, he receives his money immediately, the priests are quick<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">The statement of R. Simeon is <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 4:5:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.4.5.2">Halakhah 4:11</a>. The Mishnah there states that flour and wine bought by the Temple are bought on condition that they be qualified to be used on the altar. The risk that the flour might have worms or the wine be vinegar has to be carried by the seller; therefore he cannot be paid before the produce is used and found qualified. R. Simeon disagrees since the Cohanim will do the checking immediately. Therefore if we interpret that “the sums were disbursed” not that they were taken from the treasury to the office of the buying agent but that they were actually contracted for sacrificial animals, for R. Simeon there is no practical difference between the two statements. (Tosephta <i>Me`ilah</i>1:21).</i>. It is difficult. If somebody stole another’s elevation offering and slaughtered it without special mention, is it not without special mention atoning for the original owner<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">The entire Mishnah seems to be baseless. Since the <i>sheqalim</i> become part of a large sum, it is impossible to know whose <i>sheqel</i> pays for what and when his particular <i>sheqel</i> is disbursed.</i>? Rebbi Yudan said, explain it if it was a definite object, like that of the House of Rabban Gamliel who was taking aim throwing it into the chest<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 3:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.3.3.1">Mishnah 3:3</a>. In the House of Rabban Gamliel I they took their <i>sheqel</i> and threw it into the box from which sacrifices were bought; they had control over the time when their <i>sheqel</i> was used.</i>. But should one not worry that maybe it will become part of the remainder; is there <i>me`ilah</i> for the remainder<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 4:2:3-5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.4.2.3-5">Halakhah 4:3</a>, the leftover monies could be used for many needs of the Temple other than sacrifices; therefore larceny of these monies was not <i>me`ilah</i> which required a special sacrifice; R. Meïr disagrees and seems to restrict the uses of the money to sacrificial objects enumerated in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 4:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.4.2.1">Mishnah 4:3</a>. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 54a" href="/Kiddushin.54a">Babli <i>Qiddušin</i>54a</a>.</i>? But it must follow Rebbi Meïr, since Rebbi Meïr said, there is <i>me`ilah</i> for the remainder. Still if it was a definite object, like that of the House of Rabban Gamliel who was taking aim and disbursed it in his name<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">There can be <i>me`ilah</i> only if the misappropriated <i>sheqel</i> can be traced to the moment of its actual use for sacrifices.</i>.
How does he profit<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote">In order to be guilty of <i>me`ilah</i>, one not only must use a sacred object illegally but also profit from the action (Mishnah <i>Me`ilah</i>5:1).</i>? Rebbi Abbin said in the name of the rabbis there, since the court could take a pledge from but did not take any pledge he is like one who profited.
It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 27:26" href="/Leviticus.27.26"><i>Lev.</i> 27:26</a>.</i>, <i>but a firstling which is born first to the Eternal by a domestic animal no person can declare holy</i>. No holiness can fall on anything holy<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">The argument is based on the second part of the verse, not quoted in the text: <i>whether ox or sheep, it [already] is the Eternal’s</i>; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Arakhin 8:7" href="/Mishnah_Arakhin.8.7">Mishnah <i>Arakhin</i>8:7</a>. The problem addressed is how to rectify the situation that tithe or sabbatical money was taken for the <i>sheqel</i>. Not only is there an obligation to make up for the value taken but the coin given as <i>sheqel</i>, being already holy (of a minor degree) cannot possibly acquire the holiness of monies dedicated to the Temple. Without rectification, the use of the coin by the Temple authorities would be sinful.</i>. What does he do? He brings a profane tetradrachma and says, the monies of Second Tithe wherever they be<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning the coins given as <i>sheqel</i>.</i> are redeemed by this tetradrachma; this is designated as Second Tithe and the others<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning the coins given as <i>sheqel</i>.</i> are declared <i>sheqalim</i>.

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If somebody collects coins and says, “these are for my <i>sheqel</i>,” the House of Shammai say, the excess is gift<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">To be given into the gift account of the Temple treasury from which elevation offerings are bought to occupy the altar when otherwise it would be idle.</i>, but the House of Hillel say, the excess is profane<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in the Halakhah and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 2:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.2.3.1">Mishnah 4</a>, a <i>sheqel</i> is a fixed sum and it is reasonable to assume that only the amount necessary was dedicated. The price of an animal for a sacrifice is variable; since the person is ready to spend the entire amount, the entire amount is dedicated.</i>. “That I shall take from these for my <i>sheqel</i>,” they agree that the excess is profane. “These are for a purification offering,” they agree that the excess is gift, “that I shall take from these for a purification offering,” they agree that the excess is profane.<br>Rebbi Simeon said, what is the difference between <i>sheqalim</i> and a purification offering<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">As stated in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 2:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.2.3.1">Mishnah 3</a>.</i>? It is that <i>sheqalim</i> have a fixed value and a purification offering has no fixed value. Rebbi Jehudah said, <i>sheqalim</i> also have no fixed value. When Israel returned from the Babylonian exile they gave as Temple tax <i>darics</i><sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">A Persian gold coin.</i>, they continued to give <i>sela`im</i><sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote">In old Babylonian sources the <i>silā</i> is the standard (Sumerian) unit of volume. In the Talmudim, it is the standard expression for the silver tetradrachma (approximately 14g), roughly corresponding to the old Phoenician <i>sheqel</i>. In the context here, a similar Persian coin must be intended. The vocalization סֶלַע is customary (from the Hebrew word “rock”); probably סִלַע historically would be more correct.</i>, they continued to give minted coins<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote">In this context meaning the silver didrachma.</i>, they wanted to give denars<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote">But this reduction was never accepted, see the Halakhah.</i>. Rebbi Simeon said, anyhow everybody gave the same<sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote">While the value of the <i>sheqel</i> was not constant in time, at any given time everybody knew exactly what was required.</i>, but for a purification offering, one brings for a tetradrachma, another for two, and still another for three.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “If somebody collects coins,” etc. <sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in the Halakhah and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 2:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.2.3.1">Mishnah 4</a>, a <i>sheqel</i> is a fixed sum and it is reasonable to assume that only the amount necessary was dedicated. The price of an animal for a sacrifice is variable; since the person is ready to spend the entire amount, the entire amount is dedicated.</i> Rebbi Yose in the name of Rebbi Eleazar, where do they disagree? If he collects small change<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">One does not know what sum was accumulated without counting the copper coins. But since exactly 2 silver denars are needed, if silver coins are collected and the owner says, these are <i>sheqalim</i>, all of them are dedicated according to everybody.</i>. But if he says, these [are for my <i>sheqel</i> ]<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition. The addition is unnecessary as shown by all parallel sources and the following statement of R. Ḥizqiah. It obscures the main point that the collector of the coins says “these”, not “from these”. In the latter case everybody agrees that the excess is profane; in the first case R. Yose holds that “these” dedicated all coins in the box whereas R. Bevai holds that, in case the amount needed is known beforehand, only the amount needed is dedicated.</i>, everybody agrees that the excess is gift. Rebbi Ḥizqiah, Rebbi Bevai in the name of Rebbi Eleazar, where do they disagree? If he collects small change. But if he says, these, everybody agrees that the excess is profane. Rebbi Ḥizqiah said, a Mishnah supports Rebbi Bevai, [as we have stated]: “Rebbi Simeon says, what is the difference between <i>sheqalim</i> and purification offerings? It is that <i>sheqalim</i> are a fixed sum but purification offerings have no fixed price<sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 2:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.2.3.1">Mishnah 4</a>.</i>.” Where do we hold? If about one who says, “that I shall bring my <i>sheqel</i> from these,” everybody agrees that the excess is profane. If about one who says, “that I shall bring my purification offering from these,” everybody agrees that the excess is gift<sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote">Including the House of Shammai.</i>. But we must deal with the case of one who says “these <i>sheqalim</i>”, since from the Torah they are a fixed amount the excess is profane, “purification offerings”, since their value is not a fixed amount from the Torah the excess is gift. How does Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">This name is impossible here; one has to read with the Babli sources “R. Simeon”, denying that the argument of R. Ḥizqiah is applicable to the reasoning of the House of Shammai. The reading of the text in <i>Nazir</i>, “R. Yose” also is possible; in that case he states that the argument of R. Simeon applies only if the stated intent is to collect monies for the Temple tax, not if the declaration is made on monies already available. In the latter case, R. Simeon may agree that the excess is earmarked for the Temple gift account.</i> treat this? He explains it, if he collects small change following the House of Hillel. But did we not state<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 2:4:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.2.4.1">Mishnah 5</a>.</i>, “the excess of <i>sheqalim</i> is profane”? He explains it, if he collects small change following the House of Hillel. But did we not state, “the excess of the tenth of an <i>ephah</i>” [is profane]<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote">Addition of the corrector. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 2:4:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.2.4.1">Mishnah 5</a> clearly states that excess monies collected for a flour offering of a tenth of an <i>ephah</i>, probably not the daily offering of the rich High Priest (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 6:12-16" href="/Leviticus.6.12-16"><i>Lev.</i> 6:12–16</a>) but the purification offering of the very poor (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 5:11-13" href="/Leviticus.5.11-13"><i>Lev.</i> 5:11–13</a>), are dedicated for the gift account. The entire sentence is missing in B. In <b>ג</b> the reading is “the excess of a tenth of an <i>ephah</i> are <i>sheqalim</i>”. This is acceptable; the excess of coins collected for a <i>sanctum</i> may be used for another sacred purpose. While the sanctity of <i>sheqalim</i> is less than that of a flour offering, the switch will be permitted to the poor following the House of Hillel.</i>? Still he explains it if he collects small change following the House of Hillel.
If somebody put aside his <i>sheqel</i> in the belief that he owed it and it turned out that he did not owe, it was not dedicated<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">The entire argument follows the House of Hillel who in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Nazir 5:1:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Nazir.5.1.1">Mishnah <i>Nazir</i>5:1</a> stated that dedication in error is void, against the opinion of the House of Shammai.</i>. If he put aside two in the belief that he owed twice and it turned out that he owed only once, how do you treat the second? As one who believed that he owed it and it turned out that he did not owe, or as one who said “these”<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote">Following those who hold that dedicating “these coins” is a full dedication even if the value exceeds that of a <i>sheqel</i>.</i>?
“When Israel returned from the Babylonian exile they gave as Temple tax <i>darics</i>,” denars<sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Aurei</i>, Roman gold <i>denarii</i>. The numismatic evidence shows that the <i>Dareikos</i> was worth about twice the <i>aureus</i>.</i>, “they continued to give <i>sela`im</i>,” as their meaning<sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">The Accadic <i>sila</i> used in both Talmudim to designate the Roman tetradrachma.</i>, “they continued to give minted coins,” half tetradrachmas, they wanted to give denars,” quarters<sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote">With J. Levy reading as Latin <i>quarta</i>.</i>, but these were not accepted by the following: <i>and we accepted for us as commandment to give a sheqel three times</i><sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 10:33" href="/Nehemiah.10.33"><i>Neh</i>. 10:33</a>, following the changed wording in B which is understood also in S. The usual translation is “a third of a <i>sheqel.</i>” The verse declares the collection of <i>sheqalim</i> a post-exilic institution. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bava Batra 9a" href="/Bava_Batra.9a">Babli <i>Bava batra</i>9a</a>.</i> <i>in the year for the service in our God’s House</i>. Rebbi Ḥilkiah in the name of Rebbi Aḥa: From here that a person has to give his <i>sheqel</i> three times a year; &lt;from here that a person is responsible for the alienation of his <i>sheqel</i> three times a year;&gt;<sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote">Added from the other two sources. The omission in the text probably is a scribal error.</i> from here that one does not importune people more than three times a year. Rebbi Abbin said, from here the three <i>se`ah</i>, from here the three boxes, from here the three collection times<sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 2:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.2.3.1">Mishnah 3:1–2</a>: Money was disbursed from the <i>sheqalim</i>3 times a year; each disbursement yielded three boxes of <i>sheqalim, three se`ah each.</i></i>.
It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 30:13" href="/Exodus.30.13"><i>Ex.</i> 30:13</a>, reading הַפְּקוּדִים “the census” as Mishnaic Hebrew הַפִּקּוּדִים “the Commandments”.</i>: <i>This they shall give, everybody who violated the Commandments</i>. Rebbi Jehudah and Rebbi Neḥemiah. One said, because they sinned<sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote">Making the Golden Calf after 12 noon, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Shabbat 89a" href="/Shabbat.89a">Babli <i>Šabbat</i>89a</a>, summarized by <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 32:1" href="/Exodus.32.1">Rashi, <i>Ex.</i> 32:1</a>.</i> in the middle of the day they shall give half a <i>sheqel</i>; but the other said, because they sinned in the sixth hour they shall give half a <i>sheqel</i>; which is worth six grams<sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote">An Aramaic plural of Greek γράμμα, τό, “gram, scruple (as weight)”. One scruple is two <i>oboloi</i>, a third of a denar, approximately 1.2 metric grams, used here as name of a silver coin.</i>. Rebbi Joshua the son of Rebbi Neḥemiah in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan ben Zakkai: Because they transgressed the Ten Commandments, each of them shall give ten <i>gerah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 30:13" href="/Exodus.30.13"><i>Ex.</i> 30:13</a>, reading הַפְּקוּדִים “the census” as Mishnaic Hebrew הַפִּקּוּדִים “the Commandments”.</i>. Rebbi Berekhiah, Rebbi Levi in the name of Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish: Because they sold Rachel’s firstborn for twenty pieces of silver; each of them shall redeem his firstborn with twenty pieces of silver<sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 3:47" href="/Numbers.3.47"><i>Num</i>. 3:47</a>. The firstborn is redeemed by 5 <i>sheqalim</i>. Since it is held that the <i>sheqel</i> in the Torah is equal to a Roman tetradrachma, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 1:3:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.1.3.4"><i>Qiddušin</i>1:3 Note 339</a>, 5 <i>sheqalim</i> are 20 <i>denarii</i>. The generic expression “pieces of silver” is taken to mean the most common silver coin, the denar.<br>The homily is mentioned as introduction to the following one.</i>. Rebbi Phineas in the name of Rebbi Levi: Because they sold Rachel’s firstborn for twenty pieces of silver and each of them received a minted coin<sup class="footnote-marker">60,</sup><i class="footnote">In this context meaning the silver didrachma.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">Since Joseph was sold by 10 of his brothers. The formulation of the homily shows that in later Amoraic times the word <i>sheqel</i> had lost its meaning denoting either a standard weight or a standard coin but became the label of a religious obligation.</i>, each of them shall give a minted coin as his <i>sheqel</i>.

Halakhah 4

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The excess of <i>sheqalim</i> is profane<sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 2:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.2.3.1">Mishnah 3</a>.</i>. The excess of a tenth of an ephah<sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote">Either the daily offering of the High Priest, which is the only obligatory offering by a single person which is neither a purification nor a reparation offering, or the purification offering of the very poor, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 5:11" href="/Leviticus.5.11"><i>Lev.</i> 5:11</a>.</i>, the excess of nests<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote">Couples of pigeons or turtle doves, needed to permit the person access to <i>sancta</i>.</i> of male sufferers from gonorrhea<sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 15:14" href="/Leviticus.15.14"><i>Lev.</i> 15:14</a>.</i>, the nests of female sufferers from flux<sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 15:29" href="/Leviticus.15.29"><i>Lev.</i> 15:29</a>.</i>, the nests of women after childbirth<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 12:8" href="/Leviticus.12.8"><i>Lev.</i> 12:8</a>.</i>, or purification offerings, or reparation offerings, their excesses are gift<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning the coins given as <i>sheqel</i>.</i>. This is the principle: of anything brought for a sin or as reparation the excess is gift.<br>The excess<sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote">In all these cases the money was saved for the purpose of a certain type of sacrifice. If not all the money was actually used, the excess may be used later for the same purpose. It cannot return to profane status since “a promise to Heaven is like delivery to an individual”.</i> of elevation sacrifices is for elevation sacrifices, the excess of flour offerings is for flour offerings, the excess of well-being sacrifices is for well-being sacrifices, the excess of <i>Pesaḥ</i> is for well-being sacrifices. The excess of <i>nezirim</i> is for <i>nezirim</i>, the excess of a <i>nazir</i><sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote">If money was collected in order to help any <i>nazir</i> who might apply for a subsidy for the cost of his sacrifices, the money remain in its status even if not used in the time frame originally envisaged. But if money either was set aside by a <i>nazir</i> himself or it was given to him personally for his sacrifices and not completely used, the excess goes to the Temple’s gift account.</i> is for gift.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “The excess of <i>sheqalim</i> is profane,” etc. Rebbi Yasa<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">While all sources have “R. Yose”, the reading must be R. Yasa, a Babylonian early enough to have visited Samuel’s academy. The name is spelled correctly at the end of the Halakhah.</i> said, when I still was there, I heard the voice of Rav Jehudah asking Samuel, if somebody had set his <i>sheqel</i> apart and died? He told him, they shall fall to gift<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote">Since the monies were set aside for the <i>sheqel</i> and “a promise to Heaven is like delivery to an individual” (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 1:6:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.1.6.1">Mishnah <i>Qiddušin</i>1:6</a>), they are Temple property. Since they are not <i>sheqalim</i> they must be given to the Temple account into which all Temple monies not otherwise specified are collected.</i>. The excess of his tenth of an <i>ephah</i>, Rebbi Joḥanan said, one shall bring them to the Dead Sea<sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote">If this refers to the daily offering of the High priest and the High priest had died, then the monies cannot be used in the Temple since possibly they were not dedicated; they cannot be used as profane since possibly they were dedicated. They have to be destroyed.</i>. Rebbi Eleazar said, it shall fall to gift. The Mishnah disagrees with Rebbi Joḥanan<sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">The reading of B is “disagrees with both of them”.</i>: “The excess of <i>sheqalim</i> is profane The excess of a tenth of an <i>ephah</i>, the excess of nests of male sufferers from gonorrhea, the nests of female sufferers from flux, the nests of women after childbirth, or purification offerings, or reparation offerings, the excesses are gift.”. What does Rebbi Joḥanan do with this? He explains it as excess from the tenth of an <i>ephah</i> of the purification offering of any one in Israel<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote">This seems to be required by the wording of the Mishnah, which decrees that the excess of monies for the tenth of an <i>ephah</i> is Temple property but allows only excess of purification or reparation sacrifices to be so taken. The High Priest’s flour offering is neither of these; therefore the Mishnah cannot include it.<br>The reading of B implies that R. Eleazar identifies that tenth of an <i>ephah</i> as the High Priest’s offering.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">This and the next paragraph also appear in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 5:2:10-11" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.5.2.10-11"><i>Pesaḥim</i>5:1, Notes 80–97</a>, where also the readings of B are noted (ג is unreadable or lacunary for the present paragraph.) Only the most necessary notes are given here, the remainder should be consulted there.</i> Rebbi Joḥanan said, about this Abba bar Abba enlightened me, for they are saying, from where that <i>Pesaḥ</i> is changed into the denomination of well-being sacrifices? The verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 3:6" href="/Leviticus.3.6"><i>Lev.</i> 3:6</a>.</i>, <i>and if his sacrifice be from small cattle as meal well-being offering</i>; anything from small cattle comes as well-being offering. They objected, is there not an elevation offering from small cattle? Anything which only comes from small cattle; this eliminates the elevation offering which even may come from large cattle. They objected, is there not reparation offering? Rebbi Abun bar Cahana said, “<i>from small cattle</i>”. this eliminates the reparation offering, which only comes from rams. Everywhere you are saying that מִן (is to include) [is to exclude], but here you are saying that (מִן is to exclude) [is to include]<sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote">The text is difficult since it is standard rabbinic interpretation to consider prefix <i>mem</i> or מִן as privative, excluding certain categories (cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shabbat 7:1:11" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shabbat.7.1.11"><i>Šabbat</i>7 Note 26</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shevuot 1:2:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shevuot.1.2.4"><i>Ševuot</i>1:2 Note 75</a>, <i>Bava Meṣia`</i>4:8 Note 122, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Nazir 5:2:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Nazir.5.2.3"><i>Nazir</i>5:4 Note 105</a>). Also in the next sentence, R. Mana gives the interpretation that here מִן is privative. On the other hand, the testimony of the scribe’s two texts, the Genizah fragment available for <i>Pesaḥim</i>, and the Munich ms. of <i>Šeqalim</i> do not permit emendation. It seems that here “every where” is derogatory, meaning Babylonian. The sequence of arguments leads to a contradiction. Abba bar Abba treats מִן as inclusive, R. Abun bar Cahana as exclusive. R. Mana explains that מִן always is partitive; automatic switch to well-being offerings is possible only for sacrifices that totally correspond to the declaration צאן, i. e., both sheep and goats, male and female.</i>. Rebbi Mana said, (it excludes it,) [here also מִן is to exclude: It excludes in that it may not be brought two years old; it excludes that it cannot be brought female; and for a reparation offering also it excludes]<sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from B.</i> since it only comes from rams. They objected, is there not written,<sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 1:10" href="/Leviticus.1.10"><i>Lev.</i> 1:10</a>.</i> <i>and if his sacrifice be from small cattle, from sheep or goats, as elevation offering</i>; then excess <i>Pesaḥ</i> should become elevation offering? Rebbi Abun said, one changes something to be eaten into something to be eaten, but one does not change something to be eaten into something not to be eaten. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, one changes simple <i>sancta</i> into simple <i>sancta</i>, but one does not change simple <i>sancta</i> into most holy sacrifices. Rebbi Joḥanan said, about what Rebbi Ḥanina enlightened, that they are saying, <i>Pesaḥ</i> is changed into a well-being offering only if he slaughtered it for the purpose of well-being offering; but I am saying, even for the purpose of an elevation offering. Rebbi Illa said, the reason of Rebbi Joḥanan: <i>And if his sacrifice be from small cattle as meal well-being offering</i><sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 3:6" href="/Leviticus.3.6"><i>Lev.</i> 3:6</a>.</i>; anything to be consumed as <i>sanctum</i> is a well-being offering. Does it change with respect to disqualifying thoughts<sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote">If the animal dedicated as <i>Pesaḥ</i> is used against the rules for something other than a well-being offering, do the rules of the other kind apply or is it disqualified and no rules of intent apply?</i>? How is this? If he slaughtered it for the purpose of an elevation offering in order to pour its blood the next day. In any case, it is disqualified. If you are saying that it changes with respect to disqualifying thoughts, it is <i>piggul</i><sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote">If the animal still is a sacrifice, now under the rules of elevation sacrifices, the intention to perform any required action out of its prescribed time-frame is <i>piggul</i>, a deadly sin causing extirpation.</i>. If you are saying that it does not change with respect to disqualifying thoughts, it is disqualified<sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">If the animal is disqualified and not under the rule of any kind of sacrifice, the illegitimate intent is inconsequential.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote">In all these cases the money was saved for the purpose of a certain type of sacrifice. If not all the money was actually used, the excess may be used later for the same purpose. It cannot return to profane status since “a promise to Heaven is like delivery to an individual”.</i> For its purpose and not for its purpose on the other days of the year? Rebbi Abun bar Ḥiyya in the name of Samuel bar Abba: Since it is left without a name it is as if from the start he slaughtered for its purpose and not for its purpose in silence and is qualified. They said to him. if it is so, even if he slaughtered for its purpose to pour the blood not for its purpose it should be treated as if from the start he slaughtered for its purpose and not for its purpose in silence and be qualified. Rebbi Abba Mari said, who says that in silence it is qualified? Or may we say, in silence it is disqualified?
<sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote">This text also is in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Nazir 4:4:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Nazir.4.4.1"><i>Nazir</i>4:4 (Notes 61–72</a>, <b>נ</b>) which probably was the source. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Nazir 4:4:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Nazir.4.4.1">Mishnah <i>Nazir</i>4:4</a> deals with the case of a married woman who made a vow of <i>nazir</i> and started putting aside money for her required sacrifices when her husband dissolved her vow. Then she no longer is <i>nezirah</i> and therefore cannot bring the sacrifices, but the monies remain dedicated. The Mishnah states: “If she had money not designated, it should be given to the gift account. If the monies were designated, the value of the purification offering shall be thrown into the Dead Sea; one may not use it but there can be no <i>me`ilah</i>. For the value of the elevation offering, they shall bring an elevation offering; it is subject to the law of <i>me`ilah</i>. For the value of the well-being offering, they shall bring a well-being offering, to be eaten on one day; it does not need bread.” Money not designated is money for which it never was decided for which kind of sacrifice it should be used.</i> Rav Ḥisda said, only if his purification offering was presented last. But if his well-being offering was presented last, what is left over is for a well-being offering<sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote">If monies were collected to help indigent <i>nezirim</i> with the expenses of their sacrifices but not all was used, the remainder has to be kept in trust to be used in the future for the same purpose. But if a person dedicated his own money for his sacrifices and had money left over, if the last sacrifice bought was of the most holy kind, the leftover money is of the same kind and has to go to the account for elevation offerings. But if the leftovers are of a well-being sacrifice, a “simple <i>sanctum</i>” which may be consumed by lay people, the monies have to be used for a simple <i>sanctum</i>.</i>. Rebbi Ze`ira said, even if his well-being offering was presented last, it is a general rule for a <i>nazir</i> that his leftover be for the gift account<sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Me`ilah</i>3:2, overriding the general rule of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 2:4:5-5:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.2.4.5-5.1">Mishnah 2:6</a>. In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Nazir 25a" href="/Nazir.25a">Babli, <i>Nazir</i>25a</a>, the statement is attributed to R. Joḥanan.</i>. A <i>baraita</i> supports one and a <i>baraita</i> supports the other. A <i>baraita</i> supports Rebbi Ze`ira: “The following are not designated monies: any which contain money for purification offerings should be left to die. Even if he designated money for purification offerings that should be left to die, it remains not designated<sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Me`ilah</i>3:2, overriding the general rule of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 2:4:5-5:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.2.4.5-5.1">Mishnah 2:6</a>. In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Nazir 25a" href="/Nazir.25a">Babli, <i>Nazir</i>25a</a>, the statement is attributed to R. Joḥanan.</i>.” A <i>baraita</i> supports Rav Ḥisda: “This is for my purification offering and the rest for my <i>nezirut</i>. Then he died. One commits larceny with all of them but not with part of them.” It does not say, when he died it should be given to the gift account100.
Rav Ḥisda said, a <i>nazir</i>’s leftover bread shall be left to decay. Rebbi Yose said, that is correct. You cannot sacrifice it by itself since bread cannot be brought alone. You cannot sacrifice it together with another <i>nazir</i>’s since no <i>nazir</i> sacrifices without bread<sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote">While several flour offerings are described in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 2" href="/Leviticus.2"><i>Lev.</i> 2</a>, none is authorized for bread alone. Nowhere do we find a procedure to redeem sacrificial bread.</i>. Therefore, it was necessary to say that a <i>nazir</i>’s leftover bread shall be left to decay. They wanted to say, the same rule applies to his leftover bread as to his leftover wine offering. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, his leftover wine offering is most holy<sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 5:3:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.5.3.2">Halakhah 5, Note 81</a>.</i>; it should be given to the gift account. In the opinion of Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun, Samuel, Rav Ḥisda, and Rebbi Eleazar, all three said the same. Rav Ḥisda, as quoted here. Samuel, as Rebbi Yasa said,<sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 5:3:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.5.3.2">Halakhah 5, Note 81</a>.</i> when I still was there, I heard the voice of Rav Jehudah asking Samuel: If he designated his <i>sheqel</i> and died? He said, it should be given as gift. Rebbi Eleazar: <sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.5">Halakhah 5, Note 83</a>.</i> the leftover of his tenth of an <i>ephah</i>: Rebbi Joḥanan said, one should bring it to the Dead Sea; Rebbi Eleazar said, it should be given to the gift account..

Halakhah 5

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The excess of monies collected for kidnap victims is for kidnap victims; the excess of monies collected for a particular kidnap victim is for this kidnap victim. The excess of monies collected for the poor is for the poor; the excess of monies collected for a particular poor person is for this poor person. The excess of monies collected for the dead<sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup><i class="footnote">For funeral expenses.</i> is for the dead; the excess of monies collected for a particular dead is for his heirs; Rebbi Meïr says, the excess of monies collected for a particular dead shall be left until Elijah comes<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote">Since one does not know what to do with this money, it cannot be touched until Elijah, a member of the Heavenly Court who knows what the rules really should be, comes to announce the Messiah.</i>; Rebbi Nathan says, from the excess of monies collected for a particular dead one builds a memorial on his grave.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> If they collected for him presuming that he had nothing and it turned out that he had some<sup class="footnote-marker">106</sup><i class="footnote">The reading of ג: ”had nothing”, has to be rejected as scribal error.</i>. Rebbi Jeremiah wanted to say, the excess of monies collected for a particular dead is for his heirs. Rebbi Idi from Ḥutra said to him, think of it, did they intend only for [him<sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote">Since the intent was to bury a destitute person, should the money not be given to the administrators of welfare for the benefit of future needs?</i>? He said to him], I did [not] say this; what is your source<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote">R. Jeremiah realizes that it is a good question but he quoted a Mishnah; R. Idi has no tannaitic source to support him.</i>?
<sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Shekalim (Lieberman) 1:12" href="/Tosefta_Shekalim_(Lieberman).1.12">Tosephta 1:12</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sanhedrin 48a" href="/Sanhedrin.48a">Babli <i>Sanhedrin</i>48a</a>.</i>“It was stated in the name of Rebbi Nathan: From the excess of monies collected for a particular dead he builds a memorial on his grave or perfume<sup class="footnote-marker">109a</sup><i class="footnote">This is the corrector’s text, following B. The scibe wrote זלח, a root not otherwise recorded in rabbinic Hebrew or Aramaic.</i> his bier. It was stated, one does not redeem a kidnap victim for another kidnap victim<sup class="footnote-marker">110</sup><i class="footnote">Monies collected for a particular prisoner should not be used to redeem another, but in cases of urgent need the hands of the administrators are not tied by this rule.</i> and one does not collect a stole for a stole<sup class="footnote-marker">111</sup><i class="footnote">If clothing is collected for a particular person, he should be given exactly what was collected for him.</i>, but one does not restrict the power of the administrators of charity in this.” It was stated, Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel says, one does not build mausoleums for the just; their words are their remembrance<sup class="footnote-marker">112</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Bereishit Rabbah 82:11" href="/Bereishit_Rabbah.82.11"><i>Gen</i>. <i>rabba</i>82(11</a>).</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">113</sup><i class="footnote">As the concurrent testimony of <b>ג</b> and the scribe’s text show, the following text is not part of the original Halakhah. It was added by the corrector from B; both its Aramaic and the names appearing are Babylonian. A somewhat different Yerushalmi text is in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Berakhot 2:1:16-18" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Berakhot.2.1.16-18"><i>Berakhot</i>2:1 (Notes 53–67</a>) and <i>Mo`ed Qaṭan</i>3:7 (83c l. 40–83d l. 8).</i> Rebbi Joḥanan was leaning on Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba when Rebbi Eliezer<sup class="footnote-marker">114</sup><i class="footnote">This should read: Eleazar.</i> saw him and hid himself before him. He said, these two things the Babylonian does to me: First, that he does not greet me, and second, that he hides himself. Rebbi Jacob bar Idi said to him, thus they behave among themselves; Rebbi Ze`ira did not greet Rabba since they observe<sup class="footnote-marker">115</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Job 29:8" href="/Job.29.8"><i>Job</i>29:8</a>.</i> <i>Boys see me and hide themselves; elders rise and stand</i>. He asked him, may one pass by a cursed statue? He said to him, do you want to honor it? Pass it by and blind its eyes! He said to him, Rebbi Eliezer<sup class="footnote-marker">114</sup><i class="footnote">This should read: Eleazar.</i> did well that he did not pass before you. The other thing the Babylonian does, that he does not mention my tradition in my name. Rebbi Immi and Rebbi Assi<sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote">He is R. Yasa in Yerushalmi texts.</i> came to him. They said to him, Rabbi, so it happened that it was a synagogue of weavers, about a bolt topped by a lock<sup class="footnote-marker">117</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 10:10:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.10.10.1">Mishnah <i>Eruvin</i>10:9</a>.</i> about which Rebbi Eleazar and Rebbi Yose disagreed until they tore a Torah scroll in their rage. Would you think that they tore a Torah scroll? But that a Torah scroll was torn. There was an old man there, Rebbi Yose ben Qisma, who said, I wonder whether this synagogue will not be a place of foreign worship. He came back and asked, where is the colleague? Rebbi Jacob bar Idi came and said to him, it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">118</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 11:15" href="/Joshua.11.15"><i>Jos</i>. 11:15</a>.</i>, <i>all that the Eternal commanded to His servant Moses so Joshua commanded</i>. When Joshua explained, did he mention every time “so said Moses”? No, he explained and they knew that it was Moses’s teaching. So also Eleazar sits and explains and everybody knows that it is your teaching. He said to them<sup class="footnote-marker">119</sup><i class="footnote">R. Immi (Ammi) and R. Assi (Yasa).</i>, why do you not know to pacify like our colleague Ben Idi?
Why did Rebbi Joḥanan insist to require that traditions should be reported in his name? For also David begged for divine mercy in this respect, as it says, <i>may I dwell in Your tent forever, I shall seek shelter under the cover of Your wings, Selah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">120</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 61:5" href="/Psalms.61.5"><i>Ps.</i> 61:5</a>.</i>. Could David think of living forever? Rather, David said before the Holy One, praise to Him: Master of the World, may I have the merit that my words will be mentioned in synagogues and houses of study. What good does that do to him? Simeon, the son of the <i>Nazir</i> said in the name of Rebbi Isaac If a Sage’s pronouncement in matters of practice is mentioned in this world, the latter’s lips whisper with him in the grave for it is said<sup class="footnote-marker">121</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Song of Songs 7:10" href="/Song_of_Songs.7.10">Cant. 7:10</a>. Note that in Accadic the root <i>dbb</i> means “to speak”.</i>, <i>dripping from the lips of the sleeping ones</i>. Like that softened bunch of grapes, if a person puts his finger on it immediately it drips, so also the lips of the just drip, for if one mentions their pronouncements in matters of practice the latter’s lips whisper in the grave. What good does that do to them? The son of the <i>Nazir</i> says, like one who drinks spiced wine; Rebbi Isaac said, like one who drinks old wine, even though he cannot taste it.
<sup class="footnote-marker">122</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shabbat 1:2:5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shabbat.1.2.5"><i>Šabbat</i>1, Notes 188–191</a>.</i> Giddul said, anybody who quotes somebody should consider it as if the author of the quote stood before him, for it is said<sup class="footnote-marker">123</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 39:7" href="/Psalms.39.7"><i>Ps.</i> 39:7</a>.</i>, <i>only in image a man wanders.</i> It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">124</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 20:6" href="/Proverbs.20.6"><i>Prov</i>. 20:6</a>.</i> <i>many a man professes good will,</i> this is the rest of mankind; <i>but where will you find one you can trust</i>, that is Rebbi Ze`ira. As Rebbi Ze`ira said, should we take the traditions of Rav Sheshet into account since he is blind? Rebbi Ze`ira said to Rebbi Assi, does the Rabbi know Bar Petaiah that you quote traditions in his name? He said to him, Rebbi Joḥanan quoted them in his name. Rebbi Ze`ira said to Rebbi Assi<sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote">He is R. Yasa in Yerushalmi texts.</i>, does the Rabbi know Rav that you quote traditions in his name? He said to him, Rebbi<sup class="footnote-marker">125</sup><i class="footnote">Read: Rav.</i> Ada bar Ahavah quoted them in his name.
<sup class="footnote-marker">126</sup><i class="footnote">This again is the Babylonian version of the text in <i>Berakhot</i> and <i>Mo`ed Qaṭan</i>.</i> There is no generation without scoffers. What did the hooligans of David’s generation do? They went to David’s windows and said to him: David, when will the Temple be built, when will we go to the Eternal’s house? David said, even though they intend to enrage me, something should come over me were I not happy, <i>I enjoy it when they say to me: let us go to the Lord’s house</i><sup class="footnote-marker">127</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 122:1" href="/Psalms.122.1"><i>Ps.</i> 122:1</a>.</i>. <i>When your days will be complete and you will lie with your forefathers</i><sup class="footnote-marker">128</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 7:12" href="/II_Samuel.7.12"><i>2Sam.</i> 7:12</a>.</i>. The Holy One, praise to Him, said to David:, I am counting full days for you, I am not counting missing days for you. Will not your son Solomon build the Temple for public sacrifice? Law and justice that you are upholding is more to my liking than sacrifices, as it is said<sup class="footnote-marker">129</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 21:3" href="/Proverbs.21.3"><i>Prov</i>. 21:3</a>.</i>, <i>upholding justice and law is preferred by the Eternal to sacrifice</i>.]

Chapter 3



Halakhah 1

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Three times a year one disburses from the lodge<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">The room where the <i>sheqalim</i> were stored, to be disbursed as will be described in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 3:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.3.2.1">Mishnah 2</a>.</i>; half a month before Passover, half a month before Pentecost, and half a month before Tabernacles, and these are threshing floors<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Tithe from grain is due once the grain has been threshed and the grain kernels collected to form an orderly heap. Therefore “threshing floor” is the technical term for the term when tithe becomes due by biblical standards. All lambs and calves born after one of these terms and before the next become forbidden as food on the next term until they are counted and tithe was given.</i> for animal tithe, the words of Rebbi Aqiba. Ben Azzai says, on the 29<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Adar<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">15 days before <i>Pesaḥ</i>, the festive Passover Eve.</i>, the first of Sivan4, and the 29<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Av<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">35 days before Tabernacles.</i>. Rebbi Eleazar and Rebbi Simon say, on the first of Nisan, the first of Sivan, and the 29<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Elul<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">The last day of the year counting from the first of Tishre.</i>. Why did they say on the 29th of Elul and did not say on the first of Tishre? Because that is a holiday and it is impossible to tithe on a holiday; therefore they advanced it to the 29<sup>th</sup> of Elul.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “Three times a year,” etc. Rebbi Abbahu said, everywhere we have stated <i>pars</i>, it is one half<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">If no numbers are given, the Latin <i>pars</i>“a part” means one part of two; in this case of the month preceding the holiday.</i>. [Half of the thirty days before a holiday when one explains its rules.<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from B. Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 6b" href="/Pesachim.6b">Babli <i>Pesaḥim</i>6b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Megillah 4a" href="/Megillah.4a"><i>Megillah</i>4a</a>; <i>Sifry Num</i>. 66.</i>]
Rebbi Joḥanan said, because they are the periods of birth<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">Different kinds of livestock produce their young at different times.</i>. Rebbi Aḥa, Rebbi Tanḥum bar Ḥiyya in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: That animals be available for the pilgrims on the holidays<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Bekhorot 57b-58a" href="/Bekhorot.57b-58a">Babli <i>Bekhorot</i>57b/58a</a>. It is explained later that the main time for animal tithe is early fall. The other two times are introduced for the convenience of the farmer that he may take his tithe animal to the Temple when he makes his pilgrimage anyhow.</i>. Rebbi Yudan said, that he should not come to <i>do not tarry</i><sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">It is sinful to give tithes too late (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 22:28" href="/Exodus.22.28"><i>Ex.</i> 22:28</a>). This is interpreted to mean that one disregards a positive commandment if one does not hand over (for produce) or sacrifices (for animals) his tithes on or before the next holiday, and one transgresses the prohibition on the third holiday after the start of the obligation.</i>. Rebbi Yose said, anybody who is late with his <i>ṭevel</i> transgresses<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ṭevel</i> is untithed produce for which heave and tithes are due.</i>. There,<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Bekhorot 8:5" href="/Mishnah_Bekhorot.8.5">Mishnah <i>Bekhorot</i>8:5</a>. The text quoted here is the Mishnah text; nevertheless it seems that the statement from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Rosh Hashanah 1:1:1-16" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Rosh_Hashanah.1.1.1-16">Mishnah <i>Roš Haššanah</i>1:1</a>, quoted in B, that R. Eleazar (ben Shamua) and R. Simeon fix the date at the first of Tishre, has to be included here. From here on the text is copied in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Rosh Hashanah 1:1:15" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Rosh_Hashanah.1.1.15"><i>Roš Haššanah</i>1:1 (Note 148</a>).</i> we have stated: “Rebbi Meïr says, on the first of Elul is the New Year for animal tithes. Ben Azzai says, those born in Elul are to be tithed separately.” Rebbi Ḥuna said, The reason of Rebbi Meïr: Up to that point they finish to give birth from the old ones; after that they start to give birth from the new ones<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">Since the gestation period for sheep is 5 months, those born in Av were conceived before the start of Nisan, those in Elul after the first of Nisan. If the start of the year is fixed in spring, the natural date for a new year of animal tithes is the start of Elul.</i>. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun in the name of Rav Huna: The reason of Rebbi Eleazar and Rebbi Simeon, <i>the rams are mounting the ewes</i>, these are the early ones, <i>and the valleys are clothed in grain</i>, these are the late ones, <i>they are friends and also are tithed</i><sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 65:14" href="/Psalms.65.14"><i>Ps.</i>65:14</a>. The last word is read as if it were יְעַשְׂרוּ. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Rosh Hashanah 8a" href="/Rosh_Hashanah.8a">Babli <i>Roš Haššanah</i>8a</a>.</i>, both enter the corral to be tithed. Ben Azzai said, since these are saying this and those are saying that, those born in Elul should be tithed by themselves. How is this? If there were born in his flock five in Av, five in Elul, and five in Tishre, they do not combine<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">The tenth lamb is animal tithe. If there are 5 in Av and 5 in Elul, they cannot add up to 10 since practice may follow R. Meïr; 5 in Elul and 5 in Tishre cannot combine since practice may follow R. Simeon.</i>. If there were born in his flock five in Av and five in Tishre, they combine<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">This really should be: 5 in Tishre and 5 in the following Av, so they belong to the same fiscal year (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Bekhorot 7:6" href="/Tosefta_Bekhorot.7.6">Tosephta <i>Bekhorot</i>7:9</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bekhorot 58a" href="/Bekhorot.58a">Babli <i>Bekhorot</i>58a</a>.)</i>. Could Ben Azzai decide between his students<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">The reference to Ben Azzai in a dispute between R. Aqiba’s last students is anachronistic; Ben Azzai died young, before these became independent scholars.</i>? Rebbi Jeremiah, Rebbi Miasha in the name of Rebbi Samuel bar Rav Isaac: For so disagreed the fathers of the world. Who are the fathers of the world? Rebbi Jonah stated before Rebbi Jeremiah: Rebbi Ismael and Rebbi Aqiba<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">Ben Azzai considers the points of view of R. Aqiba and R. Ismael as equivalent even though he never was R. Ismael’s student. If he does not follow his teacher, he must be an independent authority.</i>. This implies that Ben Azzai was colleague and student of Rebbi Aqiba. If you are saying that he was his teacher, is there anybody who says to his teacher, “since these are saying this and those are saying that”? Rebbi Abun in the name of Rebbi Samuel bar Rav Isaac understood it from the following<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Bava batra</i>9:14. The testimony of a Mishnah is preferable to that of a <i>baraita</i>.</i>: “Ben Azzai said to him, we are sorry about their disagreement, and you come to find us disagreement where they are concurring.” This implies that Ben Azzai was colleague and student of Rebbi Aqiba. If you are saying that he was his teacher, is there anybody who says to his teacher, “you come to find us disagreement”?
There, we have stated: “Any born from the first of Tishre until the 29<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Elul combine; five before New Year’s day and five after New Year’s day do not combine. Five before the threshing floor and five after the threshing floor do combine<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Bekhorot 9:5" href="/Mishnah_Bekhorot.9.5">Mishnah <i>Bekhorot</i>9:5</a>. A general rule for all tithes is that they have to be given separately for each year. This is inferred from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 14:22" href="/Deuteronomy.14.22"><i>Deut</i>. 14:22</a>, referring to agricultural tithe, which has to be given <i>year by year</i>. The tax year for animal tithe is defined as from Tishre 1 to Elul 29.</i>.” Rebbi Yose said, this implies that the rules of animal tither are neither like those of germinating<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">The tax year for tithe from the yield of trees (rabbinic except for olive oil) is defined as from Shevat 15 to Shevat 14; for these purposes a fruit is defined as in existence if it started growing after the flower lost its leaves. The equivalent for animals would be a visible pregnancy.</i> nor like those of a third<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">Agricultural produce (Biblically, grain) has to be given if it is harvested when barely edible, one-third ripe. Its year is from Tishre 1 to Elul 29.</i>. If you would say like germinating, it should state, all whose pregnancy starts from the 29<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Elul. If you would say like a third, it should state, up to the 22<sup class="footnote-marker">nd24</sup>. Rebbi Shammai in the name of Rebbi Abun bar Ḥiyya: Like the third, they made it following Rebbi Simeon, since Rebbi Simeon said, {an animal} before its time enters the corral to be tithed<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">He holds that the tithe is not slaughtered at the moment it is selected; at all times it is a prospective sacrifice. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bekhorot 21b" href="/Bekhorot.21b">Babli <i>Bekhorot</i>21b</a>.</i>. Rebbi Mana met Rebbi Shammai; he asked him, did you say that? He told him, yes. He answered, but did we not state, “Ben Azzai says, those born in Elul are to be tithed separately.<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Bekhorot 8:5" href="/Mishnah_Bekhorot.8.5">Mishnah <i>Bekhorot</i>8:5</a>. The text quoted here is the Mishnah text; nevertheless it seems that the statement from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Rosh Hashanah 1:1:1-16" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Rosh_Hashanah.1.1.1-16">Mishnah <i>Roš Haššanah</i>1:1</a>, quoted in B, that R. Eleazar (ben Shamua) and R. Simeon fix the date at the first of Tishre, has to be included here. From here on the text is copied in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Rosh Hashanah 1:1:15" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Rosh_Hashanah.1.1.15"><i>Roš Haššanah</i>1:1 (Note 148</a>).</i>” Not even if it was born up to the 29<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Elul? Could you say that Ben Azzai follows Rebbi Simeon<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">Since it was explained in the preceding paragraph that Ben Azzai follows neither R. Simeon nor his opponents; his statement has to be acceptable to both parties.</i>? You have to say, he follows the rabbis. Just as you say following the rabbis, he leaves them for the next year and they will be tithed with the others of their year<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">An animal born between 23rd and 29th of Elul for Ben Azzai according to the rabbis has to be tithed the following year with the animals born the next year during Elul 1–22.</i>, so you have to say following ben Azzai, he leaves them for the next threshing floor<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">Which is a preferred but not obligatory date for tithing.</i> and they will be tithed with those from Elul. Rebbi Huna said, this implies that the days of a firstling while he still is before its time<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">The first 7 days of its life. The firstling has to be delivered to a Cohen during its first year.</i> are counted for its year. Rebbi Mana said, my father Rebbi Jonah understood this from the following<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 15:19" href="/Deuteronomy.15.19"><i>Deut</i>. 15:19</a>. Since only its date of birth is mentioned. The firstling automatically is a dedicated sacrifice, and neither may nor can be selected.</i>: <i>Any male firstling which is born to your cattle and small cattle</i>, etc. How is this? You count its year from the moment it is born.

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> One disburses from the lodge<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">The room where the <i>sheqalim</i> were stored, to be disbursed as will be described in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 3:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.3.2.1">Mishnah 2</a>.</i> into three boxes of three <i>seah</i> each, on which is written ג ,ב ,א<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">The money to be spent in the inverse order of the boxes; then it always is clear how much money is left.</i>. Rebbi Ismael says, it was written in Greek, A, B, Γ. The disburser enters neither in trousers<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">Rashi’s interpretation, Latin <i>paragauda</i>. Another interpretation: a long robe with wide cuffs (sources giben in Levy’s Dictionaty, vol. 4 col. 98b. Cf Arabic בֻּוגֻז).</i> with pockets, nor with shoes<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">The last two are sewn together; the seam could be opened and coins stuffed in there.</i>, nor with sandals, nor with phylacteries nor with an amulet<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">The last two are sewn together; the seam could be opened and coins stuffed in there.</i>, lest he become poor and people would say, he became poor because he sinned in the lodge, or he became rich and people would say, he enriched himself from the money lifted from the lodge, for a person needs to be clean before people<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">Rabbinic Hebrew distinguishes between בִּרְיָה “creature” and בְּרִיָּה “creation”.</i> as he has to be clean before the Omnipresent, as it is said<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 32:22" href="/Numbers.32.22"><i>Num</i>. 32:22</a>.</i>, <i>you have to be blameless before the Eternal and before Israel</i>, and it says<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 3:4" href="/Proverbs.3.4"><i>Prov</i>. 3:4</a>.</i>, <i>find grace and understanding in the eyes of God and men.</i>
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> [Rebbi Ze`ira asked Rebbi Joshiah, what is the measure of three baskets? He told him, let us infer the hidden from the explicit. It is stated:]<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from B, originally from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shabbat 10:2:3-3:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shabbat.10.2.3-3.2"><i>Šabbat</i>10, Notes 35–37</a>.</i> One distributes from the lodge into three boxes of three <i>seah</i> each, which is nine <i>seah</i>, which is <sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">An animal born between 23rd and 29th of Elul for Ben Azzai according to the rabbis has to be tithed the following year with the animals born the next year during Elul 1–22.</i> <i>seah</i>38; it is written on them ג ,ב ,א. Why is ,ג ב ,א written on them? To say that one does not take from the first before one has taken from the second, and not from the second before one has taken from the third<sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote">The other two sources and the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Shekalim (Lieberman) 2:1" href="/Tosefta_Shekalim_(Lieberman).2.1">Tosephta (2:1</a>) insist that the money was used in ascending order of the boxes/ “Before one has taken” means “before one has finished taking.”</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">The following text is the corrector’s addition from B; it is neither in the scribe’s text nor in <b>ג</b>. The entire Babylonian addition is irrelevant for the subject under discussion; it is a somewhat defective copy of a text in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shabbat 8:1:3-9" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shabbat.8.1.3-9"><i>Šabbat</i>8, Notes 25–51</a>, which should be consulted for the meaning of the text. The Notes here are mostly restricted to remarks about deviations of this copy from the original. An appropriate version is in 8:1.</i>[There, we have stated: “One who brings out wine to mix a cup.” Rebbi Ze`ira asked Rebbi Joshiah, what is the measure of a cup? He told him, let us infer the hidden from the explicit since Rebbi Ḥiyya stated, the Four Cups which they said add up to an Italic <i>quartarius</i> of wine.
A cup mixed by how much? Rebbi Yose bar Bevin said in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan, let us hear from the following: “Water. a gulp; Rebbi Jehudah says, for mixing a cup. Wine. a gulp; Rebbi Jehudah says, for mixing a cup.” This implies mixed as cups are mixed. What is the measure of cups? Rebbi Abun said, τέταρτρον is a quarter.
May one drink them together? Since Rebbi Meïr said,<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ecclesiastes 8:1" href="/Ecclesiastes.8.1"><i>Eccl</i>. 8:1</a>.</i> Rebbi Joḥanan said, if he heard <i>Hallel</i> in the synagogue he has fulfilled his obligation, this implies that if he drank them together he fulfilled his obligation. May one drink them with interruptions? They said that he should drink to feel differently, not that he should get drunk. If he drinks them with interruptions, he will not become drunk. May one fulfill his obligation with Sabbatical wine? Rebbi Hoshaia stated, one may fulfill his obligation with Sabbatical wine. May one fulfill his obligation with spiced wine? Since Bar Qappara stated, spiced wine is like wine, which implies that one may fulfill his obligation with spiced wine. May one fulfill his obligation with mixed wine? Since Rebbi Ḥiyya stated: the Four Cups which they prescribed, one may fulfill his obligation either with unmixed or mixed, on condition that it have the taste and looks of wine. Rebbi Jeremiah said, it is meritorious to fulfill one’s obligation with red wine. What is the reason? <i>Do not see wine when it shows its red color, when put in our cup</i><sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 23:31" href="/Proverbs.23.31"><i>Prov.</i> 23:31</a>. A hilarious misquote of בַּכּוֹס עֵינוֹ as בְּכוֹסֵינוּ, caused by the disappearance of ע as audible sound.</i>. It was stated, cooked for spice. May one fulfill his obligation with cooked wine? Rebbi Jonah said, one may fulfill his obligation with cooked wine. Rebbi Jonah follows his own opinion, since Rebbi Jonah drank his four cups in the Passover night and had a headache until Tabernacles<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">Contamination of the story of R. Jonah, who had a headache until Pentecost, with that of R. Jehudah bar Ilai, the subject of the following paragraph, who had a headache until Tabernacles.</i>.
A lady<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">A post-talmudic diminutive of Latin <i>matrona</i>.</i> saw that his face was shiny. She said to him, old man, old man, one of three things applies to you. Either you are drunk from wine, or you are lending on interest, or you are raising pigs. He answered her, this woman’s spirit shall be blown away, not one of these three things applies to me, but my learning is ever present with me, as it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ecclesiastes 8:1" href="/Ecclesiastes.8.1"><i>Eccl</i>. 8:1</a>.</i>, <i>a man’s wisdom illuminates his face</i>.
Rebbi Abbahu descended to Tiberias. The students of Rebbi Joḥanan saw that his face was shiny. They said before Rebbi Joḥanan, Rebbi Abbahu found a treasure. He came to him. He asked him, what new teaching did you hear? He said, an old Tosephta. He recited about him, <i>a man’s wisdom illuminates his face</i>.
Rebbi Ḥanan said, the <i>log</i> of the Torah is the old Sepphorean eighth of fish sauce. Rebbi Jonah said, I know it. In the House of Shammai<sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote">Anachronistic misreading for “House of R. Yannai.”</i> they were measuring honey with it. It was stated, half of the old Tiberian eighth. Rebbi Joḥanan said, this one we used. Why did he call it the old one? Because it was in his days. Some are saying, it was small, then was enlarged. But some are saying, it was diminished more than before. What is the measure of a cup? Rebbi Yose in the name of Rebbi Yose ben Pazi, Rebbi Yose ben Bevin in the name of Samuel: Two fingers by two fingers high a finger and a half and a third of a finger. The rabbis of Caesarea in the name of Rebbi Yose bar Bevin in the name of Samuel: Rebbi Nathan follows Rebbi Simeon. Just as Rebbi Simeon says, a <i>quartarius</i>, so Rebbi Nathan says, a <i>quartarius</i>, when it jells it will have the volume of an olive.
Rebbi Simon in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: It happened that a mule of Rebbi’s household died and they declared its blood pure regarding the carcass. Rebbi Eleazar asked Rebbi Simon, how much? He did not take notice of him. He asked Rebbi Joshua ben Levi who told him, it is pure up to a <i>quartarius</i>. More than that is impure. Rebbi Eleazar felt badly that Rebbi Simon had not repeated the tradition to him. Rav Beva was sitting stating this occurrence. Rebbi Isaac bar Bisna asked him, is it pure up to a <i>quartarius</i>; more than that impure? He was unfriendly to him. Rebbi Zeriqa asked him, because he asked you, you were unfriendly to him? He answered him, because my mind was not clear, I was unfriendly to him, as Rebbi Ḥanan said, <sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 28:66" href="/Deuteronomy.28.66"><i>Deut</i>. 28:66</a>.</i><i>your life will hang far from you</i>, that is one who buys a year’s supply of wheat, <i>you will be fearful night and day</i>, that is one who buys from the Saracen, <i>and you will not believe in your survival</i>, that is one who buys from the retail store, and I am dependent on retail stores. What about it? “Rebbi Joshua ben Bathyra testified about blood of carcasses that it is pure.” What means pure? It is pure in the flesh<sup class="footnote-marker">47a</sup><i class="footnote">Defective copy from <i>Šabbat</i>: הבשר instead of הֶכְשֵׁר “in that it does not prepare for impurity”.</i>, but for impurity it makes impure. There, we have stated “The blood of a crawling animal is like its flesh, it makes impure but does not prepare. Nothing else is like this,” in the amount needed that its blood makes impure like its flesh. Rav Yose said, two Amoraim disagree, one says impure, and one says pure. He who says “impure” follows Rebbi Jehudah; he of “pure” follows Rebbi Joshua ben Bathyra. Rav Abuha of Iman the sister of<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">Unintelligible misreading of the text in <i>Šabbat.</i></i> Rebbi Jehudah was the instructor of the Patriarch.]
[“Lest he become poor and people would say,” etc.] Rebbi Ismael stated, a curly head should not disburse because of the suspicion<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">That he might hide some coins in his hair.</i>. It was stated, “the treasurers were rubbing with Cilician cloth.” It was stated, “they were talking with him from the time he entered to the time he left.<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Shekalim (Lieberman) 2:2" href="/Tosefta_Shekalim_(Lieberman).2.2">Tosephta 2:2</a>. Cilician cloth was made from goats’ hair. They were checking that he had no coins on his body, and talking with him so that he could not put any coins in his mouth.</i>” Should he not fill his mouth with water? Rebbi Tanḥuma said, because of the benediction<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">If he entered with his mouth full of water and left with his mouth full of water it would be clear that he could not have hidden any coins there.<br>It is absolutely unclear to what R. Tanḥuma refers. While the root תרם means “to lift heave”, and giving heave needs a benediction, the use of the word cannot make disbursing other people’s contributions equal to dedicating from one’s own property; the obligation of dedicating heave with a benediction cannot reasonably be extended to the act of disbursing. (against the explanation by R. Eliahu Fulda on the authority of R. David Oppenheim.) It would be unavoidable that the disburser swallow some drops of water, but this does not require any benediction for the water as food.</i>.
Rebbi Samuel bar Naḥman in the name of Rebbi Jonathan: In the Torah, in Prophets, and in Hagiographs we find that a person had to be innocent in the eyes of people just as he has to be innocent in the eyes of the Omnipresent. In the Torah from where? As it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 32:22" href="/Numbers.32.22"><i>Num</i>. 32:22</a>.</i> y<i>ou have to be blameless before the Eternal and before Israel</i>. In Prophets from where? As it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote"><i><a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 22:22" href="/Joshua.22.22">Jos. 22:22</a></i>.</i>, <i>The Power, God, Eternal, the Power, God, Eternal, He knows, and Israel has to know</i>. In Hagiographs from where? As it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 3:4" href="/Proverbs.3.4"><i>Prov</i>. 3:4</a>.</i>, <i>find grace and understanding in the eyes of God and man.</i> Gamaliel the twin asked Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun, which one is the clearest<sup class="footnote-marker">52a</sup><i class="footnote">B: The most stringent.</i> of all of these? He answered him, y<i>ou have to be blameless before the Eternal and before Israel</i>.

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> A member of the household of Rabban Gamliel was entering with his <i>sheqel</i> between his fingers and threw it before the disburser<sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 2:2:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.2.2.2">Chapter 2, Note 35</a>.</i>. The disburser was directing it and threw it into the box. The disburser only starts disbursing after he asked, “shall I disburse”? And they<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">The treasurers standing outside.</i> answer him, “disburse, disburse, disburse,” three times.<br>He disburses the first time and covers it with cushions<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">Greek καταβολή “support, cushion”.</i>, the second time and covers it with cushions. The third time he was not covering<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">He covers the coins remaining in the lodge where the receipts for the <i>sheqalim</i> are kept. As explained in the Mishnah, the monies taken on the first of Nisan are from the contributions of the Land of Israel, those taken before Pentecost are from neighboring countries and those at the end of Elul from Babylonia, Persia, and other far countries. Monies not used for sacrifices are used for other expenses as explained in the next Chapter. In order to give due credit, the monies should not be mixed even though in an emergency one can have regress on those already labelled as surplus.</i>. Why did he cover? That he should not forget and disburse from anything which already had been disbursed. The first time he disbursed in the name of the Land of Israel, the second time in the name of nearby walled cities<sup class="footnote-marker">58a</sup><i class="footnote">Jewish settlemens in Syria and Egypt.</i>, and the third time in the name of Babylonia, in the name of Media, and in the name of distant countries.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “A member of the household of Rabban Gamliel was,” etc. If there were two heaps and he gave heave from one for the other, would that not remove the liability from the other<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote">Since for heave all produce of the same kind is interchangeable, by analogy all <i>sheqalim</i> are interchangeable; there is no reason why the House of Rabban Gamliel should be interested in controlling in which box their <i>sheqel</i> ends up.</i>? It gave them satisfaction that the sacrifice should be brought first from their money<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">While legally the <i>sheqel</i> becomes Temple property and is no longer their own, they derive satisfaction from knowing that their contribution will be used for sacrifices rather than for any of the ancillary uses spelled out later for which the <i>sheqel</i> also could be used.</i>.
“He disburses the first time,” etc. It was stated: If he removed the covers, all was made remainder<sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote">Since no due credit could be given to the contributors of the new <i>sheqalim</i>. The monies should be given to the gift account.</i>. It was stated: The third was the richest since it contained golden stateres<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Shekalim (Lieberman) 2:4" href="/Tosefta_Shekalim_(Lieberman).2.4">Tosephta 2:4</a> reads אִסטראות, half darics.</i> and golden darics.
It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup>: He disburses the first time in the name of the Land of Israel and in the name of all of Israel<sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Shekalim (Lieberman) 2:3" href="/Tosefta_Shekalim_(Lieberman).2.3">Tosephta 2:3</a>.</i>. The second time in the name of fortified cities<sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote">While each batch is intended to be from one definite region, one cannot be sure whether somebody from another region gave his <i>sheqel</i> with them.
