Rebbi Jeremiah and Rebbi Abun bar Ḥiyya were sitting and saying, there said Rebbi Joḥanan said, the reason of Rebbi Simeon is that we find that a female is qualified as elevation offering of a bird<sup class="footnote-marker">128</sup><i class="footnote">Male animals are prescribed for four-legged elevation sacrifices, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 1:3" href="/Leviticus.1.3"><i>Lev.</i> 1:3</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 1:10" href="/Leviticus.1.10">10</a>, but not for birds, 1:14 (<i>Sifra Wayyiqra I Parshata</i>6(2,5). Argument missing in B.</i>. And here, he<sup class="footnote-marker">149</sup><i class="footnote">Even though the statement is transmitted in the name of R. Simeon ben Laqish, we do not hear that R. Joḥanan disagrees; the statement is coming from R. Joḥanan’s Academy.</i> says so? Rebbi Yose said, I confirmed it following what Rebbi Samuel said in the name of Rebbi Ze`ira: Anything which could be sacrificed neither itself nor its money’s worth is sanctified only as money’s worth<sup class="footnote-marker">150</sup><i class="footnote">If an animal is not dedicated as sacrifice and if sold, the money cannot be used to buy an animal which can validly be dedicated (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 4:4:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.4.4.4">Note 119</a>), the animal is given for the upkeep of the Temple, not to the gift account.</i>. And you are saying, this is correct. You cannot sacrifice it, for it is written <i>in cattle</i><sup class="footnote-marker">151</sup><i class="footnote">And the public to whom the bird was given may not dedicate it as sacrifice.</i>. You cannot redeem it since birds cannot be redeemed.<sup class="footnote-marker">152</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Menachot 12:1" href="/Mishnah_Menachot.12.1">Mishnah <i>Menaḥot</i>12:1</a>. Not only birds, but also dedicated wine and flour cannot be redeemed since the rules of redemption in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 27" href="/Leviticus.27"><i>Lev.</i> 27</a> are formulated referring to four-legged animals only.</i>
The colleagues in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan; Rebbi Ayvo bar Nagari said before Rebbi Ila in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan. The reason of this Tanna: <i>But if any impure animal from which no sacrifice to the Eternal may be offered</i><sup class="footnote-marker">153</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 27:11" href="/Leviticus.27.11"><i>Lev.</i> 27:11</a>.</i>. Why does the verse say, <i>impure</i><sup class="footnote-marker">154</sup><i class="footnote">Since no impure animal can be sacrificed, either the mention of “impure” or that of “cannot be sacrificed” seems to be superfluous.</i>? But even impure for this denomination<sup class="footnote-marker">155</sup><i class="footnote">If an animal was dedicated in a category for which it was not appropriate, and it never could be sacrificed in that category, it never was dedicated to the altar and therefore can be redeemed.</i>. This is difficult; about this is written, <i>he shall stand, he shall appraise</i><sup class="footnote-marker">156</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 27:12" href="/Leviticus.27.12"><i>Lev.</i> 27:12</a>.</i>? Rebbi Ze`ira in the name of Rebbi Eleazar did not say so but, <i>but if any impure animal from which no sacrifice to the Eternal may be offered</i>; anything which could be sacrificed neither here nor at any other place does not effect substitution<sup class="footnote-marker">157</sup><i class="footnote">If “impure” really means “unfit”, e. g. cattle or sheep with a broken leg, it is not dedicated to the altar and must be redeemed with the money going for the upkeep of the Temple. However, it cannot be made to stand as required by the verse.</i>. This excludes the female of a bird which even though it cannot be sacrificed here is fit to be sacrificed at another place. Rebbi Abbin and Rebbi Abun asked before Rebbi Ze`ira: Are there not the animals used for active or passive bestiality, which can be sacrificed neither here nor at any other place, and they effect substitution<sup class="footnote-marker">158</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Temurah 1:6" href="/Tosefta_Temurah.1.6">Tosephta <i>Temurah</i>1:12</a> states that dedicating such an animal, while sinful, is equivalent to dedicating an unblemished animal which after dedication becomes blemished; all rules of <i>me`ilah</i> do apply and it may be redeemed only after it develops a permanent bodily defect.</i>? He said to them, also I did speak only about really impure ones<sup class="footnote-marker">159</sup><i class="footnote">B reads: “defective ones.”</i>. This is difficult; about this is written, <i>he shall stand, he shall appraise</i><sup class="footnote-marker">156</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 27:12" href="/Leviticus.27.12"><i>Lev.</i> 27:12</a>.</i>?

Halakhah 5

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Once every thirty days one sets the prices for the office<sup class="footnote-marker">160</sup><i class="footnote">One lets contracts to supply the Temple with wine and flour to accompany the sacrifices. This lets the Temple set the prices for these items as explained in the next Chapter.</i>. Anyone who accepts to supply fine flour at a rate of four<sup class="footnote-marker">161</sup><i class="footnote">The contract is to supply 4 <i>seah</i> of flour for one tetradrachma.</i>, if the going rate goes up to three he has to supply at the rate of four<sup class="footnote-marker">164</sup><i class="footnote">When at the time of use the items were found to be in good order.</i>; if at the rate of three and the going rate went down to four he has to supply at four since the hand of the sanctuary is privileged. If the flour turned out worm-infected, it was infected in his possession<sup class="footnote-marker">163</sup><i class="footnote">Even if the worms were not detected at the time of delivery, only at the time of use.</i>; and if the wine turned into vinegar it was vinegar in his possession. He is not paid until the altar did atone<sup class="footnote-marker">164</sup><i class="footnote">When at the time of use the items were found to be in good order.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It was stated in the name of Rebbi Simeon: he receives his money immediately, for the priests are quick<sup class="footnote-marker">165</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 2:2:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.2.2.2">Chapter 2, Note 33</a>. The text there is reproduced in B and M.</i>.

Chapter 5



Halakhah 1

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> These are the appointees who were in the Sanctuary<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">The permanent officers of the Temple who organized the service which was executed by the families of the clans of Cohanim, who came to serve in turn for one week. Different in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Shekalim (Lieberman) 2:14-15" href="/Tosefta_Shekalim_(Lieberman).2.14-15">Tosephta 2:14–15</a>.</i>: Joḥanan ben Phineas of the seals<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 5:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.5.3.1">Mishnah 4</a>, a person who brings an animal as sacrifice to the Temple buys from the Temple the appropriate flour and wine offerings (as detailed in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 15:1-12" href="/Numbers.15.1-12"><i>Num</i>. 15:1–12</a>). The “seal” (or ”signature”) is a ticket stamped with one of different stamps. The worshipper buys the ticket from the keeper of seals and delivers it to the keeper of libations who then gives him the correct amount to give to the officiating priests.</i>, Aḥiyya of the libations, Mathew ben Samuel of the lotteries<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">The lotteries which distribute the different duties to the priests who came to serve for one week, as explained in <i>Yoma</i> Chapter 2.</i>, Petaḥiah of the nests<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">He organizes the sale of “nests”, couples of pigeons or turtle doves, needed for several purification rites.</i>. Petaḥiah is Mordecai. Why was he called Petaḥiah? For he had original ideas<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">In the interpretation of biblical verses.</i> and explained them, and he knew seventy languages<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezra 2:2" href="/Ezra.2.2"><i>Ezra</i>2:2</a> and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 7:7" href="/Nehemiah.7.7"><i>Neḥemiah</i>7:7</a> in the list of returnees from Babylonia one finds Mordecai Bilshan, where the traditional interpretation is to consider the second name not as an independent (Babylonian) name but an epithet “linguist” of Mordecai. (In modern Hebrew, by mispronunciation “linguist” is <i>balshan</i>.) A linguist is a person who knows the languages of all of the 70 peoples enumerated in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 7" href="/Genesis.7"><i>Gen</i>. 7</a>.</i>.<br>Ben Aḥiyyah for indigestion; Onias the digger of ditches, Gabinius the herald, Ben Gever for locking the doors, Ben Bevai for the oakum. Ben Arza for the cymbal, Hugdas ben Levi for the song. The family Garmu for the shew-bread, the family Eutinos for producing the incense. Eleazar for the gobelins, and Phineas the clothier.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">This text is from the end of Chapter 3 in <i>Yoma</i>(Notes 238,239), where all textual variants are noted.</i>“These are the appointees who were in the Sanctuary.” Rebbi Ḥizqiah said, Rebbi Simon and the rabbis. One said, he comes to enumerate the qualified ones of every generation. But the other said, he who was in a generation enumerated what was in his generation<sup class="footnote-marker">\</sup>. He who said, he comes to enumerate the qualified ones of every generation, about all of them he says, <i>the remembrance of the just is for blessing</i><sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 10:3" href="/Proverbs.10.3"><i>Prov</i>. 10:3</a>.</i>. He who said, he who was in a generation enumerated what was in his generation, about all of them he says, <i>but the name of evildoers shall rot</i>. About whom was said, <i>the remembrance of the just is for blessing</i>? About Ben Qaṭin<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">As mentioned in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yoma 3:9:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yoma.3.9.1">Mishnah <i>Yoma</i>3:11</a>.</i> and his kind.
Rebbi Jonah said, it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 53:12" href="/Isaiah.53.12"><i>Is.</i> 53:12</a>. The verse continues: <i>For he offered himself to death and counted the sinners.</i> This applies to R. Aqiba who was a martyr and organized religious tradition in a systematic corpus.</i>: <i>Therefore, I shall distribute to him in public, and with the powerful he shall have part in booty</i>, that is Rebbi Aqiba who organized interpretation of Scripture, practice, and homiletics<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">The reading of B: Mishnah, interpretation of Scripture, and practice, seems preferable since R. Aqiba had no reputation in homiletics and as a matter of principle homiletics about biblical verses is not to be systematized.</i>. But some say, this refers to the men of the Great Assembly, who organized principles and details<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">They find in the work of the Great Assembly the essence of Second Temple and later rabbinic Judaism, the effort to turn the mostly disjointed statements of the Torah into a systematic code of laws.</i>.
Rebbi Abbahu said, it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">1<i>Chr</i>. 2:55.</i> <i>The families of counters, dwellers of Yabeṣ.</i> Why does the verse say, <i>counters</i>? Because they formulated the teaching numbers, numbers<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">In B: ciphers, ciphers.</i>. “Five shall not lift heave.<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Terumot</i>1:1.</i>” “Fifteen women free their co-wives.<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yevamot 1:1:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yevamot.1.1.1">Mishnah <i>Yebamot</i>1:1</a>.</i>” “Thirty-six extirpations in the Torah.<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Keritot 1:1" href="/Mishnah_Keritot.1.1">Mishnah <i>Keritut</i>1:1</a>.</i>” “Thirteen matters about the carcass of a pure bird.<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Ṭehorot</i>1:1.</i>” “Four main categories of torts.<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Bava Kamma 1:1:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Bava_Kamma.1.1.1">Mishnah <i>Bava Qamma</i>1:1</a>.</i>” “Thirty-nine categories of work.”
Rebbi Aḥa said, <i>for Ezra the priest, the counter</i><sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezra 7:11" href="/Ezra.7.11"><i>Ezra</i>7:11</a>.</i>. But just as he was counting in the Torah so he was counting in the words of the Sages<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">The principles of <i>mesorah</i>, to fix the text of Scriptures by noting the number of occurrences of certain forms, is attributed to Ezra in <i>Megillah</i>4:1 (47d l. 49), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Megillah 3a" href="/Megillah.3a">Babli <i>Megillah</i>3a</a>. Similarly, the fixation of <i>mishnaiot</i> by numbers is attributed to him.</i>.
Rebbi Ḥaggai in the name of Rebbi Samuel bar Naḥman. The earlier generations ploughed, and sowed, and weeded, and trimmed, and hoed, cut, made sheaves, threshed, winnowed, milled, sifted, made dough, kneaded, and baked. But we do not even have a mouth to eat<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">Even though the earlier generation organized the study of religious texts in a systematic way, still we have difficulty following them.</i>. <sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">From here to the end of the next paragraph the text is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Demai 1:3:5-6" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Demai.1.3.5-6"><i>Demay</i>1:3, Notes 131–137</a> (<b>ד</b>).</i> Rebbi Abba bar Zemina said in the name of Rebbi Ze`ira: If the earlier generations were angels, we are men; if they were men, we are donkeys. Rebbi Mana said, at that moment<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">When a great scholar ate <i>ṭevel</i> without suspecting that it was not tithed.</i> they said, we are not even comparable to the she-ass of Rebbi Phineas ben Yair.
Robbers stole the she-ass of Rebbi Phineas ben Yair at night. She was hidden with them for three days during which she did not eat anything. After three days, they took counsel to return her. They said, remove her lest she die with us. They let her out; she returned to her master’s door and started braying. He said to them, open to that poor creature because for three days now she did not taste anything. They opened for her and she entered. He said to them, give her something to eat. They put oats before her but she did not eat. They said to him, rabbi, she does not want to eat. He asked them, did you put it in order? They said: Yes. He asked them, did you remove its <i>demay</i>? They said, did the rabbi not teach us: “He who buys seeds for animals, flour for tanning, oil for lighting, is free from <i>demay</i>”? He said to them, what can we do with this poor creature since she is very restrictive for herself? They removed the <i>demay</i> and she ate.
Petaḥiah of the nests<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">He organizes the sale of “nests”, couples of pigeons or turtle doves, needed for several purification rites.</i>. Come and see how great the power of this man was, for he “had original ideas<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">In the interpretation of biblical verses.</i> and explained them, and he knew seventy languages<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezra 2:2" href="/Ezra.2.2"><i>Ezra</i>2:2</a> and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 7:7" href="/Nehemiah.7.7"><i>Neḥemiah</i>7:7</a> in the list of returnees from Babylonia one finds Mordecai Bilshan, where the traditional interpretation is to consider the second name not as an independent (Babylonian) name but an epithet “linguist” of Mordecai. (In modern Hebrew, by mispronunciation “linguist” is <i>balshan</i>.) A linguist is a person who knows the languages of all of the 70 peoples enumerated in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 7" href="/Genesis.7"><i>Gen</i>. 7</a>.</i>.” It was stated: A Synhedrion of which two know how to speak<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">As a minimum two members of the Synhedrion have to be able to interrogate any witness in his own language and the rest of them have to be able to understand the answer. The Court may not use interpreters. In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sanhedrin 17b" href="/Sanhedrin.17b">Babli, <i>Sanhedrin</i>17b</a>, the reference is not to the Synhedrion as Supreme Court but to any court of criminal jurisdiction.</i> and all of them are able to hear is acceptable<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">As a minimal requirement.</i> as Synhedrion. Three is average, four is wise, and in Jabneh there were four, Ben Azzai and Ben Zoma, Ben Ḥanikai and Rebbi Eleazar ben Matthew.
Rav Ḥisda said, once the Land of Israel was dry (and they collected from <i>Gaggot-Ṣerifin</i><sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Menachot 10:2" href="/Mishnah_Menachot.10.2">Mishnah <i>Menaḥot</i>10:2</a>. <i>Ṣerifin</i> probably is Serafand in the plain NE of Jerusalem.</i>.) [and they did not know from where to bring<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">As spelled out in the Mishnah (and B), the problem was to find barley grain for the <i>`omer</i> which must be brought from the produce of the Land. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 64b" href="/Menachot.64b">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>64b</a>.</i>. There was there a mute person who put one hand on roofs and another on a shed. They brought him before Petaḥiah, who told them, is there a place called <i>Gaggot-Ṣerifin</i> or <i>Ṣerifin-Gaggot</i>? They went there and found.] Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, once the entire world<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">In B: The Land of Israel. The Mishnah refers to wheat grain for the Two Breads.</i> was burned and they did not know from where to bring. There was there a mute person who put one of his hands over his eyes and one hand on a door lock. They brought him before Petaḥiah, who told them, is there a place called <i>`Ein-Sokher</i><sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">A place near Sichem (Nablus.)</i> or <i>Sokher-Ayin</i>. They went there and found.
Three women brought their nests<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">Since Petaḥiah was in charge of these, it was his duty to instruct the officiating Cohanim in the correct way to sacrifice the birds. As obligatory offerings of a woman after prolonged menstruation as <i>zavah</i>, one bird is to be an elevation offering and the other a purification offering. As thanksgiving offerings both birds are elevation offerings.</i>. One said, לְעֵינָתִי; and one said, לְיַמָּתִי, and one said, לְזִיבָתִי. About the one who said <sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">Since עַיִין means both “eye” and “wellhead, spring”.</i>לְעֵינָתִי, they wanted to say, her menstrual flow is like a well. He said, she was dangerously sick in her eye. About the one who said לְיַמָּתִי, they wanted to say, her menstrual flow is like the sea. He said, she was in danger on the sea. About the one who said לְזִיבָתִי, they wanted to say, she was really a <i>zavah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">While in Mishnaic Hebrew זִיבָה means the state of a <i>zavah</i> it is asserted here that after the <i>alef</i> became silent it also could not carry a separate vowel. Therefore זְאֵב “wolf” became זֵאב and since the ־ֵ was pronounced as η, it sounded like זִיב. More than 70 languages, the administrator of nests had to know all local dialects.</i>. He told them, a wolf<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">The stone floor, which was unhealthy in winter.</i> came to snatch her son.
“Ben Aḥiyyah for indigestion.” Since the Cohanim were walking barefoot on the floor<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">The stone floor, which was unhealthy in winter.</i>, and were eating meat<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote">Since the priests are obligated to eat the meat of all purification and reparation offerings in the Temple on the day of the sacrifice and the following night, and in addition to the meat they have only baked goods made from flour offerings and water, for the week of their service their diet is very unbalanced and unhealthy.</i>, and drinking water, they got indigestion. He knew which wine was good for the intestines and which was noxious<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">The translation is tentative. Brill proposes to read מְמַסְמֵס “massages”. The reading of B, “eliminates intestines” is difficult to understand.</i> for intestines.
“Onias the digger of ditches.” He was digging ditches and caves<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">To create <i>miqwaot</i> for pilgrims to the Temple.</i> and knew which rock cools the water and which rock was dry and how far its dryness extended. Rebbi Aḥa said, but (he) [his son]<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote">Reading of B and the corrector, to be deleted.</i> died of thirst. <sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote">The text also is in <i>Yom Ṭov</i>3:9 (Note 124, <b>צ</b>).</i> Rebbi Ḥanina said, anybody who says that the All-Merciful is indulgent, his intestines shall dissolve themselves; for He is forbearing and then collects His due. Rebbi Aḥa said, it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 50:3" href="/Psalms.50.3"><i>Ps.</i> 50:3</a>.</i>, <i>His surroundings are very hairy</i>. He is exact with them like a hair’s width. Rebbi Yose said, not because of this reason, but because what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 89:8" href="/Psalms.89.8"><i>Ps.</i> 89:8</a>.</i>, <i>He is awesome on His surroundings</i>, His fear on those near Him is greater than those far away.
<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">This also is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Demai 1:3:13" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Demai.1.3.13"><i>Demay</i>1:3 (Note 150</a>) and similarly in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Devarim Rabbah 3" href="/Devarim_Rabbah.3"><i>Deut</i>. <i>rabba</i>3</a>.</i> Rebbi Ḥaggai in the name of Rebbi Samuel bar Naḥman: It happened that a pious person used to dig cisterns, ditches, and caves for travellers. Once, his daughter travelled to marry<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">To sing at the daily sacrifices.</i> and she was swept away by a river. All the people came to him and wanted to console him, but he refused to be consoled. Rebbi Phineas ben Yair came to him and wanted to console him, but he refused to be consoled. He told them, is that your pious man? They said to him: Rabbi, such and such he did, such and such happened to him. He replied: It is impossible that he would honor his Creator by water and He hurts him by water! Immediately, there started a rumor in the town that the man’s daughter had returned. Some say, she got trapped in a hedge of thorns, others say that an angel came in the appearance of Rebbi Phineas ben Yair and saved her.
“Gabinius the herald.” He was announcing in the Temple. What did he say? “The Cohanim to the service, and the Levites to the podium<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">To sing at the daily sacrifices.</i>, and Israel to stand by<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote">Representing the entire people for whom the sacrifices were brought, in later Second Temple times a delegation of the people from the district of the week’s Cohanim was present during the offering of the daily sacrifices.</i>.” King Agrippas heard his voice at a distance of eight parasangs<sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote">Using Egyptian measures this would be about 36 km. B (but not M) reads “one parasang”, about 4.5 km.</i> and gave him rich gifts.
“Ben Gever for locking the doors.” Rav explained for the House of Rebbi Shila, “when <i>gever</i> called<sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yoma 1:8:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yoma.1.8.1">Mishnah <i>Yoma</i>1:8</a>.</i>” as “when the herald proclaimed.” They said to him, “when the rooster called.” He said to them, did we not state “Ben Gever”? Could you say, “the son of the rooster”?
“Ben Bevay for the oakum, he was threading the wicks<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">This is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yoma 2:2:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yoma.2.2.3"><i>Yoma</i>2:2, Note 106</a>.</i>. <sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">This text is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Peah 8:6:5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Peah.8.6.5"><i>Peah</i>8:7, Notes 94–96</a> (<b>פ</b>).</i> Rebbi Yose went up to Kufra and wanted to appoint providers<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote">Overseers of charity.</i> there, but they did not accept. He came and said before them: “Ben Bavai over the oakum.” If this one had been appointed over the wicks and therefore merited to be counted with the leaders of his generation, you who are being appointed over the lives of people, so much more.
“Ben Arza for the cymbal;” as we have stated there<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Tamid 7:3" href="/Mishnah_Tamid.7.3">Mishnah <i>Tamid</i>7:3</a>.</i>, “the executive officer waves a sheet and Ben Arza plays the cymbal.”
“Hugdas ben Levi for the song.” Rebbi Aḥa said, he knew a special melody. When he put his thumb in his mouth he produced all kinds of sounds and the heads of his fellow Levites were taken aback.
<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote">This and the next paragraphs are from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yoma 3:9:2-4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yoma.3.9.2-4"><i>Yoma</i>3:8, Notes 225–235</a>, where also the differences in readings are noted. The additions of the corrector in the story of the family Eutinos are from B.</i> The family Garmu were experts in preparing the shew-bread and its removal from the oven, but they did not want to teach. They sent and brought craftsmen from Alexandria who were experts in preparing the shew-bread but were not experts in its removal from the oven. The family Garmu were heating from within and removing from the outside, and it did not become moldy. But those were heating from the inside and removing from the inside, and it became moldy. When the Sages realized this situation, they said, everything which the Holy One, praise to Him, created, he created to His glory; <i>all work of the Eternal is for Himself</i><sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 16:4" href="/Proverbs.16.4"><i>Prov</i>. 16:4</a>.</i>. They sent after them, but they refused to come until they doubled their wages. They used to take twelve <i>mina</i>, so they gave them twenty-four. Rebbi Jehudah says, they used to take 24, so they gave them 48. They asked them, why do you not want to teach? They answered them, there is a tradition among us from our forefathers that this Temple will be destroyed in the future. Others should not learn and prepare the same before their foreign worship. In the following matter one mentions them for praise, that in the hands of their children white bread was never found, so people should not say, from the preparation of shew-bread they are eating.
“The family Eutinos were experts in preparing the incense and the smoke-creating herb, but they did not want to teach. They sent and brought craftsmen from Alexandria who were experts in preparing the incense but were not experts in the smoke-creating herb. The family Eutinos’s was going straight up, and spread, and descended. But theirs was immediately spreading. When the Sages realized the situation, they said, everything which the Holy One, praise to Him, created, he created to His glory; as it is said<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 43:7" href="/Isaiah.43.7"><i>Is.</i>43:7</a>.</i>, <i>all which is called by My Name,</i> etc. They sent after them, but they refused to come until they doubled their wages. They used to take twelve <i>mina</i>, so they gave them twenty-four. Rebbi Jehudah says, they used to take 24, so they gave them 48. They asked them, why do you not want to teach? They answered them, there is a tradition among us from our forefathers that this Temple will be destroyed in the future. Others should not learn and prepare the same before their foreign worship. In the following matter one mentions them for praise, that no woman of any of them ever went out perfumed. Not only that, but if one of them married a woman from outside, he contracted with her that she should not use perfume, [that one should not say, they perfume themselves from the compounding of incense, to confirm what is said, <i>you shall be innocent in the eyes of the Eternal and of Israel</i>.]
Rebbi Yose said, I found a child of the family Eutinos. I said to him, my son, from which family are you? he told me, from family X. I said to him, my son, because your forefathers intended to increase their prestige and to decrease Heaven’s prestige, therefore their prestige was diminished and Heaven’s prestige increased. Rebbi Aqiba said, Simeon ben Lagos told me, I was collecting herbs, I and a youth from the family Eutinos, when I saw him crying and laughing. I said to him, my son, why did you cry? He said to me, about the prestige of my family which is diminished. And why did you laugh? About the glory prepared for the Just in the future world. [What did you see?] There is smoke-creating herb before me! I said to him, my son, show it to me. He answered me, I have a tradition from my ancestors not to show it to any creature.’ Rebbi Joḥanan ben Nuri said, I met an old man from the family Eutinos [who held a scroll about chemicals.]. He said to me, ‘Rabbi. In the past my family were humble, and transmitting this scroll one to the other. But now they are not trustworthy; here the scroll is yours and take care of it.’ When I came and repeated these words before Rebbi Aqiba, his tears flowed and he said, from now on we do not have to mention them for shame.
“Eleazar for the gobelins,” he was appointed to oversee the weavers of the gobelins. “Phineas the clothier.” He clothed the garments of the High Priesthood. It happened that a Cohen dressed a general<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote">Greek στρατιώτης.</i> who gave him 8 pieces of gold, and some say, he gave him twelve.

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> One does not appoint less than seven overseers<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">In the Temple. The etymology of the word seems to be אָמַר-כֹל “he commands everything.”</i> and three treasurers<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">In the Temple.</i>, and one does not appoint less than two persons to an executive office spending money<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">This includes treasurers of public funds outside the Temple.</i>, except Ben Aḥiyyah for indigestion and Eleazar for the gobelins, for these the public accepted<sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote">The Temple had to pay for Ben Aḥiyya’s prescriptions and Eleazar’s assignments for work delivered on their signature alone, without co-signer.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “One does not appoint less than three treasurers and seven overseers.” It was stated: And two καθολικοί<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote">In imitation of the financial administration of the Roman Empire which at the Emperor’s court was directed by the katholikoi.</i>. That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 31:13" href="/II_Chronicles.31.13"><i>2Chr.</i> 31:13</a>, misquoted (but less badly than in B.) Description of Ezekias’s Temple organization.</i>, <i>and Yeḥiel, and Uzziahu, and Maḥat,</i> treasurers; <i>and Asael, and Yerimot, and Yozavad, and Eliel, and Samkhiahu, and Maḥat, and Conaiahu,</i> overseers, <i>officers supervised by Konaniahu and his brother Simei</i>, katholikoi; <i>appointed by King Yeḥizkiahu and Azariahu the governor of God’s House</i>, King and High Priest.
When he seals<sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote">Money bags.</i>, the treasurer seals and gives it to the overseer. The overseer seals and gives it to the katholikos. The katholikos seals and gives it to the High Priest. The High Priest seals and gives it to the King. And if the break the seals, the King sees his seal and breaks it<sup class="footnote-marker">62a</sup><i class="footnote">In all cases, B reads “recognizes” instead of “breaks”.</i>. The High Priest sees his seal and breaks it. The katholikos sees his seal and breaks it. The overseer sees his seal and breaks it. The treasurer sees his seal and breaks it.
“One does not appoint less than two persons to an executive office spending money.” Rebbi Naḥman in the name of Rebbi Mana: Following<sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 28:5" href="/Exodus.28.5"><i>Ex.</i> 28:5</a>.</i> <i>they should take</i><sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">Formulated in the plural; one never lets public property be used by a single person. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bava Batra 8b" href="/Bava_Batra.8b">Babli <i>Bava Batra</i>8b</a>.</i> <i>the gold, and the blue wool, and the purple wool.</i>
<sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Nedarim 38a" href="/Nedarim.38a">Babli <i>Nedarim</i>38a</a>, <i>Tanḥuma Eqev</i>(9), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Shemot Rabbah 46:2" href="/Shemot_Rabbah.46.2"><i>Ex. rabba</i>46(2</a>).</i> Rebbi Ḥama ben Rebbi Ḥanina said, Moses got rich from the refuse of the tablets. That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 34:1" href="/Exodus.34.1"><i>Ex.</i> 34:1</a>.</i>, <i>cut for yourself two stone tablets</i>. <i>Cut for yourself</i><sup class="footnote-marker">667</sup>, the refuse shall be yours. Rebbi Ḥanin said, The Holy One, praise to Him, created<sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote">B: uncovered.</i> a quarry of precious stones and pearls in his tent, and from this Moses got rich.
<sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 30:11-34:35" href="/Exodus.30.11-34.35"><i>Tanḥuma Ki Tissa</i>26</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 33b" href="/Kiddushin.33b">Babli <i>Qiddušin</i>33b</a>. A slightly differently arranged text is <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Bikkurim 3:3:2-20" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Bikkurim.3.3.2-20"><i>Bikkurim</i>3:3</a>. This text shows that the corrector’s addition [in brackets] is from B; it is missing in the Yerushalmi sources and M.</i> It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 33:8" href="/Exodus.33.8"><i>Ex.</i> 33:8</a>.</i>, <i>they looked after Moses until he reached the Tent.</i> Two Amoraim, one says for shame, the other one says for praise. He who says for shame, “look at the thigh, look at the feet, look at his flesh. He eats from the Jews, and drinks from the Jews, everything he has is from the Jews.” He who says for praise, to see the just ones is meritorious [great for one who was worthy to see him.]

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Four stamps<sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in the next Mishnah, with these tickets one bought the prescribed amounts of flour, oil, and wine, prescribed for each kind of sacrifice (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 15:1-16" href="/Numbers.15.1-16"><i>Num</i>. 15:1–16</a>.)</i> were in the Temple; on them was written calf, ram, lamb, sinner. Ben Azzai says, there were five, and Aramaic was written on them, calf, ram, lamb, poor sinner, rich sinner. “Calf” serves for the libations of cattle, large or small, male or female<sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote">3/10 of an <i>ephah</i> of flour, half a <i>hin</i> olive oil and half a <i>hin</i> wine. An <i>ephah</i> is 3 <i>seah</i>; in the Roman system (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Kelim 17:11" href="/Mishnah_Kelim.17.11">Mishnah <i>Kelim</i>17:11</a>) a <i>cadus</i> of about 38 l. A <i>hin</i> is half a <i>seah</i>; half a <i>hin</i> is a Roman <i>congius</i> of about 3.2 l. The basic fluid measure is the <i>log</i>(<i>sextarius</i>) of about .53 l; half a <i>hin</i> are 6 <i>log</i>.</i>. “Lamb” serves for the libations of sheep and goats, large or small, male or female<sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">1/10 <i>ephah</i> of flour, 1/4 <i>hin</i>(3 <i>log</i>) each of oil and wine.</i>, except for rams. “Ram” only serves for the libations with a ram<sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote">2/10 <i>ephah</i> of flour, 1/3 <i>hin</i>(4 <i>log</i>) each of oil and wine. A ram is a male sheep older than 13 months (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Parah 1:3" href="/Mishnah_Parah.1.3">Mishnah <i>Parah</i>1:3</a>)</i>. “Sinner” serves for the three animals of the sufferer from skin disease<sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote">The rich healed sufferer from skin disease had to bring 3 sheep and an extra <i>log</i> of oil, in total 3/10 of an <i>ephah</i> of flour, 10 <i>log</i> of oil, and 9 <i>log</i> of wine. As explained in the Halakhah, the anonymous majority holds that the poor healed sufferer from skin disease, who had to bring only one sheep, buys the ticket for the sheep and brings the extra <i>log</i> of oil with him. Since skin disease led to social ostracism, it is not mentioned on the ticket.</i>.<br>If somebody needs libations he goes to Joḥanan who is overseeing the stamps, gives him the money, and receives a ticket from him. He goes to Aḥiyya who is overseeing the libations, gives him the ticket, and receives the libations from him. In the evening they<sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">Joḥanan and Aḥiyya.</i> come together, Aḥiyya produces the tickets and receives money correspondingly<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote">Since he not only handed out the materials but also bought them for the Temple from wholesalers.</i>. If there was a deficit, it is his<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">Joḥanan’s.</i> deficit and Joḥanan has to pay from his own. But if there was excess<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">If more money was taken in than the value of the libations handed out.</i> it belongs to the Temple since the hand of the Temple is privileged.<br>If somebody lost his ticket, one lets him wait until the evening. If they find for him corresponding to his ticket one gives to him; otherwise one does not give to him.<sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote">If a person notified the authorities that he had lost his ticket and the daily accounting at the end of the day showed that libations in the value of what he claimed was his ticket remains after the other claims had been paid, the difference is not declared as excess but is used to provide him with his libations. Otherwise he has lost his money.</i> The date was written on it because of the tricksters<sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote">The ticket was valid only one day so nobody could claim that he had lost his ticket, and if he was lucky got his libations without paying, and then presented the ticket on another day.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> And following Ben Azzai, why the [poor]<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from B.</i> sinner? He brought his <i>log</i> with him, and following the rabbis he brings a lamb<sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 5:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.5.3.1">Note 75</a>.</i>. What are the libations for a mother sheep<sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote">Since there is a difference between the libations needed for a young male sheep and those for an adult male, why does one not make the same distinction for females?</i>? Since we stated, “ ‘lamb’ serves for the libations of sheep and goats, large or small, male or female,” this implies that the libations of a mother sheep are like the libations of a lamb. It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 15:11" href="/Numbers.15.11"><i>Num</i>. 15:11</a>.</i>, <i>so you shall do for one bull, or for one ram, or an animal from sheep or goats.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sifry Num.</i>107.</i> This tells that He did not differentiate between libations for a calf and libations for a bull. Since one could argue, an animal from the flock needs libations, a bovine animal needs libations. Since we find that He distinguished between the libations for a sheep and the libations for a ram, so we should differentiate between libations for a calf and libations for a bull. The verse says, <i>so you shall do for one bull</i>; this implies that He did not distinguish between libations for a calf and libations for a bull. Why was it said, <i>or for a ram</i>? Since one could argue, if we find that He differentiated between libations for a yearling and libations for a two-year old, so we should differentiate between libations for a two-years old and a three-years old. The verse says, <i>or for one ram.</i> Why was it said, <i>or for an animal from sheep</i>? Since one could argue, if we find that He differentiated between libations for a sheep and libations for a ram, so we should differentiate between libations for a young female sheep and libations for a mother sheep. The verse says, <i>or for an animal from sheep</i>. Why was it said, <i>or a goat</i>? Since one could argue, if we find that He differentiated between libations for a sheep and libations for a ram, so we should differentiate between libations for a kid goat and libations for a bellwether. The verse says, <i>or for a goat</i>, it compared the smallest kid goat to the largest bellwether<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">The distinction by age applicable to sheep is not applicable to goats.</i>. Since one needs three <i>log</i>, so the other needs three <i>log</i>.
Think of it, if he matched it<sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote">Writing the day of the week on the ticket will not defeat the trickster who will wait just one week to cash in on his ticket.</i> with that day! The name of the watch<sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote">The name of the one of 24 priestly watches which serves in the week of this particular sacrifice.</i> was written on it. Think of it, if he matched the watch<sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote">The ticket will be valid again in another 24 weeks.</i>. The name of the day, the week<sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">The week is named after the portion to be read from the Torah on the following Sabbath.</i>, and the month was written on them; then it is impossible to match<sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote">Since the length of the lunar/solar year varies between 50 and 55 weeks, even with a computed calendar it will take very many years before the same watch will officiate again in the same week, and without a computed one it is totally impossible to predict the recurrence of this match.</i>.

Halakhah 4

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Two lodges were in the Temple, one the silence lodge and one the vessel lodge. The silence lodge: Silently did sin-fearing people contribute there and poor people from good families were supported from there in silence. The vessel lodge: Anybody who vowed a vessel throws it in there. Once in 30 days the treasurers open it. Any vessel which they deem is needed for the upkeep of the Temple they keep, but the remainder is sold and their proceeds belong to the lodge of upkeep of the Temple.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote">The following text (except the last paragraph) also is found in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Peah 8:8:7-14" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Peah.8.8.7-14"><i>Peah</i>8:9, Notes 149–167</a> (<b>פ</b>). Also there exists a Genizah text from here to Chapter 7 (<b>ג</b>).</i> Rebbi Jacob bar Idi and Rebbi Isaac bar Naḥman were providers<sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote">Administrators of the welfare fund.</i> and gave a denar to Rebbi Ḥama the father of Rabbi Oshaia, but he gave it away to others. All were saying evil things about Rebbi Zachariah, the son-in-law of Rebbi Levi; they said that he was taking while he did not need it. When he died, they checked and found that he was splitting it up for others.
Rebbi Ḥinena bar Pappos used to distribute his charity in the night. Once the prince of spirits encountered him. He said to him, did not our teacher teach us: <i>Do not displace your neighbour’s boundaries</i><sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 19:14" href="/Deuteronomy.19.14"><i>Deut</i>. 19:14</a>.</i>? He said to him, but is it not written, <i>a gift in secret appeases anger</i><sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 21:14" href="/Proverbs.21.14"><i>Prov</i>. 21:14</a>.</i>? He was afraid of him and fled from him.
Rebbi Jonah said, it is not written, “hail to him who gives to the needy,“ but: <i>hail to him who is considerate to the needy</i><sup class="footnote-marker">99</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 41:2" href="/Psalms.41.2"><i>Ps.</i> 41:2</a>.</i>; this refers to him who fulfills this commandment intelligently. How did Rebbi Jonah do it? When he saw a son of a prominent family who had lost his property, he used to say to him: My son, since I heard that an inheritance fell to you at another place, take and you will pay back. When he had taken it, he said to him, it is a gift.
Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Ada said, in our days there were old people who used to take if somebody gave to them between New Year’s Day and the Great Fastday. After that, they were not taking. They said, there is permission for us.
Neḥemiah from Shiḥin met a Jerusalemite who said to him, acquire merit by giving me a chicken. He said to him, here is its value, go buy red meat; he bought, ate and died. He said, come and eulogize him whom Neḥemiah killed.
Naḥum from Gimzo was carrying a gift to the house of his father-in-law when he met a person afflicted with boils who asked him, acquire merit from what you have on you. He said to him, when I shall return. He returned and found him dead. He said before him, his eyes which saw you and did not give to you shall go blind, his hands which did not stretch out to give to you shall be cut off, his feet which did not run to give to you shall be broken. This happened to him. Rebbi Aqiba came to visit him and said, woe to me that I see you in this state. He answered, woe to me that I do not see you in this state. He asked, why do you curse me? He answered, why are you contemptuous of suffering?
The teacher of the great Rebbi Hoshaia’s son was blind and he used to invite him to eat with him every day. One day there were guests and he did not ask him to eat with him. In the evening, he went to him and said: Please, Sir, do not be angry with me. [Since I had guests, I did not want risking injuring the Sir’s honor, therefore I did not eat with you today.]<sup class="footnote-marker">100</sup><i class="footnote">The corrector’s addition in this paragraph is necessary as shown by the parallels.</i> He said to him, you assuaged him who is seen but does not see; may He be appeased by you Who sees but is not seen. He asked him, from where do you have this? He said, from Rebbi Eliezer ben Jacob. For there came a blind man to Rebbi Eliezer ben Jacob’s town; Rebbi Eliezer ben Jacob sat below him so that they should say if he were not a great person, Rebbi Eliezer ben Jacob would not sit below him. They provided for him in honor. He asked them, what is this? They told him, because Rebbi Eliezer ben Jacob sat below you. He prayed for him the following prayer: You did a good deed for one who is seen but does not see; He Who sees but is not seen may be appeased by you and do good for you.
Clarification. Rebbi Ḥama bar Ḥanina and Rebbi Hoshaiah were strolling through the synagogue of Lod. Rebbi Ḥama bar Ḥanina said to Rebbi Hoshaiah: How much money did my forefathers invest here! He answered him: How many souls did your forefathers invest here, there is no one in here who studies Torah<sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote">In B: How many souls did your forefathers lose here, are there no ones here who study Torah?</i>!
Rebbi Abun made doors for the main house of study. Rebbi Mana came to him; he said to him, look what I did. He told him, <i>Israel forgot its Creator and built palaces</i><sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Hosea 8:14" href="/Hosea.8.14"><i>Hos.</i>8:14</a>.</i>. Were there no people who study Torah<sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote">Support of needy students is more important than great buildings on campus.</i>?
It was stated: Altar <i>sancta</i> take what is appropriate for them from <i>sancta</i> of upkeep of the Temple. <i>Sancta</i> of upkeep of the Temple do not take what is appropriate for them from altar <i>sancta</i><sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup>. But did we not state, “any vessel which they deem is needed for the upkeep of the Temple they keep, but the remainder is sold and their proceeds fall into the lodge of upkeep of the Temple<sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote">This implies that vessels needed for the service of the altar cannot be used directly but must be sold and other vessels bought in their stead.</i>”? Rebbi Ḥizqiah said, so is the Mishnah: in case of need<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote">For any need, including the altar.</i> from the lodge of upkeep of the Temple.

Chapter 6



Halakhah 1

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Thirteen horns, thirteen tables, and thirteen prostrations were in the Temple. The family of Rabban Gamliel and of Rebbi Ḥanania the Second in Command of the priests were prostrating themselves fourteen times. And where was the additional one? In front of the storage room of the wood since they had a tradition from their forefathers that there the Ark was hidden.<br>It happened that a Cohen was occupied when he saw that a floor tile was different from the others. He went to tell it to a comrade but could not finish speaking before his soul left him; then they knew with certainty the the Ark was hidden there.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “Thirteen horns,” etc. It was stated: these horns were curved; narrow on top and wide on the bottom because of the tricksters<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">The “horns” were chests for the money given to the Temple for various reasons, as detailed in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 6:4:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.6.4.1">Mishnah 7</a>. A person putting money into one of the chests could not put his hand into it, he had to let the coins drop in from the top.</i>.
It was stated in the name of Rebbi Eliezer: <sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Shekalim (Lieberman) 2:18" href="/Tosefta_Shekalim_(Lieberman).2.18">Tosephta 2:18</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 53b" href="/Yoma.53b">Babli <i>Yoma</i>53b</a>..</i>“The Ark was deported with them to Babylon. What is the reason? <i>There will not remain a word</i><sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Kings 20:17" href="/II_Kings.20.17"><i>2K.</i>20:17</a>.</i>. <i>Word</i> refers only to what contains the Words. And so it says, <i>at the turn of the year king Nebuchadnezzar sent and brought him to Babylon with the desirable vessels of the Eternal’s House</i><sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 36:10" href="/II_Chronicles.36.10"><i>2Chr.</i>36:10</a>. In the Tosephta this is the reason given by R. Simeon (ben Yoḥay) in support of R. Eliezer.</i>. What are <i>the desirables of the Eternal’s House</i>? This is the Ark. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">This name of an Amora is impossible in a Tosephta. B has R. Jehudah bar Ilay; the Tosephta R. Jehudah ben Laqish (a fifth generation Tanna). Also quoted in <i>Sefer Wehizhir</i> p. 92a.</i> said, at its place it was hidden. That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 8:8" href="/I_Kings.8.8"><i>1K</i>. 8:8</a>.</i>, <i>the poles were long; the tips of the poles were seen in the Sanctuary, in front of the Hall, but were not seen outside,</i>&lt;<i>and were there until this day.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">The additional words are only in <b>ג</b> and the Tosephta; they are the reason for ben Laqish’s statement.</i>&gt; It is written, <i>were seen</i>, and you are saying, <i>but were not seen</i>. They protrude and stick out like a woman’s breasts<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">This argument only explains the wording of the verse, explaining that the ends of the poles with which the Ark was carried were noticed on the gobelin between the Sanctuary and the Holiest of Holies. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 54a" href="/Yoma.54a">Babli <i>Yoma</i>54a</a> in the name of Rav Jehudah.</i>.
But the rabbis say, the Ark was hidden in the storage room of the wood. It happened that a blemished Cohen was splitting wood in the storage room of the wood and saw a floor plate different from the others. <sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">This and the next sentences are missing in B and M; the full text is quoted by <i>Sefer Wehizhir</i>(p. קיג); a slightly different full version is in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 54a" href="/Yoma.54a">Babli <i>Yoma</i>54a</a>.</i> He came and said to a colleague, come and see this floor plate which is different from the others. They did not finish the matter before his soul left him; then they knew that there the Ark was hidden. Rebbi Hoshaia stated<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">B and M: It was stated in R. Hoshaia’s name.</i>: He hit on it with a sledgehammer; fire erupted and burned him.
<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">From here to the end of the Halakhah the text is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 8:3:3-12" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.8.3.3-12"><i>Soṭah</i>8:3 (Notes 43–130</a>,<b>ס</b>), where all references to the Babli are given.</i> It was stated: “Rebbi Jehudah ben Laqish says, two arks were travelling with Israel in the desert; one in which the Torah was deposited and one in which the broken pieces of the tablets were deposited. The one in which the Torah was deposited was put into the Tent of Meeting; that is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 14:44" href="/Numbers.14.44"><i>Num</i>. 14:44</a>.</i>: <i>Moses and the Ark of the Eternal’s covenant did not move from the camp</i>. The one in which the broken pieces of the tablets were deposited was going out and coming in with them<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sifry Num</i>. #82, referring to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 10:33" href="/Numbers.10.33"><i>Num</i>. 10.33</a>.</i>. But the Rabbis say, it was only one, and once it went out in the days of Eli and was taken prisoner. A verse supports the Rabbis: <i>Woe to us, who will save us from this mighty god</i><sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 5:8" href="/I_Samuel.5.8"><i>1S.</i>5:8</a>.</i><i>?</i> A word which shows that they never had seen it before. A verse supports Rebbi Jehudah ben Laqish. <i>Saul said to Aḥiya: present God’s Ark</i><sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 14:18" href="/I_Samuel.14.18"><i>1S.</i>14:18</a>.</i>. But was the Ark not at Qiryat Ye`arim? What do the rabbis do with it? ‘Present to me the High Priest’s diadem<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">This is the correct interpretation, as explained at the end of <i>Yoma</i> Chapter 7, not “ephod” following LXX and many moderns.</i>’ Another verse supports Rebbi Jehudah ben Laqish: <i>The Ark, Israel, and Jehudah, dwell in huts</i><sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 11:11" href="/II_Samuel.11.11"><i>2S.</i> 11:11</a>.</i>. Was the Ark not in Zion? What do the rabbis with it? The straw roof cover that was in the walls, since the Temple was not yet built.
When the ark was hidden, there were hidden with it the flask of Manna, the bottle of anointing oil, Aaron’s staff with its almonds and flowers, and the chest which the Philistines returned as a reparation sacrifice for Israel’s God. Who hid it? Josiah hid it. When he saw that it was written: <i>The Eternal will lead you and your king whom you will have put above you, to a people whom</i> neither you nor your fathers had known, he started and hid it. That is what is written: <i>He said to the Levites, who instruct all of Israel, the ones holy to the Eternal, put the Ark into the House that Salomon, son of David, King of Israel, built; you do not have to carry it on your shoulder.</i>” He said, if it is exiled with you to Babylonia, you will never return it to its place. But <i>now, serve the Eternal, your God, and his people Israel.</i>
The preparation of the anointing oil. <i>Take for yourself select spices,</i> etc. <i>and cassia 500,</i> etc., altogether 1500 parts. <i>And olive oil one hin</i>, that is twelve <i>log</i>, in which the roots were cooked, the words of Rebbi Meןr. Rebbi Jehudah says, he cooked them in water, then poured the oil on them, and when it had absorbed the fragrance one removed it, just as the perfumers do. That is what is written: <i>holy anointing oil</i>, etc.
<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">This and the following paragraph also are in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Horayot 3:2:2-5:7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Horayot.3.2.2-5.7"><i>Horaiot</i>3:3</a> (<b>ה</b>).</i> Rebbi Jehudah bar Ilay stated: The anointing oil made by Moses in the desert was from the start to the end a work of wonders, since there were only twelve log to start with, as it was said, <i>and olive oil one hin</i>. It would not have been enough to rub the wooden planks with it; so much more since the fire swallows, wood absorbs, and the kettle absorbs! From it the Tabernacles and all its vessels were anointed, the table and its vessels, the candelabrum and all its vessels. From it Aaron and his sons were anointed all of the seven days of induction, from it all high priests and kings were anointed. A king who is first needs anointing, a king who is a king’s son does not need anointing. [What is the reason? <i>Do anoint him, for this one is it</i><sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 17:20" href="/I_Samuel.17.20"><i>1S</i>. 17:20</a>.</i>, this one needs anointing but his son does not need anointing.]<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from B.</i> But a High Priest who is the son of a High Priest needs anointing, even for ten generations. Nevertheless, it is all there for the future; that is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 30:31" href="/Exodus.30.31"><i>Ex.</i> 30:31</a>.</i>, <i>a holy anointing oil will this be for Me, for all your generations</i>.
One anoints kings only at a spring, as it was said<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 1:33-34" href="/I_Kings.1.33-34"><i>1K</i>. 1:33–34</a>.</i>: <i>Let Solomon, my son, ride on my mule and take him down to the Giḥon; there Ṣadoq the priest and</i> Nathan the prophet shall anoint him as king over Israel. One anoints (kings) [kings sons of kings]<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from B, not found in Yerushalmi sources. The mention of Jehu shows that the scribe’s text is the correct one.</i> only because of disputes. Why was Solomon anointed? Because of the dispute of Adoniahu, Joash because of Athaliah, Jehu because of Joram. Is it not written<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 17:20" href="/I_Samuel.17.20"><i>1S</i>. 17:20</a>.</i>, <i>do anoint him, for this one is it,</i> this one needs anointing, but the kings of Israel do not need anointing? But Joaḥaz because of his brother Joiakim who was two years his elder. But did not Josiah hide it<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">The anointing oil. Therefore none of Josia’s sons could be anointed with the anointing oil.</i>? That means that they anointed with balsamum. One anoints kings only from a horn. Saul and Jehu were anointed from a can because their kingdom was temporary; David and Solomon were anointed from a horn because their kingdom was permanent. One does not anoint priests as kings<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">Text missing in B but implied by R. Ḥiyya bar Ada.</i>. Rebbi Jehudah Antordiya said, because<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 49:10" href="/Genesis.49.10"><i>Gen</i>. 49:10</a>.</i> <i>the scepter shall not be removed from Jehudah</i>. Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Ada said, because of<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 17:20" href="/Deuteronomy.17.20"><i>Deut</i>. 17:20</a>.</i> <i>he shall have many days of his kingdom, he and his sons in the midst of Israel</i>. What is written after that? <i>The levitic Cohanim should not</i><sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 18:1" href="/Deuteronomy.18.1"><i>Deut</i>. 18:1</a>.</i>.
Rebbi Joḥanan said, Joḥanan is Joaḥaz. But is it not written: <i>The first born Joḥanan</i><sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 3:15" href="/I_Chronicles.3.15"><i>1Chr</i>. 3:15</a>.</i>, the first in kingdom. Rebbi Joḥanan said, Shallum is Sedekiah. But is it not written,<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 3:15" href="/I_Chronicles.3.15"><i>1Chr</i>. 3:15</a>.</i> <i>the third Sedekiah, the fourth Shallum</i>? <i>Sedekiah</i>, the third in birth, the fourth in kingdom. <i>Sedekiah</i>, because he accepted the judgment on himself, <i>Shallum</i>, because in his days the dynasty of David was completed. <sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">In B this is a statement by R. Simeon ben Laqish, disputing R. Joḥanan’s.</i> His name was neither Shallum nor Sedekiah but Mattaniah. That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Kings 24:17" href="/II_Kings.24.17"><i>2K.</i> 24:17</a>.</i>: <i>The king of Babylon made his uncle Mattaniah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">B’s reading מתתיה probably is a scribal error, not a different reading in the verse.</i> <i>king in his stead and changed his name into Sedekiah</i>.
Rebbi Joḥanan said, the Ark was made with a cubit of six hand-breadths. Who stated “a cubit of six hand-breadths“? This is Rebbi Meןr’s. [As we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Kelim 17:10" href="/Mishnah_Kelim.17.10">Mishnah <i>Kelim</i>17:10</a>.</i>: “Rebbi Meןr says, all cubits were of buildings; Rebbi Jehudah says, the cubit of buildings six, of vessels five.”] According to Rebbi Meןr who says that the Ark was made with a cubit of six hand-breadths, the length  of the Ark was fifteen cubits, as it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 25:10" href="/Exodus.25.10"><i>Ex.</i> 25:10</a>.</i>: <i>Its length two cubits and a half</i>. Each cubit was six and half a cubit three. Four tablets were in it, two whole ones and two broken ones, as it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 10:2" href="/Deuteronomy.10.2"><i>Deut</i>. 10:2</a>.</i>: <i>Which you broke and put into the Ark</i>. Each of the tablets was six hand-breadths in length and three in width. Put the widths of the tablets in the length of the Ark, there were three hand-breadths left. Apply them to the cylinder<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">The Torah scroll.</i>. [On each side half a hand-breadth to have a handle, and two hand-breadths as place to put there the Torah scroll.]<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from B, to be deleted.</i> The width of the Ark was nine hand-breadths, as it is written: <i>A cubit and half a cubit</i>. A cubit six and half a cubit three. Four tablets were in it, two whole ones and two broken ones. Each of the tablets was six hand-breadths in length and three in width. Put the lengths of the tablets in the length of the Ark, there were three hand-breadths left. On each side half a hand-breadth to have a handle, and two hand-breadths as a place to put there the Torah scroll.
Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, the Ark was made using a cubit of five hand-breadths. Who stated “a cubit of five hand-breadths”? This is Rebbi Jehudah. As we have stated there<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Kelim 17:10" href="/Mishnah_Kelim.17.10">Mishnah <i>Kelim</i>17:10</a>.</i>: “Rebbi Jehudah says, the builders’ cubit was of six hand-breadths, but that of vessels five hand-breadths.” And the Ark is a vessel. According to Rebbi Jehudah who says that the Ark was made with a cubit of five hand-breadths, the length of the Ark was twelve and one half cubits, as it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 25:10" href="/Exodus.25.10"><i>Ex.</i> 25:10</a>.</i>: <i>Its length two cubits and a half</i>. Each cubit was five and half a cubit two and one half. Four tablets were in it, two whole ones and two broken ones, as it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 10:2" href="/Deuteronomy.10.2"><i>Deut</i>. 10:2</a>.</i>: <i>Which you broke and put into the Ark</i>. Each of the tablets was six hand-breadths in length and three in width. Put the width of the tablets in the length of the Ark, there remains there half a handbreadth. One finger’s thickness for the wall on either side. The width of the Ark was seven and a half hand-breadths, as it is written, <i>Its width a cubit and half a cubit</i>. A cubit five and half a cubit two and a half. Four tablets were in it, two whole ones and two broken ones, as it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 10:2" href="/Deuteronomy.10.2"><i>Deut</i>. 10:2</a>.</i>: <i>Which you broke and put into the Ark</i>.. Each of the tablets was six hand-breadths in length and three in width. Put the lengths of the tablets in the width of the Ark, there was one and a half hand-breadths left. <sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote">This sentence is not a continuation of the preceding text but the conclusion of an additional argument about the width of the Ark, reproduced in B and <i>Soṭah</i>.</i> One finger’s thickness for the wall on either side and on each side half a hand-breadth to have a handle.
How did Beṣalel make the Ark? Rebbi Ḥanina said, he made three boxes, two of gold and one of wood. He put (the one of wood inside one of gold and) one of gold inside the one of wood, [and the one of wood inside the other one of gold] and covered it, as is written<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 25:11" href="/Exodus.25.11"><i>Ex.</i>25:11</a>. As usual, the proof is by the part of the verse not quoted: <i>You shall cover it, with pure gold inside and out you shall cover it</i>, implying separate covers.</i>: <i>You shall cover it with pure gold inside and out.</i> Why does the verse say, <i>you shall cover it</i>? To include the upper rim. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, he made one box and gilded it, as is written: <i>You shall cover it with pure gold inside and out.</i> Why does the verse say, <i>you shall cover it</i>? Rebbi Phineas said, also between the planks.
How were the tablets written? Rebbi Ḥanania ben Gamliel says, five on one tablet each<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">This minority opinion is everywhere accepted in depictions of the tablets.</i>. But the rabbis say, ten on each tablet, as it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 4:13" href="/Deuteronomy.4.13"><i>Deut</i>. 4:13</a>.</i>: <i>He informed you of His covenant which He had commanded you to do, the ten words</i>, ten on each tablet. Rebbi Simeon ben Yoḥai<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">The name tradition here is very varied.</i> said, twenty on each tablet, as it is written: <i>He informed you of His covenant which He had commanded you to do, the ten words</i>, twenty on each tablet<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">Ten on the top, ten on the bottom.</i>. Rebbi Simai says, forty on each tablet, as it is written, <i>on each side they were written</i><sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 32:15" href="/Exodus.32.15"><i>Ex.</i> 32:15</a>.</i>, a square<sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote">Greek τετράγωνον. He holds that the tablets were cubes, top and bottom empty and identical writing on each of the faces.</i>. Ḥananiah, the son of Rebbi Joshua’s brother, says: Between every two commandments, the details and the letters [of the Torah] were written. <i>Filled with tarsis</i><sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Song of Songs 5:14" href="/Song_of_Songs.5.14"><i>Cant</i>. 5:14</a>. <i>His hands are golden cylinders, inlaid with tarsis,</i> the cylinders being Torah scrolls (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Shir HaShirim Rabbah 5:12" href="/Shir_HaShirim_Rabbah.5.12"><i>Cant. rabba</i>5:12</a>). The Palestinian Targum to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 28:20" href="/Exodus.28.20"><i>Ex.</i> 28:20</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 39:13" href="/Exodus.39.13">39:13</a> translates <i>taršiš</i> by כְּרוֹם יַמָּא רַבָּא ”the color of the Great Sea.“ One may assume that the scribe of the Yerushalmi did not understand the Greek χρω̅μα “color” and shortened it to .כְּ. The Targum to Cant. translates <i>taršiš</i> by the Syriac/Pahlevi word פֵּירוֹזַג (Farsi פירוזה) “turquoise”. The sentence is missing in the Genizah text and in B.</i>, like the Great Sea. When Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish had occasion to discuss this verse, he said, Ḥananiah, the son of Rebbi Joshua’s brother, did teach us correctly. Just as in the sea there are small waves between a large wave and the next, so between any two commandments there are the details and the letters of the Torah.
Rebbi Tanḥuma said, I asked before Rebbi Phineas: It is acceptable following Rebbi Jehudah<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">The verse quoted next which implies that the Torah scroll was not in the Ark.</i>, it is not acceptable following Rebbi Meןr. What is the reason of Rebbi Jehudah? <i>To take this Torah scroll and put it next to the side of the Ark of the Eternal’s covenant</i><sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 31:26" href="/Deuteronomy.31.26"><i>Deut</i>. 31:26</a>.</i>, etc In the opinion of Rebbi Jehudah, who said, where the Torah scroll was put? They made for it a kind of case<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">Greek γλωσσοκομε̅ι̅ον, τό.</i> outside and the Torah scroll was put into it. What is the reason of Rebbi Meןr? <i>You should put the cover on top of the Ark</i><sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 25:21" href="/Exodus.25.21"><i>Ex.</i> 25:21</a>.</i>. In the opinion of Rebbi Meןr who says that there is no earlier and later in the Torah, i<i>n the Ark you shall put the testimony that I shall give to you</i><sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 25:16" href="/Exodus.25.16"><i>Ex.</i> 25:16</a>.</i>, and after that, <i>you should put the cover on top of the Ark.</i> Rebbi Phineas in the name of Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish: <sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">Text of B: The Torah which He gave to Moses was white fire engraved in black fire; it is of fire quarried from fire, born from fire, given into the right hand of the Holy One, praise to Him, at it is said, <i>From His right hand, the fiery law to them.</i></i> The Torah which the Holy One, Praise to Him, gave to Moses, was white fire engraved in black fire. It was fire mixed with fire; hewn from fire, given from fire: That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 33:2" href="/Deuteronomy.33.2"><i>Deut</i>33:2</a>.</i>: <i>From His right hand, the fiery law to them.</i>

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Where were these prostrations? Four in the North, four in the South, three in the East, and two in the West, corresponding to the thirteen gates.<br>The Southern gates close to the West<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">The gates of the Temple courtyard were not symmetrical in the wall but more to the West; they are enumerated from West to East.</i>: the Upper Gate, the Fuel Gate, the Firstborns’ Gate, the Water gate. And why was it called Water Gate? For there they bring in the phial of water for the water libation on Tabernacles. Rebbi Eliezer ben Jacob said, the water will drizzle in the future from under the threshold<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">As predicted in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 47:1-5" href="/Ezekiel.47.1-5"><i>Ez</i>. 47:1–5</a>.</i><br>Opposite them<sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote">Continued enumeration of the 13 gates of the Temple compound.</i> in the North, close to the West, the Jechoniah<sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">He is called Jehoiachin in <i>Kings</i> and <i>Chronicles</i>, Koniahu in <i>Jeremiah,</i> Jechoniah in <i>Esther.</i></i> gate, the Sacrifice gate, the Women’s gate, the Song’s gate. And why was it called the Jechoniah gate? For through it Jechoniah left in his deportation<sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Middot</i>35b.</i>. In the East the Nikanor gate<sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <i>Yoma</i>3:8, Notes 317 ff.</i>, which had two small entrances<sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote">Where the people charged with opening the large doors to the public could enter with a key.</i>, one to the right and one to the left. And two in the West which had no names.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> The Mishnah is Abba Yose ben Ḥanin’s, since Abba Yose ben Ḥanin said, corresponding to the thirteen gates. But according to the Rabbis there were seven gates<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">As described in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Middot 1:4" href="/Mishnah_Middot.1.4">Mishnah <i>Middot</i>1:4</a>.</i>. In the Rabbis’ opinion, where were the thirteen prostrations? As we have stated there<sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Middot 2:3" href="/Mishnah_Middot.2.3">Mishnah <i>Middot</i>2:3</a>.</i>, “There were thirteen breaches, were the Greek kings breached it; they came back and closed them and decided correspondingly thirteen prostrations.”
It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Zechariah 14:8" href="/Zechariah.14.8"><i>Sach</i>. 14:8</a>.</i>, <i>on that day, fresh water will flow out from Jerusalem</i>, etc. It was stated: From the Holiest of Holies to the gobelins like the feelers of <i>silai</i> and <i>bilai</i><sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote">These seem to be tiny insects, not further identified.</i>. From the gobelins to the golden altar like the horns of locusts. From the golden altar to the courtyards like a shut-thread, from the courtyards to the threshold of the Temple like woof-thread, from there onwards like the pouring from a jug: <i>behold, water drizzled from the right hand side</i><sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 47:2" href="/Ezekiel.47.2"><i>Ez</i>. 47:2</a>. (<i>Yoma</i>77b–78a).</i>.
