It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 47:3-5" href="/Ezekiel.47.3-5"><i>Ez</i>. 47:3–5</a>. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sukkah (Lieberman) 3:3-7" href="/Tosefta_Sukkah_(Lieberman).3.3-7">Tosephta <i>Sukkah</i>3:3–7</a>.</i>, <i>when the man left towards the East, with a measuring rod in his hand, he measured a thousand cubits and made me cross the water, ankle water</i>. Up to his ankles. <i>Then he measured another thousand cubits and made me cross the water, knee water.</i> Up to his knees. <i>Then he measured another thousand cubits and made me cross the water, hip water.</i> Up to his hips. From there on, <i>then he measured another thousand, a river which cannot be crossed.</i> Even a large Liburnian<sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">Latin <i>liburna</i>(<i>sc. navis</i>), the standard fast commercial sail ship.</i> could not cross it. What is the reason? <i>No mighty ship may cross it</i><sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 33:21" href="/Isaiah.33.21"><i>Is.</i>33:21</a>.</i>; why? <i>The water was high, swimming water</i><sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 47:5" href="/Ezekiel.47.5"><i>Ez</i>. 47:5</a>. The word has to be explained since in common usage שיט, not שחה, was used for “to swim”.</i>. What is “swimming water”? Where one swims. Rebbi Ḥuna said, in our place one calls the swimmer <i>seḥuna</i>. <i>He moves his hands in himself, as a swimmer would move to swim</i><sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 25:11" href="/Isaiah.25.11"><i>Is.</i> 25:11</a>.</i>. What means “to swim”? Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, in unruly water<sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote">Explanation of the verse; the movements referred to are those of a desperate person.</i>. It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Zechariah 13:1" href="/Zechariah.13.1"><i>Sach</i>. 13:1</a>. It is presumed that the prophesies of Ezechiel and Sachariah refer to the same matter and one may be used to explain to other.</i>: <i>On this day, a water-source will be opened for the House of David and the dwellers in Jerusalem, for purification and impurity.</i> Rebbi Samuel bar Naḥman in the name of Rebbi Jonathan: From the House of David<sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote">The Temple.</i> to the dwellers in Jerusalem it is qualified for impurity and purification<sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote">“Purification” here means water with ashes of the Red Cow, used to purify from the impurity of the dead, which in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 19:9" href="/Numbers.19.9"><i>Num</i>. 19:9</a> is called “purification”.</i>. Farther away it is mixed water, qualified for impurity but disqualified for purification<sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote">Only spring water is qualified as “purification,” <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 19:17" href="/Numbers.19.17"><i>Num</i>. 19:17</a>. All other impurities are removed by immersion in a <i>miqweh</i>, which may contain any kind of water, including rain water.</i>. Rebbi Eleazar said, from the House of David to the dwellers in Jerusalem it is qualified for impurity and purification. Farther away it is water running down<sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">Greek καταφερής, -ές <i>adj</i>. “inclines downwards”, used in the sense of “rapidly flowing water”.</i>, disqualified for impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote">Since a <i>miqweh</i> is a “collection” of water, it cannot be a waterfall (or any shower). The same holds for rapidly flowing water; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Tahorot 8:9" href="/Mishnah_Tahorot.8.9">Mishnah <i>Ṭahorot</i>8:9</a>.</i> and purification.
It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 47:8" href="/Ezekiel.47.8"><i>Ez</i>. 47:8</a>.</i>: <i>He said to me, these waters flow out to the Eastern district</i>, this is Lake Samchonitis<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote">Lake Huleh.</i>, <i>and descends to the lowlands</i>, this is Lake Tiberias, <i>and comes to the sea,</i> this is the Salt Sea<sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote">The Dead Sea.</i>, <i>the sea of outgoing water</i>, this is the Great Sea<sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote">The Mediterranean.</i>. And why is it called <i>the sea of outgoing water</i>? For the two times it came out, [once in the generation of Enosh, and once in the generation of the Dispersal.]<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from B; its statement understood by all texts..</i> Rebbi Eleazar in the name of Rebbi Ḥanina: The first time it went out up to Calabria, the second time it went to the Capes of Barbary<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote">He holds that the Eastern Mediterranean was part of the original creation; it was connected to the Okeanos through the Straights of Gibraltar by later catastrophes. Cf. <i>Gen</i>. <i>rabba</i>23(11).</i>. Rebbi Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Ḥanina: The first time it went out to the Capes of Barbary, the second time it came to Acco and Jaffa<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">He holds that the Mediterranean was not part of the original creation; it was formed by waters of the Okeanos through the Straights of Gibraltar by later catastrophes.</i>. <i>Up to here you shall come but no more</i><sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Job 38:11" href="/Job.38.11"><i>Job</i>38:11</a>.</i>; up to Acco you shall come but not add. <i>And there you stop the might of your waves</i><sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Job 38:11" href="/Job.38.11"><i>Job</i>38:11</a>.</i>, at Jaffa<sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote">Reading וּפֹא as יפו. <i>Yalqut Šim`ony</i>#924.</i> you stop the might of your waves. One understands the Great Sea and the Salt Sea, to make them sweet. Lake Tiberias and Lake Samchonitis<sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">Since it is written that the river flowing out from the Temple brings healing to the water, what healing can it bring to sweet water lakes?</i>? To increase their fish; <i>their fish shall be in kinds</i><sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 47:10" href="/Ezekiel.47.10"><i>Ez</i>. 47:10</a>.</i>; in great number shall be the kinds of their fish. It was stated: Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel said, it happened that I went to Sidon and they brought before me more than 300 kinds of fish on one tray.
<i>The waters will be healed</i><sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 47:8" href="/Ezekiel.47.8"><i>Ez</i>. 47:8</a>.</i>. <i>Its ponds and its puddles will not be healed, they will be given for salt</i><sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 47:10" href="/Ezekiel.47.10"><i>Ez</i>. 47:10</a>.</i>. It is written, <i>the waters will be healed,</i> and you are saying, <i>they will not be healed?</i> There is a place called “will not be healed.”
It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 47:11" href="/Ezekiel.47.11"><i>Ez</i>. 47:11</a>. <i>Taaniot</i>1:2 (<b>ת</b>).</i>, <i>on the banks of the river on both sides all kinds of fruit tree will grow; its leaf shall not wilt, and its fruit not stop; in its months it shall produce first fruits.</i> It was stated: Rebbi Jehudah said, in the present world grain grows in six months and trees produce every twelve months, but in the future grain will grow in a month and trees will produce in two months. Rebbi Yose said, in the present world grain grows in six months and trees produce every twelve months, but in the future grain will grow in fifteen days and trees will produce in a month, for so we find that grain grew in the days of Joel in fifteen days, and the ‘<i>Omer</i> was brought from it. What is the reason? <i>The people of Zion shall enjoy and be happy in the Eternal, your God, for He in truth gave you strong rain, early rain and late rain in the first {month}</i><sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 47:12" href="/Ezekiel.47.12"><i>Ez</i>. 47:12</a></i>. How does Rebbi Yose satisfy <i>in its months it shall produce first fruits</i>? Every month it shall produce first fruits<sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Joel 2:23" href="/Joel.2.23"><i>Joel</i>2:23</a>.</i>. <i>And its leaf as medicine</i><sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 47:11" href="/Ezekiel.47.11"><i>Ez</i>. 47:11</a>. <i>Taaniot</i>1:2 (<b>ת</b>).</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan said, its healing is that one looks at it and food is turned into medicine. Rav and Samuel, one says, to open the upper mouth<sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote">Toothaches and any disease of the mouth. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 95a" href="/Menachot.95a"><i>Menaḥot</i>95a</a>.</i>, but the other one says, to open the lower mouth<sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote">Constipation.</i>. Rebbi Ḥanina and Rebbi Joshua ben Levi, one says, to open the mouth of sterile women<sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote">The womb.</i>, but the other one says, to open the mouth of the dumb.
<sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote">A shortened version of a text in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Vayikra Rabbah 19:6" href="/Vayikra_Rabbah.19.6"><i>Lev. rabba</i>19(6</a>). For the first part, cf. also <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bereishit Rabbah 94" href="/Bereishit_Rabbah.94"><i>Gen. rabba</i>94</a>, end. The text cannot be considered as historical reconstruction; it is part of an attempt to project the rabbinic establishment of the time as dominating factor inherited from Moses, prophets, and kings.</i> You are finding that when Nebuchadnezzar campaigned here, he came and sat in Daphne of Antiochia. The Great Synhedrion went to him and said to him, did the time come that this House be destroyed? He said to them, give me the one which I made king over you and I will depart. They came and said to Jehoiachin, the king of Judea, Nebuchadnezzar wants you. <sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote">This is better read as a story about the destruction of the Temple, Babli <i>Ta`anit</i>29a, where the two Amoraic statements are combined into one (and the language of B is adjusted to fit the language there.)</i> When he heard this from them, he took the keys of the Temple and climbed to the roof of the Temple. He said before Him: Master of the world! In the past we were trustworthy for You and Your keys were handed to us. Now that we are not trustworthy for You, Your keys are handed to You. Two Amoraim, One said, he threw them upwards and they never returned. The other said, He saw that something like a hand came and took them from him. When all the freeholders of Jehudah heard this, they climbed to the tops of their roofs, fell down, and died. That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">99</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 22:1" href="/Isaiah.22.1"><i>Is.</i>22:1</a>.</i>, <i>Saying about the valley of vision: Why are you doing this, that you climbed on all roofs, the noisy, full, humming city</i>.

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> There were thirteen tables in the Temple<sup class="footnote-marker">100</sup><i class="footnote">For the sacred service. There were more tables in the back part of the Temple domain, between the walls of the Temple and the walls of the enclosure, where the Cohanim had to eat their part of the most holy sacrifices. Thirteen, as the number of the Divine attributes of mercy, is a most lucky number in religious matters.</i>. Eight marble ones in the slaughterhouse on which one was soaking the intestines<sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote">Which must be washed before being sacrifices, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 1:9" href="/Leviticus.1.9"><i>Lev.</i> 1:9</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 1:13" href="/Leviticus.1.13">13</a>.</i>. Two West of the ramp, one of marble and one of silver. On the marble one they put the limbs, on the silver one the vessels of service<sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote">Where the flour and wine sacrifices were deposited before being brought up to the altar.</i>. And two in the vestibule<sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote">The small hall in front of the main Temple hall in the Temples of Solomon and Herod, in contrast to the Tabernacle.</i> inside, near the entrance to the Temple Hall, one of marble and one of gold. On the marble one they put the shew-bread when it was brought in, and on the golden one when it was brought out, for one increases in holiness and does not decrease<sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup><i class="footnote">The bread was brought in on Friday, but was exchanged for the old bread in the main Temple hall only on the Sabbath. The removed bread was deposited in the vestibule until it could be distributed to the Cohanim at the end of the <i>musaf</i> service. Since it was laying during the week on the golden table inside, it could not be deposited on a table of lesser value. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 99b" href="/Menachot.99b">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>99b</a>.</i>. And a golden one inside on which the shew-bread was permanently<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 25:30" href="/Exodus.25.30"><i>Ex.</i> 25:30</a>.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It was stated, “on the silver one”<sup class="footnote-marker">106</sup><i class="footnote">It is not perfectly clear to what this <i>baraita</i> refers. In the Babli version, there were no marble tables, only silver ones. In the Yerushalmi version, it either can mean that in the vestibule there was a silver table instead of the marble one mentioned in the Mishnah, or that the sentence is not from a <i>baraita</i>, but a quote from the Mishnah, implying that according to R. Joḥanan there was no silver table at all in the Temple, and that wine and flour offerings also had to be kept cool.</i>. Rebbi Yose in the name of Rebbi Samuel bar Rav Isaac; Rebbi Ḥananiah brought it in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: There was none of silver because it heats<sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote">Assuming one speaks about the silver table mentioned in the Mishnah, one has to be careful to keep the flour offering cool lest it become leavened and forbidden in the Temple. If it is indicated that the table in the vestibule was of silver, the question is whether putting the new shew-bread on a warm table would spoil it. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tamid 31b" href="/Tamid.31b"><i>Tamid</i>31b</a>.</i>. But did we not state<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 21a" href="/Yoma.21a">Babli <i>Yoma</i>21a</a>, in the name of R. Joshua ben Levi.</i>, this is one of the wonders which happened in the Temple, that just as they were putting it down hot, so they were removing it hot, [as it is written]<sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from B, missing in <b>ג</b> and deleted by the scribe himself in the Leiden ms.</i>, <i>to put hot bread as on the day it was removed</i><sup class="footnote-marker">110</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 21:7" href="/I_Samuel.21.7"><i>1S</i>. 21:7</a>. The implication is that a warm silver table would be more appropriate for the shew bread than a cold marble one.</i>. Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said, one does not mention wonders<sup class="footnote-marker">111</sup><i class="footnote">One may not act trusting that a wonder will occur in one’s behalf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 60a" href="/Berakhot.60a">Babli <i>Berakhot</i>60a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 121b" href="/Yevamot.121b"><i>Yebamot</i>121b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Chullin 43a" href="/Chullin.43a"><i>Ḥulin</i>43a</a>.</i>. They asked before Rebbi Ila: If they did not have bread, may they leave it for the coming week<sup class="footnote-marker">112</sup><i class="footnote">Since the shew-bread has to be exchanged every Sabbath (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 24:8" href="/Leviticus.24.8"><i>Lev.</i>24:8</a>), if there was no replacement available is it better to leave the table empty or leave the old bread in its place.</i>? He said to them, it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">113</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 25:30" href="/Exodus.25.30"><i>Ex.</i> 25:30</a>.</i>: <i>you shall put on the table the shew-bread before Me permanently.</i> The shew-bread, even disqualified<sup class="footnote-marker">114</sup><i class="footnote">Since the shew-bread removed from the sanctuary had to be eaten by the Cohanim as most holy sacrifice (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 24:9" href="/Leviticus.24.9"><i>Lev.</i>24:9</a>), it must be eaten on the day it becomes available and will be disqualified the next morning, to be burned. But this rule does not apply to bread never removed from the Sanctuary.</i>.
Solomon made ten tables: <i>Solomon made ten tables and deposited them in the Temple Hall, five to the right and five to the left</i><sup class="footnote-marker">115</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 4:8" href="/II_Chronicles.4.8"><i>2Chr.</i> 4:8</a>.</i>. If you would say, five to the North and five to the South, but the table is only qualified in the North, as it is said, <i>and the table put on the North side</i><sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 26:35" href="/Exodus.26.35"><i>Ex.</i> 26:35</a>.</i>. Why does the verse say, <i>five to the right and five to the left</i>? Five to the right of Moses’s table, and five to its left. Nevertheless, only Moses’s alone was used, as it is said<sup class="footnote-marker">117</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 7:49" href="/I_Kings.7.49"><i>1K.</i> 7:49</a>.</i>, <i>the table on which is the shew-bread.</i> Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Jehudah says, all of them were used, for it is said<sup class="footnote-marker">118</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 4:19" href="/II_Chronicles.4.19"><i>2Chr.</i> 4:19</a>.</i>, <i>the tables on which the shew-bread is</i>. It was stated: They were put East and West, the words of Rebbi. Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon says, they were put North and South. He who says East and West is understandable; all of them are proper for Service<sup class="footnote-marker">119</sup><i class="footnote">As prescribed in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 40:22" href="/Exodus.40.22">Ex. 40:22</a>,, the table at the North side of the Tabernacle, and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 40:24" href="/Exodus.40.24"><i>Ex.</i> 40:24</a>, the candelabrum at the South side, standing East-West, opposite the table.</i>. He who says, North and South, would then not the table be in the South and the candelabrum in the North? But was it not stated, the table was in the middle of the Temple, more to the inside, about two cubits away from the wall to the North, and opposite it the candelabrum in the South<sup class="footnote-marker">120</sup><i class="footnote">If they are all in one line, at the North side of the Temple, the long side oriented East-West, all pentateuchal requirements are satisfied. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 99a" href="/Menachot.99a">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i> 99a</a>.</i>. The golden altar was in the middle of the Temple, dividing the Temple, inside, a little bit drawn to the North<sup class="footnote-marker">121</sup><i class="footnote">While the center of the golden altar exactly determines the middle of the Temple hall for distances measured East-West, i. e., between the entrance and the gobelins shielding the Holiest of Holies, it does not exactly determine the middle of the center of the distance of North to South walls.</i>. All were put inside of a third of the Temple<sup class="footnote-marker">122</sup><i class="footnote">The first third of the distance between entrance and the Holiest of Holies was empty.</i>.
Solomon made ten candelabra, [as it is said]<sup class="footnote-marker">123</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s insert following B.</i>, <i>he made the ten candelabra according to its rules</i><sup class="footnote-marker">124</sup><i class="footnote"><i>2 Chr</i>. 4:7. In the other two sources correctly “their rules”, and they add the end of the verse, to which the next argument refers: <i>and put them in the Temple Hall, five to the right and five to the left.</i> Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 98b-99a" href="/Menachot.98b-99a">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>98b–99a</a>.</i>. If you would say, five to the North and five to the South, but the candelabrum is only qualified in the South, as it is said, <i>and the candelabrum opposite the table on the South side</i><sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 26:35" href="/Exodus.26.35"><i>Ex.</i> 26:35</a>.</i>. Why does the verse say, <i>five to the right and five to the left</i>? Five to the right of Moses’s candelabrum, and five to its left. Nevertheless, only Moses’s alone was kindled, as it is said<sup class="footnote-marker">125</sup><i class="footnote"><i>2 Chr.</i>13:11, showing actual practice.\</i>, <i>and the golden candelabrum and its lights to kindle evening by evening.</i> Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Jehudah says, all of them were kindled, for it is said<sup class="footnote-marker">126</sup><i class="footnote"><i>2 Chr</i>. 4:20–21.</i>, <i>the candelabra and their lights, to kindle them regularly in the Temple Hall, closed gold</i><sup class="footnote-marker">127</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yoma 4:4:5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yoma.4.4.5"><i>Yoma</i>4:4, Note 101</a>.</i>, <i>and the flower</i><sup class="footnote-marker">128</sup><i class="footnote">According to Rashi, the ornament of the candelabrum mentioned in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 8:4" href="/Numbers.8.4"><i>Num</i>. 8:4</a> but not in the original instructions, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 25:31-40" href="/Exodus.25.31-40"><i>Ex.</i> 25:31–40</a>.</i>, <i>and the lights, and the pincers of gold, this uses up the gold.</i> These used up Solomon’s gold. Rav Jehudah in the name of Assi<sup class="footnote-marker">129</sup><i class="footnote">In B a Tannaitic text, a statement of R. Jehudah in the name of Issy.</i>: Solomon took 1’000 talents of silver, put them repeatedly into the (fire) [smelting furnace]<sup class="footnote-marker">130</sup><i class="footnote">The scribe’s text (in parentheses) is confirmed by the Genizah text; the corrector’s [in brackets] is from B.</i> until they were reduced to one, to fulfill what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">131</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 37:24" href="/Exodus.37.24"><i>Ex.</i> 37:24</a>.</i>, <i>from one talent of pure gold he made it</i>. It was stated, Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Jehudah said, <sup class="footnote-marker">132</sup><i class="footnote">The following is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yoma 4:4:7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yoma.4.4.7"><i>Yoma</i>4:4, Notes 107–108</a>.</i> it happened that the golden candelabrum which Moses made in the desert was in excess of one gold denar, and they returned it to the fire eighty times and it did not lose anything<sup class="footnote-marker">133</sup><i class="footnote">This seems to contradict the preceding story of Solomon’s refining smelter.</i>. This is correct. Before it is refined it loses a lot, once it is refined it will not miss anything.

Halakhah 4

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Thirteen horns<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">The “horns” were chests for the money given to the Temple for various reasons, as detailed in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 6:4:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.6.4.1">Mishnah 7</a>. A person putting money into one of the chests could not put his hand into it, he had to let the coins drop in from the top.</i> were in the Temple, and it was written on them: New <i>sheqalim</i>, and old <i>sheqalim</i>, nests<sup class="footnote-marker">134</sup><i class="footnote">Obligatory purification or reparation offerings, as prescribed in <i>Lev.</i> In all cases, two birds are required, one as purification and one as elevation offering, following different rules.</i>, young birds for elevation sacrifices<sup class="footnote-marker">135</sup><i class="footnote">Voluntary offerings which may be for a single bird.</i>, wood<sup class="footnote-marker">136</sup><i class="footnote">A person vowing firewood for the Temple does not bring wood but the money for it.</i>, and incense, gold for the cover<sup class="footnote-marker">137</sup><i class="footnote">To cover the Holiest of Holies in the absence of the Ark; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 4:2:1-6" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.4.2.1-6">Mishnah 4:4</a>.</i>, and six for voluntary gifts<sup class="footnote-marker">138</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in the Halakhah and in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Shekalim (Lieberman) 3:7" href="/Tosefta_Shekalim_(Lieberman).3.7">Tosephta 3:7</a>.</i>. New <i>sheqalim</i> for the current year, and old ones, one who did not bring the past year, gives it for the next one<sup class="footnote-marker">139</sup><i class="footnote">New <i>sheqalim</i> are given for current use; <i>sheqalim</i> for past years are treated directly as remainders from that year (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 4:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.4.2.1">Mishnah 4:3</a>).</i>.<br>“Nests” are turtle doves and “young birds as elevation offerings” are pigeons, all for elevation offerings, the words of Rebbi Jehudah<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">It was explained in the preceding Halakhah that R. Jehudah cannot accept the explanation of Mishnah 7 given in Note 134, but must require that a person offering two birds to be able to partake in <i>sancta</i>, the woman after childbirth (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 12:8" href="/Leviticus.12.8"><i>Lev.</i> 12:8</a>), the poor person healed from skin disease (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 14:22" href="/Leviticus.14.22"><i>Lev.</i> 14:22</a>), the male healed from gonorrhea (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 15:14" href="/Leviticus.15.14"><i>Lev.</i> 15:14</a>) and the female from flux (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 15:29" href="/Leviticus.15.29"><i>Lev.</i> 15:29</a>), personally deliver the birds to the Cohen who thereby is assured that the person is alive. As a consequence, for him the money deposited for “nests” is for elevation sacrifices; the distinction from “young birds for elevation offerings” only is in the amount of money required and the kind of birds bought. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 6:4:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.6.4.1">Mishnah 7</a> was explained following the Sages in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 6:4:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.6.4.1">Mishnah 8</a>.</i>. But the Sages say, of “nests” one is a purification offering and one an elevation offering; “young birds as elevation offerings” are all elevation offerings. If one says, “I am obligated for wood logs”, he may not give less than for two logs; “incense”, he may not give less than for a fistful; “gold”, he may not give less than for a gold denar<sup class="footnote-marker">148</sup><i class="footnote">25 silver denars, or their equivalent in small change.</i>. “Six for voluntary gifts.” What did they do with this? One buys with it elevation offerings<sup class="footnote-marker">149</sup><i class="footnote">As with any money delivered to the gift account.</i>; the flesh is for the Eternal and the skins are for the Cohanim. This explanation did Jehoyada the High Priest explain: <i>It is a reparation offering, repairing, a reparation offering for the Eternal</i><sup class="footnote-marker">150</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 5:19" href="/Leviticus.5.19"><i>Lev.</i> 5:19</a>.</i>; this is the principle: Elevation offerings should be bought from anything coming<sup class="footnote-marker">151</sup><i class="footnote">It is obvious that money given to the Temple for purification or reparation offerings must be used for the kind of offering specified. Money “coming from” these kinds of offerings are excess monies, not used for the obligatory offerings. Since obligatory offerings cannot be brought voluntarily, nor can monies dedicated to the Temple be returned, the excess has to be deposited in the gift account and used for elevation offerings.</i> because of sin or reparation; the flesh is for the Eternal and the skins are for the Cohanim. It turns out that both parts of the verse are fulfilled, a reparation offering for the Eternal and reparation for the Cohanim. And it says, money for reparation offerings and money for purification offerings are not to be brought to the Eternal’s House, it shall be for the Cohanim<sup class="footnote-marker">152</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Kings 12:17" href="/II_Kings.12.17"><i>2K.</i> 12:17</a>. The money is not for the Cohanim but the Cohanim receive the skins of the animals bought with the excess monies.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">140</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 55a" href="/Yoma.55a">Babli <i>Yoma</i>55a</a>. This paragraph is two texts in one. The Yerushalmi text is that of the scribe of the Leiden manuscript; the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 55b" href="/Yoma.55b">Babli text (<i>Yoma</i>55b</a>) is reproduced in Babylonian Aramaic in B and the corrector’s text given in brackets here.</i>: “Rebbi Jehudah said, there was no horn for nests in Jerusalem because of mix-up.<sup class="footnote-marker">141</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Shekalim (Lieberman) 3:3" href="/Tosefta_Shekalim_(Lieberman).3.3">Tosephta 3:3</a>.</i>” Maybe one of them would die and it turn out that moneys of dying purification sacrifices were mixed up in them<sup class="footnote-marker">142</sup><i class="footnote">This is the Yerushalmi’s explanation for R. Jehudah’s statement, as noted in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 55b" href="/Yoma.55b"><i>Yoma</i>55b</a>. An animal dedicated as a purification sacrifice whose owner died between dedication and sacrifice cannot be used for anything, but it has to be let to die (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Temurah 4:1" href="/Mishnah_Temurah.4.1">Mishnah <i>Temurah</i>4:1</a>). Moneys dedicated for a purification sacrifice under the same circumstances have to be destroyed; in Israel this means to be thrown into the Dead Sea. R. Jehudah holds that such money mixed up with other moneys makes everything unusable and worthless.</i>. [But did we not state] (It was stated): A woman who said, I have to bring a nest, brings the money for the nest and puts it in the horn, and eats from <i>sancta</i> without worry. And the Cohen does not worry that maybe moneys of dying purification sacrifices are mixed up in them<sup class="footnote-marker">143</sup><i class="footnote">The woman is recovering from childbirth or from flux; she may not eat <i>sancta</i> unless a sundown was preceded by her sacrifice. (Therefore <b>ג</b> reads “gets up in the morning and eats.”) The statement implies that the horn for nests was emptied several times every hour and any money deposited there immediately used for the required sacrifice. This makes R. Jehudah’s objection moot; practice follows the Mishnah.<br>In Babylonia, the Galilean explanation was rejected (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 55b" href="/Yoma.55b"><i>Yoma</i>55b</a>); therefore, the <i>baraita</i> is read as a question, and an objection to R. Jehudah.<br><a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 32a" href="/Eruvin.32a">Babli <i>Eruvin</i>32a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 27a" href="/Menachot.27a"><i>Menaḥot</i>27a</a>.</i>. [For what we are saying is about purification sacrifices whose owner certainly died<sup class="footnote-marker">144</sup><i class="footnote">Everybody agrees that the requirement to destroy the money is rabbinical, restricted to cases of certainty. R. Jehudah’s statement is rejected as a matter of principle.</i>. We could say, let us choose two <i>zuz</i> and throw them into the River<sup class="footnote-marker">145</sup><i class="footnote">The River is the Euphrates, which here appears as Babylonian equivalent of the Dead Sea. The argument is that even in case it is known that a woman died after paying her fee into the horn and the next sacrifices of nests, could not the amount of the Temple’s charge for the nest be taken from the horn, designated as this woman’s contribution, and eliminated?</i>, then the remainder should be permitted, but do we not say in general that Rebbi Jehudah does not accept retroactive choices<sup class="footnote-marker">146</sup><i class="footnote">It is generally agreed that a later choice can retroactively eliminate rabbinic prohibitions but not biblical ones. R. Jehudah represents a minority opinion which rejects retroactivity in all cases. Therefore the remedy proposed according to R. Jehudah cannot be applied; for the majority, whom practice follows, there is a horn for nests, but for R. Jehudah this is an impossibility.</i>?]
<sup class="footnote-marker">153</sup><i class="footnote">A copy of this text, except for the last sentence, is in <i>Shevi`it</i>9:7, Notes 95–97.</i> Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, Rebbi Abba bar Mamal asked: If he said, I am obligated [to offer] a log, does he bring one log? Rebbi Eleazar said, a Mishnah says that each one is a separate sacrifice, as we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">154</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yoma 2:4:1-4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yoma.2.4.1-4">Mishnah Yoma 2:5</a>.</i>, “two, holding in their hands two wooden logs.” This adds single logs.
<sup class="footnote-marker">155</sup><i class="footnote">The version of B and the corrector’s, derived from B, have to be understood from the parallel in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 62" href="/Zevachim.62">Babli <i>Zevaḥim</i>62a/b</a>, which, however, can better be read as supporting the readings of the scribe of the Leiden ms.</i> Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said, their width was (like an engraver’s cubit<sup class="footnote-marker">156</sup><i class="footnote">A short cubit, of five hand-breadths, based on small hands.</i>) [in an expansive cubit<sup class="footnote-marker">157</sup><i class="footnote">A long cubit, of seven hand-breadths, based on large hands. Only two dimensions are given. In the Babli more correctly the logs were hewn as rectangular solids with a base of one cubit square and small height. A similar statement is required here by the <i>baraita</i> quoted at the end.</i>], and its width (a dwarf) [an excessive] cubit. Rebbi Onias in the name of Rebbi Immi: Like scales<sup class="footnote-marker">158</sup><i class="footnote">Latin <i>trutina</i>, Greek τρυτάνη. Since it is specified later that the fire place on Moses’s altar was only one cubit square, the two logs put on the altar at the beginning of each day’s service had to be half a regular cubit’s height and lying strictly parallel, as are the scales on a balance.</i>. Rebbi Samuel bar Rav Isaac said, because the place of the fire was only one cubit square, therefore they only could be a (dwarf) [excessive] cubit. It was stated thus<sup class="footnote-marker">159</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 62a" href="/Zevachim.62a"><i>Zevaḥim</i>62a</a>. The altar was five-by-five cubits (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 27:1" href="/Exodus.27.1"><i>Ex.</i> 27:1</a>). This included the basis where most of the blood had to be spilled onto, a walkway at half height for the Cohen to sprinkle blood on the horns, the copper enclosure delineating the upper part. In the description given here, the place of the fire is given a full cubit; all the other items are half a cubit since there is one of them on each side. This is too much for the copper enclosure and too little for the walkway, but is possible if both together are taken to be 2 cubits. In these enumerations, very frequently “hand-breadth” means “not more than a hand-breadth” and “cubit” “more than a hand-breadth but not more than a cubit”.</i>: One cubit the basis, one cubit the walkway, one cubit the enclosure, and one cubit the horns, and one cubit the fire place.
“Incense”, he may not give less than for a fistful. It is said here “remembrance” and it is said there, “remembrance”<sup class="footnote-marker">160</sup><i class="footnote">“Here” means the rules of voluntary flour offerings, described in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 2" href="/Leviticus.2"><i>Lev.</i> Chapter 2</a>. “There” means either the rules of the shew bread, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 24:7" href="/Leviticus.24.7"><i>Lev.</i> 24:7</a> or that of the obligatory flour offering of the poor sinner, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 5:12" href="/Leviticus.5.12"><i>Lev.</i> 5:12</a>. In the first case, there are two rows of bread, each one with a portion of incense which at the end has to be entirely burned on the altar. In the second case, it is stressed that the entire fistful has to be burned. In both cases it can be inferred that for voluntary flour offerings, where “entire” is not mentioned, only an entire fistful is qualified.</i>. Since “remembrance” there means a full fistful, so “remembrance” here must mean a full fistful. Since “remembrance” there means two fistfuls<sup class="footnote-marker">161</sup><i class="footnote">This can apply only to the shew bread.</i>, does “remembrance” here mean two fistfuls? Rebbi La said, they inferred fistfuls only from the shew bread<sup class="footnote-marker">162</sup><i class="footnote">In B: From the poor sinner’s flour offering.</i>. Since there a deficient fistful is disqualified, also here a deficient fistful is disqualified. Rebbi Yose said, the word of Rebbi Ila implies that one who volunteers a flour offering brings it according to the High Priest’s<sup class="footnote-marker">163</sup><i class="footnote">It seems that one refers not to a High Priest, but to a large priest, whose fistful can be enormous. Since the donor does not know which Cohen will present his offering to the altar, he must prepare for the largest possible fistful.</i> fistful. Rebbi Ḥizqiah in the name of Rebbi Jeremiah: even according to the owner’s fistful.
“Gold”, he may not give less than for a gold denar. Rebbi Eleazar said, only if he mentioned minting<sup class="footnote-marker">164</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 107a" href="/Menachot.107a">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>107a</a>.</i>. But if he did not mention a coin he even may bring a hook.
“Six for voluntary gifts.” Ḥizqiah said, corresponding to the six clans<sup class="footnote-marker">165</sup><i class="footnote">During the week of service of a “watch” of Cohanim, each of the six workdays another clan would serve, whose members then had claim to all hides of elevation offerings of that day.<br>In B, the statement is ascribed to Rav, Ḥizqiah’s cousin, and fellow student of the Elder R. Hiyya, Rav’s uncle and Ḥizqiah’s father.</i>. Bar Pedaiah said, corresponding to seven animals: bull, and calf, and he-goat, ram, and lamb, and kid goat. Samuel said, corresponding to six sacrifices: the nests of the sufferer from gonorrhea, the nests of the sufferer from flux, the nests of the new mother, purification sacrifices, and reparation sacrifices, flour offerings, and the Tenth of an Ephah<sup class="footnote-marker">166</sup><i class="footnote">This list has 7 items. The corresponding list in B has only six, but the selection in unconvincing. Probably the correct list is <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Shekalim (Lieberman) 3:7" href="/Tosefta_Shekalim_(Lieberman).3.7">Tosephta 3:7</a>: The excesses of money for 1) purification sacrifices, 2) reparation sacrifices, 3) nests of sufferers from gonorrhea or flux, 4) nests of a woman after childbirth, 5) offerings of a <i>nazir</i>, 6) of a healed sufferer from skin disease.</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan said, because the gifts were many, they added many horns for it. [As it is said]<sup class="footnote-marker">167</sup><i class="footnote">This addition by the corrector, taken from B, has to be deleted, since it hides the fact that the following quote is the start of a question. The remaining additions by the corrector, while unnecessary, are not in conflict with the line of thought.</i>, <i>when they were finished they brought before the king and Jehoyada</i><sup class="footnote-marker">168</sup><i class="footnote"><i>2 Chr.</i>24:14. The problem is that the remaining part of the verse, quoted in full in <b>ג</b> nd B, notes that the excess money donated for the renovation of the Temple under King Joash was used to make silver and gold vessels for the Temple, while the corresponding verse in <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Kings 12:14" href="/II_Kings.12.14"><i>2K.</i> 12:14</a> declares the opposite.</i> etc. Rebbi Samuel ben Naḥman in the name of Rebbi Jonathan [said], two voluntary gifts<sup class="footnote-marker">169</sup><i class="footnote">The two verses refer to two separate collections.</i>. Rebbi Ismael stated, one gift. But is it not written<sup class="footnote-marker">170</sup><i class="footnote"><i>2 Chr.</i>24:8, while in <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Kings 12:10" href="/II_Kings.12.10"><i>2K.</i> 12:10</a> it is reported that the chest was deposited in the priests’ courtyard, to the right (East) of the altar.</i>, <i>the king commanded and they made a chest and put it at the outside of the gate of the Eternal’s House.</i> Rav Ḥuna said, because of those impure. Rebbi Ḥuna in the name of Rav Joseph: Because of <i>but silver cups would not be made in the Eternal’s House</i><sup class="footnote-marker">171</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Kings 12:14" href="/II_Kings.12.14"><i>2K.</i> 12:14</a>.</i>. Things similar to silver cups would not be made in the Eternal’s House<sup class="footnote-marker">172</sup><i class="footnote">Either there were two different calls for gifts to the Temple, or for the same collection period there were two chests, one inside and one outside, and vessels were made only from the money which never entered the sacred domain.</i>.

Chapter 7



Halakhah 1

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Coins which are found between the <i>sheqalim</i> and the voluntary gifts, if closer to <i>sheqalim</i> they have to be given to <i>sheqalim</i>, closer to voluntary gifts to voluntary gifts; in the middle they have to be given to voluntary gifts<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">As explained at the end of the Mishnah, in general coins found are assigned to the box closest to the place where the coins were found. Only if the coins are strictly in the middle between two boxes they are assigned to the more holy use. Since voluntary gifts are strictly for elevation offerings but <i>sheqalim</i> are used for all needs of the Temple, voluntary gifts represent the more holy use.</i>. Between wood and incense, if closer to wood they have to be given to wood, closer to incense to incense; in the middle they have to be given to incense<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Incense is an offering in itself, whereas wood is only an auxiliary to offerings on the altar; incense is more holy.</i>. Between nests and young birds for elevation sacrifices, if closer to nests they have to be given to nests, closer to young birds for elevation sacrifices to young birds for elevation sacrifices; in the middle they have to be given to young birds for elevation sacrifices<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">According to the rabbis, nests contain one bird as purification offering and one as elevation offering, whereas young birds for elevation sacrifices are all elevation sacrifices; the latter are more holy.</i>. Between profane money and Second Tithe<sup>\4</sup>, if closer to profane money they have to be given to profane money, closer to Second Tithe to Second Tithe; in the middle they have to be given to Second Tithe. This is the principle: one follows proximity; in the middle one is stringent.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “Coins which are found between the <i>sheqalim</i> and the voluntary gifts,” etc. It would only be necessary between <i>sheqalim</i> and nests<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Since <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 6:4:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.6.4.1">Mishnah 6:7</a> states that the horn for nests is next to the two for <i>sheqalim</i>, how can coins be found between <i>sheqalim</i> and gifts?</i>! They were arranged like a snail<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Greek κοχλίας, “snail with a spiral shell”. If the horns are arranged almost in a circle, the box for new <i>sheqalim</i> is next to the last box for gifts. If they would be in a straight line then the box near to “nests” is that for “old <i>sheqalim</i>”, which are never used for sacrifices and therefore the coins found halfway should be given to “nests”.</i>. Would it not be necessary that it be given to <i>sheqalim</i><sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Since “gifts” provide private sacrifices but <i>sheqalim</i> public ones, the sanctity of <i>sheqalim</i> should be greater than that of “gifts”.</i>? Some want to say, maybe they would remain with the excess of the lodge<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Which are not used for sacrifices.</i>. Some want to say, in the middle it is as if he died. <sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">This text to the end of the paragraph is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 7:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.7.2">Halakhah 2:5, Notes 81–83</a>. The origin of the text is there, since the last two sentences, about the High Priest’s flour offering, have no connection with the topic under discussion here.</i> Rebbi Yasa said, when I still was there, I heard the voice of Rav Jehudah asking Samuel, if somebody had set his <i>sheqel</i> apart and died? He told him, they shall fall to the gift account. The excess of his tenth of an ephah, Rebbi Joḥanan said, one shall bring them to the Dead Sea. Rebbi Eleazar said, it shall fall to the gift account.
And it is difficult. May purification offering be brought as elevation offering<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">If coins lie in the middle between nests and young birds for elevation sacrifices, there is a 50% chance that the money was brought by a woman for her obligatory nests. How can one justify a rabbinical rule that assigns the money to elevation sacrifices against a possibly biblical injunction against doing this?</i>? Rebbi Ḥizqiah (brother)<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">The correct reading is preserved in B, א׳ (אָמַר) “said”.</i> in the name of Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish: It is a stipulation of the Court that the excesses be brought as elevation sacrifices<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">Everybody bringing a gift to the Temple knows that these will be evaluated by Temple rules and the donor accepts these rules by giving. Therefore the money never was absolutely dedicated for purification offerings.</i>. By what is that woman atoned for<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">Since the money may have been given by a woman needing purification, if it happens that her monies were used as elevation offering, how can she ever eat <i>sancta</i>? The sentence and the next are reproduced at the end of the Chapter (7).</i>? Rebbi Isaac said, it is a stipulation of the Court that the providers of nests also provide the disqualified ones<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">The provider has to provide a few extra birds which are treated as possible purification offerings (a situation impossible for four-legged animals) but are not eaten.</i>. Would it not also be necessary between incense and wood, and frankincense, and gold for the cover<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">The Mishnah does not treat a number of other possible cases.</i>? As it is stated at the end, “one follows nearness; in the middle one is stringent.”

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Coins found near vendors of animals always are Tithe money<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">Most kosher animals sold in Jerusalem are sold to pilgrims who use their tithe money for their living expenses in Jerusalem. If not all this money is spent during their visit, the remaining coins used to be given to their hosts, to be used to buy food consumed in purity according to the rules of second Tithe. Therefore the presumption is that money in the hand of resident Jerusalemites found near venders of animals for slaughter is Second Tithe money. The finder will have to use the coins according to Tithe standards.</i>. On the Temple Mount, profane. In Jerusalem, during the remainder of the year they are profane, during the holidays everything is Second Tithe.<br>Of meat found in the Temple courtyard, limbs are elevation sacrifices and cuts purification sacrifices<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">Elevation sacrifices have to be dissected into limbs (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 1:6" href="/Leviticus.1.6"><i>Lev.</i> 1:6</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 1:12" href="/Leviticus.1.12">12</a>) before being brought to the altar, but purification sacrifices have to be eaten by the Cohanim in the holy precinct and for this purpose have to be cut into portions.</i>; in Jerusalem well-being sacrifices<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">Since usually meat in Jerusalem is from a family sacrifice.</i>. In either case it has to lose its shape and be taken out to be disposed of by burning<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">The meat can neither be eaten nor brought to the altar since it might be impure or otherwise disqualified; it cannot be disposed of immediately since it might be pure and qualified. One has to wait until the time allotted for each kind having passed and the meat automatically becoming disqualified; this is the remainder of the day for elevation sacrifices, the remainder of the day plus the following night for purification sacrifices, and the following day for well-being sacrifices.</i>.<br>If it was found in the countryside<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">Palestine outside of Jerusalem and its surroundings.</i>, limbs are carrion<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">Since the butcher did not care to cut it into slices, one must assume that it was notkosher and thrown away for the dogs.</i>, cuts are permitted<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">If there are no sources of non-kosher meat in the neighborhood.</i>. On holidays, when meat is abundant, even limbs are permitted<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">Since for big family meals one may buy whole limbs and cut them after cooking.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Would it not be necessarily holy on the Temple Mount<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">Since it is forbidden to enter the Temple Mount in private business (Mishnah <i>Berakhot</i>9:8), how can there be a presumption that monies lost there are profane?</i>? Rebbi Abba, Rebbi Ḥiyya in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: There is a presumption that no Cohen will remove money from the lodge unless it is redeemed by an animal<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">The money legitimately in the hands of private persons on the Temple Mount is money received from the Temple for delivery of goods or services. While the origin of the money is from the Temple, it is legitimately profane in the hands of its owner.</i>.
Rebbi Eleazar in the name of Rebbi Hoshaia: Diversion of attention requires {loss of} shape<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">Sacrificial meat which is left unattended even for a moment cannot be used any more; it has to be kept as is until the time of its sacrificial use has elapsed and then disposed of by burning outside the sacred domain. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 34a" href="/Pesachim.34a">Babli <i>Pesaḥim</i>34a</a>.</i>. Rav Hoshaia said, the Mishnah says so, “it has to lose its shape and be taken out to be disposed of by burning.” <sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">The rest of this Halakhah is missing in B.</i> Rebbi Yose says, this is correct. You may not eat it for maybe its shape already is lost. &lt;you may not burn it<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">On the altar.</i> for maybe its shape is not lost&gt;<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">Missing in the Leiden text, added from <b>ג</b>. Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 7:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.7.2.1">Note 21</a>.</i> Therefore it had to say, “it has to lose its shape and be taken out to be disposed of by burning”.
<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">This Halakhah is missing in B.</i> Rebbi Crispus in the name of Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Ḥanina: One flogs for carrion limbs because of carrion31; and the Mishnah says so: “limbs are carrion, cuts are permitted.” Are cuts not really permitted? And similarly, one flogs for carrion limbs because of carrion.
Rebbi Crispus in the name of Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Ḥanina: If they were strung they are permitted<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">If all butcher shops in the neighborhood are kosher and all households eat kosher, nobody expends the work to string pieces (or sausages) together if they are not kosher and have to be fed to the dogs.</i>. <sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">This sentence is missing in <b>ג</b> and B but there is no reason to doubt its authenticity.</i> Ten stores, nine sell carrion and one sells kosher slaughtered meat, if it was switched, he worries. For what is found, one follows the majority. Ten stores, nine sell kosher slaughtered meat and one sells carrion, if it was switched, he worries<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">In the language of the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ketubot 15a" href="/Ketubot.15a">Babli (<i>Ketubot</i>15a</a>), “anything whose provenience is fromknown fixed sources is considered as 50–50”, and therefore one has to consider the switched package as coming from the store which sells carrion, whether this is one in ten or nine in ten.</i>. For what is found, one follows the majority<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote">If a package of meat is found and provenience and buyer are unknown.</i>.
Rebbi Joḥanan said, what is in the hand of a Gentile is as found on a thoroughfare<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">Greek πλατεῑα (sc. ‘οδός) “a wide (road)”. On a thoroughfare the traffic is not local; even if all local shops are kosher, the majority of travelers come from places which are not kosher, and meat found there automatically is forbidden.</i>. Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Ḥaggai was supporting Rebbi Mana. He saw an Aramean cutting from his horse and feeding his son. He said to him, that is what Rebbi Joḥanan said, what is in the hand of a Gentile is as found on a thoroughfare<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">Meat at the disposal of a Gentile automatically is forbidden.</i>. He answered him, so said the great Rebbi Yose<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote">R. Yose ben Ḥalafta, the Tanna.</i>: Only<sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote">That meat in the possession of the Gentile possibly is kosher.</i> if they saw him leaving a Jewish butcher shop<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">Latin <i>macellum</i>.</i>. A man in Sepphoris went and wanted to buy red meat from a butcher, but he did not give to him. He told a Roman, who brought him. He said to him, did I not buy against your will? He retorted, did I not give carrion to him<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">Disproving R. Yose’s statement. The butcher is happy to sell his non-kosher meatto a Gentile since it is worthless for his Jewish clientele.</i>? Rebbi Jeremiah in the name of Rebbi Ḥanina: A case came before Rebbi who said, it is not believable to forbid the butcher shop of Sepphoris<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">He doubts the genuineness of the story. Since Rebbi Joḥanan lived a generation after Rebbi, his ruling has to be followed.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">42a</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph, accepting the Babylonian opinion that “meat which was out of sight”, out of control for a moment, is prohibited, annulling the Mishnah here, appears in a different order of the cases in <i>Avodah zarah</i> 2:9, Notes 393-395. The Genizah text here follows the arrangement of <i>Avodah zarah</i>.</i> Rav returned there and saw them taking things lightly and was restrictive with them. A man went to wash a piece of meat in the river. He forgot it and left. Then he went and wanted to sell it. Rav told him, it is forbidden to you, for I am saying the other one was carried away by the river and it brought another piece of carcass meat in its place. A man was carrying meat while walking on the market. There came a vulture, seized it from his hand, and dropped it off. He came back and wanted to sell it. Rav told him, it is forbidden to you, for I am saying that it was carrying carcass meat, dropped it and took the other instead.
Ginai<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">A river not otherwise identified (also mentioned in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Demai 1:3:11" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Demai.1.3.11"><i>Demay</i>1:3 (Note 144</a>), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Chullin 7a" href="/Chullin.7a">Babli Ḥulin 7a</a>. Since both known authorities called R. Isaac ben Eleazar were Galilean, the river must be a Galilean brook. The statement made here is that even though wineskins may have been used for non-kosher wine, if they were swept away by a brook but then recovered, identification confirms not only ownership but also possibility of use for kosher wine.</i> swept away wineskins. The case came before Rebbi Isaac ben Eleazar who said, may the vintners recognize their knots.
A sausage was found in the meeting room of the town council. The case came before Rebbi Jeremiah who said, may the butchers recognize their handiwork<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">Since the sausage was whole, the problem of meat out of sight does not arise if the maker recognizes it.</i>.
A roast kid goat was found in the main street of Gufta<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote">The meaning of this word is not clear. It seems to denote the Jewish part of Sepphoris.</i>. They permitted it because of two things, as a find<sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote">Because it was found on a thoroughfare it is ownerless and the finder may take possession without trying to find the owner.</i>, and because of the majority of passers-by<sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote">Since the place was Jewish, the meat is presumed to be kosher.</i>. As a find, as it was stated: If one saves from before a lion, from before an army, from a surge of the sea, or the surge of a river, from a wide road, or a wide plaza, it belongs to him, since the owners give up on them. Because of the majority of passers-by, because of a Gentile’s slaughter. It turned out<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">Nevertheless, nobody tried to eat from the meat before its kosher state was ascertained and certified.</i> that it was from the House of Rebbi.
A wheel of cheese was found in the hostelry of Levi. They permitted it because of two things, as a find, and because of the majority of passers-by. As a find, as it was stated: If one saves from before a lion, from before an army, from a surge of the sea, or the surge of a river, from a wide road, or a wide plaza, it belongs to him, since the owners give up on them. Because of the majority of passers-by, because of Gentile’s cheese. It turned out that it was from Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Yose.
Rebbi Mana said before Rebbi Yose, but do we not see that the rabbis publicize<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the monetary aspect, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 7:2:10" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.7.2.10">Note 46</a>. Rabbis will advertise to find the prior owner even if the find was laying on a well-travelled road.</i>? He told him, if you had been there, you would not have taken it. Your father, Rebbi Jonah, did not say so, but he said, if only I would find it inside from the circular road<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <i>Eruvin</i> Chaptrer 8, Note 102; the access road to and from a town along a long-distance road. “Inside” is the major road in the town, where many people are passing by at all times.</i>. Even so, he found and did not take<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">In practice he did not follow his own permissive ruling which therefore cannot be practice.</i>.

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If it was found in the countryside<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">Palestine outside of Jerusalem and its surroundings.</i>, limbs are carrion<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">Since the butcher did not care to cut it into slices, one must assume that it was notkosher and thrown away for the dogs.</i>, cuts are permitted<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">If there are no sources of non-kosher meat in the neighborhood.</i>. On holidays, when meat is abundant, even limbs are permitted<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">Since for big family meals one may buy whole limbs and cut them after cooking.</i>.<br>Rebbi Simeon said, the Court<sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">The body empowered by the returnees from Babylonia to oversee the functioning of the Second Temple.</i> stipulated seven things, and this<sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote">The stipulation mentioned in the preceding Mishnah, that the libations for a stray animal used as sacrifice should be paid for by the half-<i>sheqel</i> tax.</i> was one of them: If a Gentile<sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote">Who may bring all kinds of voluntary offerings; only obligatory offerings are restricted to full members of the Jewish faith.</i> sent his elevation offering from overseas also sent its libations, they are brought from his property; otherwise they are brought from public money. Similarly, if a proselyte<sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote">He failed to contract a Jewish marriage and start a Jewish family; therefore he has no heirs and his estate is ownerless.</i> died and the estate includes well-being offerings; if he also has flour offerings they are brought from his property; otherwise they are brought from public money. It is a stipulation of the Court that the flour offering of a deceased High Priest<sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote">The daily offering of the High Priest should not stop between the death of one High Priest and the investiture of the next; the only question is whether it is paid for by the heirs of the deceased or by the public.</i> be brought from public money; Rebbi Jehudah says, from his heirs, and it was brought whole<sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote">The offering of the living High Priest is brought in two parts (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 6:13" href="/Leviticus.6.13"><i>Lev.</i>6:13</a>); the offering in the interim is brought whole according to everybody.</i>.<br><sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote">Continuation of the Court stipulations from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 7:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.7.3.1">Mishnah 5</a>.</i> About salt and wood that the Cohanim may use them<sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote">The Cohanim who have to consume most holy sacrifices in the sacred compound may use salt and wood bought with <i>sheqalim</i> to cook the meat and bake <i>maṣsot.</i></i>, and about the Cow that one does not commit larceny with its ashes<sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote">Even though the ashes of the Red Cow are called חַטָּאת, this does not mean “purification sacrifice” but only “(means of) purification.” Even though the Cow was bought with <i>sheqel</i> money, the ashes are no <i>sancta</i>.</i>. And about disqualified nests<sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup><i class="footnote">If a woman put money for a “nest” in the corresponding box, and the birds given to the Cohen for the corresponding sum turned out to be disqualified, they must immediately be replaced since the woman trusts that she may eat <i>sancta</i> after sundown. Since her identity is unknown, she cannot be asked to pay a second time; therefore her nest has to be paid by the public. R. Yose disagrees and holds that the contract with the supplier of birds stipulates that the birds supplied must be qualified. Therefore disqualified birds have to be replaced by the supplier at no cost to the Temple.</i> that they be charged to the public; Rebbi Yose says, he who provides the nests provides the disqualified ones.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">The present paragraph has a parallel in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 2:7:9" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.2.7.9"><i>Qiddušin</i>2:8 (Notes 202–210</a>) of which, however, it is not a direct copy.</i> The elder Rebbi Hoshaia said (more)&lt;to his son&gt;`<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">Of the three readings given by the three parallel sources, the one <b>ג</b> is supported by the parallel in <i>Qiddušin</i> and making sense. In the translation, the texts in parentheses should be disregarded.</i> this was taught for their monetary value<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">It is impossible to say that a male animal which was found ownerless should be taken as elevation offering since it might have been dedicated as well-being offering. The animal should be redeemed and the redemption money used for an elevation offering. The same argument is given in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 55a" href="/Kiddushin.55a">Babli, <i>Qiddušin</i>55a</a>.</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan said to him, does one say to a person, go and commit larceny with sacrifices<sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote">It is impossible to redeem an unblemished dedicated animal (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 27:10" href="/Leviticus.27.10">Lev. 27:10</a>.) Any redemption is both sinful and ineffective. R. Hoshiah’s rule seems to be impossible.</i>? But they followed the majority of cases: If most<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote">The animal itself should be used for what was its most probable dedication.</i> are male, they are elevation offerings, if most are female, well-being offerings. But do not well-being offerings come from males and females? What does he do? He redeems them as profane and then turns them into elevation offerings<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote">One follows both R. Hoshaia and R. Joḥanan. The animal is first redeemed and then rededicated; this precludes the sin of freeing a dedicated animal and removes the prior specific dedication. In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 55b" href="/Kiddushin.55b">Babli, <i>Qiddušin</i>55b</a>, R. Joḥanan holds that the redemption of unblemished animals is never possible. He requires that the animal be put out to graze until it develops a blemish; then it can be redeemed and the proceeds used for another sacrifice. In any case, the answer is unsatisfactory. Since the Mishnah states that people were refraining from picking up stray animals because they did not want to pay for its flour offerings, they certainly do not want to take upon themselves the much greater expense of redemption.</i>. Rebbi Ze`ira said, it is a stipulation by the court that all redundant animals should be brought as elevation offerings, so it is a stipulation by the court that lost animals should be brought as elevation offerings<sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote">Therefore, it is part of every dedication of any male animal that, if not needed for its original purpose, it should be used as an elevation offering. It is also part of every dedication of any male animal that, if lost and then found by another person, it should become an elevation offering.</i>. Rebbi Yose said to Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa<sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote">Since R. Jacob bar Aḥa lived two generations before R. Yose, the reading of B, R. Assi (= Yasa) has to be accepted.</i>, is that not intentional misuse? He said to him, since it is a stipulation by the court, it is not intentional misuse.
<sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 2:4:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.2.4.2">Chapter 2, Notes 81–83</a>.</i> Rebbi Yasa said, when I still was there, I heard the voice of Rav Jehudah asking Samuel, if somebody had set his <i>sheqel</i> apart and died? He told him, they shall fall to gift. The excess of his tenth of an ephah, Rebbi Joḥanan said, one shall bring them to the Dead Sea. Rebbi Eleazar said, it shall fall to gift.
The tenth of an <i>ephah</i> from the High Priest<sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 6:12-16" href="/Leviticus.6.12-16"><i>Lev.</i> 6:12–16</a>.</i>. [Rebbi Joḥanan said,]<sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote">Correct addition by the corrector.</i> he splits it and then dedicates<sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">The requirement is a tenth of an <i>ephah</i> daily, half in the morning and half in the evening. Since the volume of the flour is prescribed, it must be measured. R. Joḥanan must hold that the measuring vessel is not a Temple vessel which automatically dedicates anything poured into it; otherwise there would be no possibility of dedicating the two parts separately.</i>. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, he dedicates and afterwards splits it. A Mishnah<sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Menachot 4:5" href="/Mishnah_Menachot.4.5">Mishnah <i>Menaḥot</i>4:5</a>.</i> disagrees with Rebbi Joḥanan: “He brings half of it; the other half is lost.<sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote">If a High Priest died after he had brought his morning offering and another was appointed before the evening, the second part of the first’s offering cannot be used anymore, but has to be kept to the next day and then burned outside the sacred compound as disqualified sacrifice. The second one must bring a tenth of an <i>ephah</i>, but only the second half may be used.</i>” He explains it, because even the money has to be brought to the Dead Sea<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote">Since R. Joḥanan holds that even money set aside for the Tenth but not used has to be destroyed (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 7:3:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.7.3.3">Note 70</a>), he will agree that the second half cannot be used even if not dedicated.</i>. A Mishnah<sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Menachot 4:5" href="/Mishnah_Menachot.4.5">Mishnah <i>Menaḥot</i>4:5</a>.</i> disagrees with Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish: “It turns out that two halves are brought and two halves are lost.” And it was stated on this<sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Menachot 7:5" href="/Tosefta_Menachot.7.5">Tosephta <i>Menaḥot</i>7:10</a>.</i>: “If the first one’s, the second half should lose its shape and be brought to the place of burning.<sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote">This text is difficult for R. Joḥanan (reading of B) and R. Simeon ben Laqish. For R. Joḥanan, why should the flour become unusable if it was not yet dedicated? The answer is given in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 7:3:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.7.3.4">Note 76</a>. For R. Simeon ben Laqish, the entire flour is dedicated as sacrifice from the start; if it becomes disqualified in any way, it should be burned immediately and not need waiting for the next day.</i>” He explains it following Rebbi Ismael, for Rebbi Ismael said, the <i>issaron</i><sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote">Since the dedication is automatic, not by his conscious act, it does not have the status of a directly dedicated animal and needs waiting for the next day.</i> dedicates. “If a Cohen comes first to serve, he brings his Tenth and officiates himself.<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Sifra, Tzav, Section 3 3" href="/Sifra,_Tzav,_Section_3.3"><i>Sifra Ṣaw Parashah</i>3(3</a>). He has to bring the tenth of an <i>ephah</i> once in his lifetime, when he officiates in the Temple the first time. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 6:13" href="/Leviticus.6.13"><i>Lev.</i> 6:13</a>.</i>” The officiating of both a High Priest and a common priest who officiated before they brought their tenth of an <i>ephah</i> is valid. Rebbi Mana wanted to say, if on that very day<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">A Cohen was appointed as High Priest on the day he first came to officiate in the Temple. Confirmed <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 78a" href="/Menachot.78a">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>78a</a>.</i> he was appointed High Priest he brings two, one for his initiation and one as daily obligation.
תּוּפִינֵי<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 6:14" href="/Leviticus.6.14"><i>Lev.</i> 6:14</a>, a word of unknown etymology.</i>. It has to be תּוּפִינֵי when it is brought, it does not have to be תּוּפִינֵי early in the morning<sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote">A Second Temple source.</i>. But did we not state<sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote">A Second Temple source.</i>, “they place those who bake the baked goods to make the baked goods”? Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Ada said, to make the hot water to soften them. תּוּפִינֵי, Rebbi Yasa in the name of Rebbi Ḥanina, he fries them and after that bakes them. Rebbi Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Ḥanina, he bakes them and after that fries them. תּוּפִינֵי, they shall be baked cooked<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote">An attempt to explain the word תפיני as contraction of תאפה נא. The following two statements have to be explained in a similar way. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 50b" href="/Menachot.50b">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>50b</a>.</i>. Rebbi said, they shall be baked softly; Rebbi Dosa said, they shall be baked beautifully. This disagreement is parallel to the other disagreement. He who says, they shall be baked beautifully, is like him who says, he fries them and after that bakes them<sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote">The daily offering of the High Priest should not stop between the death of one High Priest and the investiture of the next; the only question is whether it is paid for by the heirs of the deceased or by the public.</i>. He who says, they shall be baked softly is like him who says, he bakes them and after that fries them.
Not only if he died, but even if he became impure; and even if he became disabled by a defect<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">Since <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 6:13" href="/Leviticus.6.13"><i>Lev.</i> 6:13</a> reads: <i>this is the offering of Aaron and his sons which they have to offer to the Eternal</i>, the daily flour sacrifice should be offered by the High Priest himself. While the service can be delegated to a common priest, the High Priest must be able to do it himself. If somehow he is disabled, it is as if there were no High Priest.</i>. Rebbi Jehudah bar Pazi stated from Bar Delaia<sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote">A Second Temple source.</i>: Even if he became disabled by a defect. <sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 51b" href="/Menachot.51b">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>51b</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sifra, Tzav, Chapter 5 3" href="/Sifra,_Tzav,_Chapter_5.3"><i>Sifra Ṣaw Pereq</i>5(3</a>).</i>“From where that if a High Priest dies and no other was appointed in his stead that his flour offering is brought from the heirs? The verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 6:15" href="/Leviticus.6.15"><i>Lev.</i> 6:15</a>.</i>, <i>from his sons he shall make</i>. I could think that he should bring it in halves, the verse says, <i>it</i>, entire I said, the words of Rebbi Jehudah. Rebbi Simeon says, it only comes from the public, for it says, <i>an eternal law</i>, (to whom the creatures belong.)<sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote">This text does not make any sense. It seems necessary to adopt the reading of <i>Sifra</i>, בְּרִית “covenant”, instead of “creatures”. Then, Ravad explains, the expression חָק־עוֹלָ֕ם is compared to the same expression used for the shew-bread (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 24:9" href="/Leviticus.24.9"><i>Lev.</i> 24:9</a>) where in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 24:8" href="/Leviticus.24.8">v. 8</a> בְּרִ֥ית עוֹלָֽם is used. The translation then is: “who are in the covenant.” The Babli (<i>loc. cit.</i>) simply reads עוֹלָם as in rabbinic Hebrew “public”.</i> <i>Totally it shall be burned</i>, all is for burning.
Rebbi Abba bar Mamal asked, the system of Rebbi Simeon seems inverted.
