There he says, from the heirs, but here he says, from the public<sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote">In the Mishnah he qualifies the rule that the daily flour offering in the absence of a High Priest is charged to the public as a Court stipulation, implying that by biblical law it should be charged to the High Priest’s heirs. In <i>Sifra</i> he deduces the rule from a biblical verse.</i>. Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba said, is that not a pertinent question? There came Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa, Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: It is a word from the Torah that it should be brought from the public. I could say, one should tax for it<sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote">In the Mishnah he qualifies the rule that the daily flour offering in the absence of a High Priest is charged to the public as a Court stipulation, implying that by biblical law it should be charged to the High Priest’s heirs. In <i>Sifra</i> he deduces the rule from a biblical verse.</i>; they instituted that it should come from what is taken from the lodge<sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">It seems that one should read with B: collect it from the heirs.</i>.
Rebbi Yose<sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote">With B read: Yasa (Assi).</i> said, Rebbi Joḥanan asked: Entire in the morning and entire in the evening, or half in the morning and half in the evening, [or entire in the morning and nothing in the evening]<sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote">The High Priest has to bring a fIour offering mornings and evenings (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 6:13" href="/Leviticus.6.13"><i>Lev.</i> 6:13</a>). If the High Priest is dead or disabled and according to the Mishnah his flour offering has to be brought entire, does that mean two offerings per day, or only one in the morning? It is clear that the sentence about bringing two halves has to be deleted and the corrector’s addition from B accepted.</i>? Then it should be obvious to him, what about three log<sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote">The text about the High Priest’s offering only mentions oil but does not specify its quantity. It is deduced either from the libations required in general for a sheep (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 15:4" href="/Numbers.15.4"><i>Num</i>. 15:4</a>) or from the specifics indicated for the daily sacrifice (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 28:5" href="/Numbers.28.5"><i>Num</i>. 28:5</a>) that a tenth of an <i>ephah</i> of flour requires a quarter of a <i>hin</i>, 3 <i>log</i>, of olive oil. This therefore is the quantity of oil required here, even though it is used for frying, not for mixing as in the cases where the quantities are specified. <i>Sifra Ṣaw Pereq</i>4:1–5; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 52b" href="/Menachot.52b">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>52b</a>.</i>? Three log in the morning and three log in the afternoon, or a log and a half in the morning and a log and a half in the afternoon? Rebbi Ḥizqiah said, also the following was a problem for him: Two handful<sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote">In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 52a" href="/Menachot.52a">Babli, <i>Menaḥot</i>52a</a>, R. Joḥanan reports that the Tenth of the High Priest also requires addition of a handful of incense like other flour offerings. He also reports that there is a dispute whether the living High Priest has to bring one handful, which is split into two, or two separate handfuls for morning and evening services. But since here the question is about the Tenth for the absent or incapacitated High Priest, one infers that the Yerushalmi holds that the living High Priest only brings one handful.</i> in the morning and two handful in the evening or one handful in the morning and one handful in the evening? Rebbi Yose said, did they not the two handful infer from the sinner’s flour offering<sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote">This reading is impossible since the sinner’s flour offering (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 5:11" href="/Leviticus.5.11"><i>Lev.</i> 5:11</a>) is brought without oil and incense. The commentators conjecture an emendation “from the shew bread” which is put onto the table in two rows, each one with a cup of incense.</i>? Just as there two handful, also here two handful. Just as there it was problematic for him, so here it is problematic for him<sup class="footnote-marker">99</sup><i class="footnote">Missing in B and M, probably correctly.</i>. Rebbi Ḥizqiah said, did one not infer the three log from the daily afternoon sacrifice<sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote">The text about the High Priest’s offering only mentions oil but does not specify its quantity. It is deduced either from the libations required in general for a sheep (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 15:4" href="/Numbers.15.4"><i>Num</i>. 15:4</a>) or from the specifics indicated for the daily sacrifice (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 28:5" href="/Numbers.28.5"><i>Num</i>. 28:5</a>) that a tenth of an <i>ephah</i> of flour requires a quarter of a <i>hin</i>, 3 <i>log</i>, of olive oil. This therefore is the quantity of oil required here, even though it is used for frying, not for mixing as in the cases where the quantities are specified. <i>Sifra Ṣaw Pereq</i>4:1–5; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 52b" href="/Menachot.52b">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>52b</a>.</i>? Since there {are} three log, so also here three log. [Just as] there it was problematic for him, [so] here it is (obvious) [problematic] for him1<sup>00</sup>.
Rebbi Samuel ben Naḥman in the name of Rebbi Jonathan: It would have been logical<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote">Since the Cow is treated as a <i>sanctum</i>, it is clear that until its ashes are collected as required in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 19:9" href="/Numbers.19.9"><i>Num</i>. 19:9</a>, any action not in accordance with the procedure prescribed in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 19:2-9" href="/Numbers.19.2-9">vv. 2–9</a> will invalidate the procedure and usufruct of correct procedure will be larceny of <i>sacra</i>. According to the general principle that once the required procedures are executed, there can be no longer larceny of <i>sacra</i>, the problem is to decide whether the correct preparation of the ashes is the final step in this regard, or the sprinkling on a person impure in the impurity of the dead, as described in the verses following. To say that it would be logical is tantamount to a statement that one could argue the second position but, since the answer is not clear from the biblical text, it is up to the Court overseeing the Temple to decide which opinion to follow.</i> that one commit larceny with them, but they decided that one does not commit larceny with them. But did we not state<sup class="footnote-marker">106</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 51b-52a" href="/Menachot.51b-52a">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>51b/52a</a>.</i>: “<i>it is ḥattat</i>, this teaches that one commits larceny with it. [With it one commits larceny,]<sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition following B and M, correct but not absolutely necessary.</i> with its ashes one does not commit larceny.” Rebbi Abbahu said, at the beginning they were using it as a disinfectant<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote">Reading as Arabic שקשק “to rinse”.</i> and were putting it on their wounds and therefore they decided that one would commit larceny with it<sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote">But biblically the ashes never could lead to larceny of <i>sacra</i>.</i>. When they were fenced in<sup class="footnote-marker">110</sup><i class="footnote">It was certain that no illegitimate use would be tolerated.</i>, they decided that one does not commit larceny with it.
By what is that woman atoned for<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">Since the money may have been given by a woman needing purification, if it happens that her monies were used as elevation offering, how can she ever eat <i>sancta</i>? The sentence and the next are reproduced at the end of the Chapter (7).</i>? Rebbi Isaac said, it is a stipulation of the Court that the providers of nests also provide the disqualified and the lost ones<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">The provider has to provide a few extra birds which are treated as possible purification offerings (a situation impossible for four-legged animals) but are not eaten.</i>.

Chapter 8



Halakhah 1

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> All spittle<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Any impurity caused by a human body itself, such as in a person afflicted by gonorrhea, is a source of severe impurity, and all his body fluids are sources of severe impurity. In any place other than Jerusalem, one must assume that spittle was ejected by an impure person whose impurity was caused by his body (cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Tahorot 4:5" href="/Mishnah_Tahorot.4.5">Mishnah <i>Ṭahorot</i>4:5</a>). By rabbinic usage, all Gentiles are considered to be in this category. In Jerusalem, where people are used to eat <i>sancta</i> the entire year according to R. Meןr, or on the holidays according to R. Yose, one may assume that impure people are careful not to contaminate their pure neighbors. This is a reconstruction by authors living two generations after the destruction of the Temple.</i> found in Jerusalem is pure except on the Upper Market<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">A Gentile neighborhood.</i>, the words of Rebbi Meןr. Rebbi Yose says, on all other days of the year, those in the middle of the road are impure, and those on the sides pure. On holidays, those in the middle of the road are pure and those on the sides impure since the minority will remove themselves to the sides.<br>All implements which are found in Jerusalem on the road descending to the place of immersion are impure, on the way ascending they are pure since they were brought down on a way different from that on which they were brought up, the words of Rebbi Meןr. Rebbi Yose says, all are pure except the bag and the rake<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">As the Halakhah shows, a word “the hoe” is missing here, found in B and the independent Mishnah mss.</i> set apart for graves.<br>If a knife was found on the Fourteenth<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">The 14<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Nisan, the day of slaughter of the <i>Pesaḥ</i> sacrifice. Even though the previous Mishnah stated that all implements found in Jerusalem are presumed to be pure, for use on <i>sancta</i> one is restrictive and requires immersion in a <i>miqweh</i> and waiting for the following sundown. The only time this requirement is waived is the 14<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Nisan, the day of mass slaughter, where it is presumed that every knife which is qualified to be used for ritual slaughter was immersed in a <i>miqweh</i> the previous day.</i>, one may slaughter with it immediately; on the Thirteenth one has to repeat and immerse<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">Since all knives are immersed on the 13<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Nisan, one has to assume that this particular knife was lost on the way to the <i>miqweh</i>.</i>. A dagger<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">Which is not usable for slaughter and therefore not necessarily immersed in a <i>miqweh</i>.</i> in either case one has to repeat and immerse. If the Fourteenth falls on a Sabbath, one may slaughter with it immediately<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">Since one may not immerse on that day, certainly the knife had been immersed on the 13<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup>.</i>; on the Fifteenth one may slaughter with it immediately<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">Since the 15th of Nisan is a holiday where immersion is not done, and the knife was purified for the 14th, the presumption of purity extends to this case.</i>. If it<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">The dagger.</i> was tied to a knife its status is that of the knife.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “All spittle,” etc. Rebbi Abbin in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: A Gentile fortification<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Reading קצטרן, “their <i>castra</i>”. The Babli text reads קצרן “their laundry”.</i> was there. Rebbi Ḥanina said, they were stabbing wild donkeys in Jerusalem and the feet of the pilgrims were immersed in blood up to their knee joints<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in the next paragraph, while carcasses of four-legged animals are a source of impurity (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 11:26-28" href="/Leviticus.11.26-28"><i>Lev.</i> 11:26–28</a>), this does not extend to their blood, which does not cause impurity. Gentile circus games have no impact on purity in Jerusalem (except for the removal of the carcasses which must be done by Gentiles.) <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 103b" href="/Menachot.103b">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>103b</a>.</i>. [They came before the Sages who did not tell them anything.]<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from B, correct but unnecessary.</i> Rebbi Simeon bar Abba in the name of Rebbi Ḥanina: A Gentile fortification was there.
<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">The text was copied more or less in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 3:2:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.3.2.3">Chapter 3:2, Notes 40</a> ff. The full explanation is given in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shabbat 8:1:9" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shabbat.8.1.9"><i>Šabbat</i>8, Notes 51–62</a>.</i> Rebbi Simon in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: It happened that a mule of Rebbi’s household died and they declared its blood pure regarding the carcass. Rebbi Eleazar asked Rebbi Simon, how much? He did not take notice of him. He asked Rebbi Joshua ben Levi who told him, it is pure up to a <i>quartarius</i>. More than that is impure. Rebbi Eleazar felt badly that Rebbi Simon had not repeated the tradition to him. Rav Bevai was sitting stating this occurrence. Rebbi Isaac bar Bisna asked him, is it pure up to a <i>quartarius</i>; more than that impure? He was unfriendly to him. Rebbi Zeriqa asked him, because he asked you, you were unfriendly to him? He answered him, because my mind was not clear, as Rebbi Ḥanin said, <sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 28:66" href="/Deuteronomy.28.66"><i>Deut</i>. 28:66</a>.</i><i>your life will hang far from you</i>, that is one who buys a year’s supply of wheat, <i>you will be fearful night and day</i>, that is one who buys from the Saracen, <i>and you will not believe in your survival</i>, that is one who buys from the retail store, and I am dependent on retail stores. What about it? “Rebbi Joshua ben Bathyra testified about blood of carcasses that it is pure.<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Eduyot 8:1" href="/Mishnah_Eduyot.8.1">Mishnah <i>Idiut</i>8:1</a>.</i>” What means pure? It is pure in that it does not prepare, but for impurity it makes impure. There, we have stated “The blood of a crawling animal is like its flesh, it makes impure but does not prepare. Nothing else is like this,<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Makhshirin 6:5" href="/Mishnah_Makhshirin.6.5">Mishnah <i>Makhširin</i>6:5</a>.</i>” in the amount needed for impurity but its blood makes impure like its flesh. Rav Joseph said, he who says “impure” follows Rebbi Jehudah; he who said “pure” follows Rebbi Joshua ben Bathyra. Rav Eudaimon the emigrant said to him, this is correct. Rebbi Jehudah was the instructor of the Patriarch.
Did not Rebbi Abbahu say in the name of Rebbi Yose ben Ḥanina, they did not decide about spittle in Jerusalem<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">Nobody required that heave and other <i>sancta</i> be considered potentially impure because they touched spittle of unknown provenience, in contrast to all places in the Holy Land outside of Jerusalem (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Tahorot 4:5" href="/Mishnah_Tahorot.4.5">Mishnah <i>Ṭahorot</i>4:5</a>), since the number of people whose impurity is caused by their own body is minuscule. Then why is the Upper Market in Jerusalem excluded? <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 19b" href="/Pesachim.19b">Babli <i>Pesaḥim</i>19b</a>.</i>? [Was it not said]<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from B, in Babli terminology.</i> about this, Rebbi Abbin in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: A Gentile fortification<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Reading קצטרן, “their <i>castra</i>”. The Babli text reads קצרן “their laundry”.</i> was there<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">One must assume that the spittle is a Gentile’s, automatically impure by rabbinic standards.</i>? In the remainder of the days of a year the impure ones are walking on the path<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">A form of שביל “path”, not “ear of grain”.</i> and the pure ones are walking on the shoulder. The pure ones walk without saying anything, the impure ones tell them, keep apart. During a holiday<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">When practically everybody was pure as long as the Temple existed.</i> the pure ones are walking on the path and the impure ones are walking on the shoulder. The impure ones walk without saying anything, the pure ones tell them, keep apart.
But did not Rebbi Abbahu say in the name of<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">Missing in B.</i> Rebbi Joḥanan, they did not decide about vessels in Jerusalem<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">In contrast to all other places in the Holy Land, one does not have to presume that vessels found in Jerusalem be impure. Then why does R. Meןr declare some vessels impure?</i>? Since they were found on the road descending to the place of immersion, it is proof<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">These must be presumed impure unless the opposite is proven.</i>.
Abba Shaul used to call it<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">The word for “hoe” missing in the Mishnah. The word מְרִיצָה is a <i>hapax</i> and according to the second opinion used exclusively for the gravedigger’s (or burial cave excavator’s) hoe.</i> “fingernail” since it is shaped like a fingernail. He who said מְרִיצָה because it quickly dispatches the stone [to the cemetery.]<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from B; questionable since the text seems to refer to excavating burial caves (impossible in the Iraqi plain.)</i>
It was stated: If he knife was tied to it<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">The dagger.</i> its status is that of the knife<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">It seems that the last sentence in the Mishnah was missing in the original Yerushalmi Mishnah; therefore it is quoted as a <i>baraita</i>; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 8:2:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.8.2.4">Note 43</a>.</i>.

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If a gobelin<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">In the Temple, separating the Holiest of Holies from the Temple Hall. Since it is an implement, not a fixed part of the building, it may become impure.</i> became impure by derivative impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">A rabbinic impurity. By biblical standards, implements may become impure only by contact with original impurity.</i>, one immersed it inside and brought it back immediately. But if by original impurity, one immersed it outside and spread it out in the ante-court<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">The enclosed plaza in front of the entrance to the Temple courtyard.</i> because it requires sundown. If it was new, one spreads it out on the roof of the stoa<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">The double stoa built by Herod as enclosure of the Temple district.</i> so the people could see its workmanship, which was beautiful.<br>Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel says in the name of Rebbi Simeon, the son of the Executive Officer of the Temple<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">Who credibly could inform about details of the Temple some 80 years after its destruction.</i>: The thickness of a gobelin was a hand-width. It was woven on 72 strings<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">Of the warp.</i> and each string was composed of 24 threads<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">Since the gobelin had to be made from blue, purple, and crimson wool, and byssus (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 26:31" href="/Exodus.26.31"><i>Ex.</i> 26:31</a>), and each kind was twined of six threads.</i>. Its length 40 cubits and its width 20 cubits; it was made for 820’000 {denar}. Two were made every year<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote">According to the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Shekalim (Lieberman) 3:15" href="/Tosefta_Shekalim_(Lieberman).3.15">Tosephta (3:15</a>), one was hung new on the Eve of the Day of Atonement and the other kept in reserve if some impurity should occur on one of the two which were in use.</i> and 300 Cohanim were immersing it<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">For purification; see end of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 8:2:2-4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.8.2.2-4">Halakhah 4</a>.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> If it had said “thread”, one, “double”, two, “twisted”, three, “<i>entwined</i>”, six<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">One tries to explain why the expression <i>entwined</i> used in the biblical text for all woven textiles used in the Temple (except the garments of the simple priests) means a multiply twisted string. Since there are other words available for small numbers of threads, <i>entwined</i> must designate heavy strings.</i>. There are four kinds, this makes 24. It was stated 32. If it had said “thread”, one, “double”, two, “twisted”, four, “<i>entwined</i>”, eight. There are four kinds, this makes 32. It was stated 48. If it had said “thread”, one, “double”, two, “plaited” three, “twisted”, six, “<i>entwined</i>”, twelve. There are four kinds, this makes 48.
<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Shekalim (Lieberman) 3:14" href="/Tosefta_Shekalim_(Lieberman).3.14">Tosephta 3:14</a>; explained differently in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 72b" href="/Yoma.72b">Babli <i>Yoma</i>72b</a>.</i>“One verse says <i>embroidered work</i><sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 26:36" href="/Exodus.26.36"><i>Ex.</i> 26:36</a>.</i>, and one verse says, <i>intelligent work</i><sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 26:31" href="/Exodus.26.31"><i>Ex.</i> 26:31</a>.</i>. <i>Embroidered work</i>, one face<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">Greek προσώπον, τό. The scribe originally wrote correctly פרוסיף.</i>, <i>intelligent work,</i> two faces.” Rebbi Jehudah and Rebbi Nehemiah, one said <i>embroidered work,</i> a lion on each side, <i>intelligent work,</i> a lion on one side and nothing on the other side. The other one said, <i>embroidered work,</i> a lion on one side and nothing on the other side, <i>intelligent work,</i> a lion on one side and an eagle on the other side.
(It was stated:)<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">This was written by the scribe but then deleted. S. Liebermann (<i>Tarbiz</i>5, p. 261) also sees here a sign that the statement was not part of the original Galilean Mishnah.</i> “It was made for 820’000 {denar}.” Rebbi Isaac bar Bisna in the name of Samuel: exaggerated<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">In the Babli, as also in B, always the noun “exaggeration” is used.</i>. There, we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Tamid 2:2" href="/Mishnah_Tamid.2.2">Mishnah <i>Tamid</i>2:2</a>, describing the amount of ashes accumulated on the altar at the end of a night. B quotes the entire Mishnah.</i>: “Sometimes there was on it about 300 <i>kor</i><sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote">About 114m<sup>3</sup>, a volume impossible for the surface area of 174.5m<sup>2</sup> of the fire on the altar. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tamid 29a" href="/Tamid.29a">Babli <i>Tamid</i>29a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Chullin 90b" href="/Chullin.90b"><i>Ḥulin</i>90b</a>.</i>.” Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun in the name of Samuel: exaggerated.

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Flesh of most holy sacrifices<sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote">Elevation, purification, and reparation sacrifices, whose flesh never should leave the sacred precinct.</i> which became impure either by original impurity or by derivative impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">Derivative impurity is rabbinic impurity; according to biblical standards the flesh could be eaten.</i>, whether inside or outside, the House of Shammai are saying that everything has to be burned inside except what became impure outside by original impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">Since most holy sacrifices may not leave the sacred precinct, flesh disqualified for the altar must be burned in the courtyard. Only if the flesh was taken outside and became biblically impure can it not be returned and must be disposed of by being burnt outside.</i>. The House of Hillel are saying that everything has to be burned outside except what became impure inside by derivative impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote">They hold that flesh impure by biblical standards has to be removed as quickly as possible from the sacred precinct; then it can be burned outside in leisurely fashion. Flesh inside which is considered impure only by common usage, not biblical decree, may be burned in the courtyard. No flesh impure in any way may be introduced into the sacred precinct.</i>.<br>Rebbi Eliezer says, what became impure by original impurity, whether inside or outside, shall be burned outside. But what became impure by derivative impurity, whether inside or outside, shall be burned inside<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">In the matter of burning, he considers rabbinic impurity as nonexistent.</i>. Rebbi Aqiba said, the place of its impurity is the place of its burning<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote">This is his interpretation of the hidden meaning of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 6:23" href="/Leviticus.6.23"><i>Lev.</i> 6:23</a>, as explained in <i>Sifra Saw Pereq</i>8(5–6), where also additional opinions of RR. Meïr and Jehudah are reported.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote">The same statement is found in <i>Ma`aser Šeni</i>3:8 (Note 103) and <i>Pesaḥim</i>1:7, Notes 166,167.</i> Bar Qappara said, original impurity is a word from the Torah, derivative impurity is of their words. Rebbi Joḥanan said, both these and those are words of the Torah<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 7:19" href="/Leviticus.7.19"><i>Lev.</i> 7:19</a> one reads: <i>Any meat which touches anything impure may not be eaten, in fire it shall be burned</i>. Since it is not stated “touches any impure person”, one has to conclude that <i>anything impure</i> refers to implements or similar things which became impure from the touch of an impure person. Therefore it is clear that by biblical standards there exist derivative impurities. Bar Qappara holds that anything which makes something else impure is called original impurity. Since the verse does not refer to the meat as impure, he will hold that it is disqualified but its touch will not make the implement touched impure. He restricts the term “impure” to matter able to transmit impurity; matter disqualified is classifioed as “derivative impurity”. R. Joḥanan will hold that the meat, two touches distant from original impurity, still is impure by biblical standards (even though it is not called so in the text.) Everybody will agree that further impurities, 3 and 4 touches separated from original impurity, are rabbinic (or customary) categories of impurity.</i>. <sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote">Similar discussions, referring to other Mishnaiot, are in <i>Ma`aser Šeni</i>3:8 (Note 103) and <i>Pesaḥim</i> 1:7, Notes 166,167.</i> The House of Shammai is difficult for Rebbi Joḥanan, since the House of Shammai said, “everything has to be burned inside except what became impure outside by original impurity.” What is the difference between [original]<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">Correct addition by the corrector. (The clause is missing in B.)</i> impurity and derivative impurity outside, are not both of them words of the Torah? And even the House of Hillel is difficult for him, since the House of Hillel say, “everything has to be burned outside except what became impure inside by derivative impurity.” What is the difference between derivative impurity inside and original impurity inside, are not both of them words of the Torah? The rabbis only discuss Bar Qappara’s opinion<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">Since the objections to R. Joḥanan’s opinion cannot be answered, his statement cannot be valid in rabbinic tradition.</i>. The House of Shammai is difficult for Bar Qappara, since the House of Shammai said, “everything has to be burned inside except what became impure outside by original impurity.” What is the difference between original impurity outside or inside, are not both of them words of the Torah? Because of Rebbi Aqiba, who said “the place of its impurity shall be the place of its burning.<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">The House of Shammai will accept R. Aqiba’s interpretation of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 6:23" href="/Leviticus.6.23"><i>Lev.</i> 6:23</a>; this explains their position without reference to Bar Qappara’s statement.</i>” Would not the House of Hillel also be difficult for him, since the House of Hillel say, “everything has to be burned outside except what became impure inside by derivative impurity.” What is the difference for derivative impurity inside or outside, are not both of them their words? Because of Rebbi Simeon, since Rebbi Simeon said, food and drink of a person afflicted with skin disease are sent outside the three camps<sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote">This is a complicated formulation of the simple statement of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 8:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.8.3.1">Note 50</a>. It is inferred from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 5:2-4" href="/Numbers.5.2-4"><i>Num</i>. 5:2–4</a> (<i>Sifry Num</i>. 1) that there were three encampments in the desert, the holy precinct of the Tent of Meeting, the encampment of the Levites, and that of the Israelites. These are represented by the Temple enclosure, the Temple Mount, and Jerusalem (or any walled city in the Holy Land). Then it is stated that from the categories of people excluded from the holy sites, people impure in the impurity of the dead are excluded from the Temple precinct, those suffering from gonorrhea (or anybody whose impurity is caused by his own body) is excluded from the Temple Mount, and the sufferer from skin disease is excluded from the city. R. Simeon explains that the sufferers from skin disease under no circumstance can enter the city; this is a paradigm for the statement that anything impure never may be brought into a place from which it is excluded.</i>.

Halakhah 4

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The limbs of the daily sacrifice are deposited on the lower part of the ramp to the West<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in <i>Yoma</i> Chapter 2, the sacrifices were slaughtered and cut into pieces which immediately were carried to the ramp leading up to the altar, but then were taken up one by one to be burned on the relatively small area of the fire on the altar.</i>, those of the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote">Of the Sabbaths and holidays.</i> on the lower part of the altar. Those of the days of the New Moon on the rim<sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in the Halakhah, on top of the altar, between its horns, on the place usually reserved for the Cohanim serving at the altar.</i> on the top of the altar. <i>Sheqalim</i> and First Fruits<sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sheqalim</i> are dedicated for the Temple service; if there is no Temple there are no <i>sheqalim</i>. Of First Fruits it says (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 23:19" href="/Exodus.23.19"><i>Ex.</i> 23:19</a>): <i>Bring the First Fruits of your land to the Eternal’s House</i>; if there is no House they cannot be brought (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Shekalim (Lieberman) 3:24" href="/Tosefta_Shekalim_(Lieberman).3.24">Tosephta 3:24</a>).</i> apply only if there is a Temple, but tithes of grain, and tithes of animals, and firstlings<sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">Of all these, the verse (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 18:12-19" href="/Numbers.18.12-19"><i>Num</i>. 18:12–19</a>) says that these are <i>given to the Eternal</i>; therefore they are obligations independent of the Temple.</i>, apply whether there is a Temple or there is no Temple. If somebody dedicates <i>sheqalim</i> or First Fruits<sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote">Today, in the absence of a Temple. R. Simeon holds that a dedication as First Fruits is a vow in error which does not need annulment.</i>, they are sanctified. Rebbi Simeon says, even if somebody designates First Fruits as holy, they are not holy.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “What is ‘the rim of the altar<sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote">The word is a <i>hapax</i> in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 27:5" href="/Exodus.27.5">Bible, <i>Ex.</i> 27:5</a>. The explanation is intended also as applicable to the biblical word. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Shekalim (Lieberman) 3:19" href="/Tosefta_Shekalim_(Lieberman).3.19">Tosephta 3:19</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 62a" href="/Zevachim.62a">Babli <i>Zevaḥim</i> 62a</a>.</i>’? A cubit between two horns, on the place reserved for the feet of the Cohanim walking.”
<sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph is copied in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sukkah 5:6:7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sukkah.5.6.7"><i>Sukkah</i>5:6 (Note 124</a>).</i> Which of the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices of the Sabbath and of the New Moon has precedence<sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote">The question may be asked here since the limbs of the sacrifices of the New Month are stored much closer to the fire on the altar than those of the Sabbath sacrifices.</i>? Rebbi Jeremiah wanted to say, between the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices of the Sabbath and of the New Month, the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices of the New Month have precedence. The strength of Rebbi Jeremiah is from the following: Between the song of the Sabbath and the song of the New Month<sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Sukkah 54b" href="/Sukkah.54b">Babli <i>Sukkah</i>54b</a>.</i>, the song of the New Month has precedence. Rebbi Yose said, there is a difference there since Rebbi Ḥiyya said in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: To make a proclamation to publicize that it is the start of a new month. How does one do it? One slaughters the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices of the Sabbath and says for them the song of the New Month. But here, between the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices of the Sabbath and of the New Month, the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices of the Sabbath have precedence, under the category: what is more frequent than another precedes the other<sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote">A general principle, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yoma 2:2:8" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yoma.2.2.8"><i>Yoma</i>2:3 (Note 127</a>), <i>Ta`anit</i>4:5 (68b l.30), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 51b" href="/Berakhot.51b">Babli <i>Berakhot</i>51b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 114a" href="/Pesachim.114a"><i>Pesaḥim</i>114a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 91a" href="/Zevachim.91a"><i>Zevaḥim</i>91a</a>.</i>.
Did <i>sheqalim</i> therefore<sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote">Since in the Mishnah R. Simon only states that dedications of First Fruits are ineffective; he is silent about <i>sheqalim</i>.</i> become holy<sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote">Is a <i>sheqel</i> dedicated today reserved for use in the Temple; in absence of a Temple any use of it would be larceny of <i>sacra</i>.</i>? Rebbi Simeon ben Jehudah in the name of Rebbi Simeon: Both these and those<sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">First fruits and <i>sheqalim</i>.</i> did not become holy. It was stated:<sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Shekalim (Lieberman) 3:22" href="/Tosefta_Shekalim_(Lieberman).3.22">Tosephta 3:22</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Rosh Hashanah 31b" href="/Rosh_Hashanah.31b">Babli <i>Roš Haššanah</i>31b</a> (in the name of R. Simeon ben Eleazar), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Keritot 9a" href="/Keritot.9a"><i>Keritut</i>9a</a>. <i>Sifry zuta Šelaḥ</i> explains the sacrifice as necessary before the proselyte will be permitted to partake of <i>sancta</i>, since every person whose body was the cause of his impurity, once he is pure he needs such a sacrifice to be admitted to <i>sancta</i>(cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 8:1:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.8.1.1">Note 1</a>).</i> A proselyte today has to bring for his nest a quarter of a silver {denar}. Rebbi Simeon said, Rabban Joḥanan ben Zakkai already disestablished this because of the mishap. What is “because of the mishap”? As was stated, today one does neither dedicate as sacrifice, nor dedicate one’s value, nor dedicate as <i>ḥerem</i>, nor does one collect [heave and tithes]<sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addtion from B, totally erroneous since heave and tithes are applicable today. Probably the addition “and tithes” is a scribal error in the ms. underlying B, since “heave and tithes” is a common expression. If “and tithes” is deleted, then the reference is not to heave from agricultural produce but to the money taken from the depository of <i>sheqalim</i> for use in the Temple. Therefore, this “lifting” is dedication as <i>sheqalim</i>.</i>. If somebody dedicates as sacrifice, or dedicated one’s value, or dedicated as <i>ḥerem</i>, or collected, cloth must be burned, an animal castrated. [How? One locks it in and it dies by itself.]<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addtion from B, inappropriate here. It is possible to be careful not to use an animal, but it must be prevented from producing offspring (even though castrating is sinful.)</i> Monies shall go to the Dead Sea<sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 66a" href="/Yoma.66a">Babli <i>Yoma</i>66a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bekhorot 23a" href="/Bekhorot.23a"><i>Bekhorot</i>23a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Avodah Zarah 13a" href="/Avodah_Zarah.13a"><i>Avodah zarah</i>13a</a>.</i>. If he<sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote">A person dedicating <i>sheqalim</i> does not sanctify his money according to R. Simeon; a proselyte dedicating money for his sacrifice in case the Temple will be rebuilt does sanctify the money set apart.</i> transgressed and dedicated, since Rebbi Simeon said, Rabban Joḥanan ben Zakkai already disestablished this because of the mishap, this implies if he transgressed and dedicated, it became sanctified. Rebbi Yudan from Antodria asked before Rebbi Yose: here you are saying it became sanctified, and there you are saying, it did not become sanctified<sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote">A person dedicating <i>sheqalim</i> does not sanctify his money according to R. Simeon; a proselyte dedicating money for his sacrifice in case the Temple will be rebuilt does sanctify the money set apart.</i>. He said to him, there <sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from B, best deleted as a wordy paraphrase of the text obtained by deletion.</i>[because of the following one may not dedicate from the start because it is an obligation to bring from the new contribution, and this would be from the old one. Here, what can you say? That one is old. But in respect to other dedications, the proselyte’s nest does not have to be from new money; if he dedicated it is holy;] maybe the Temple will be built like earlier and the heave of the lodge will be lifted on time on the first of Nisan<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote">Then any moneys set apart before the First of Adar are not admissible as new <i>sheqalim</i>; dedicating them before the Temple was rebuilt would be a self-defeating act.</i>. But here, what do you have? Rav Ada and Rav Hamnuna, Rav Ada bar Aḥawa in the name of Rav: Practice follows Rebbi Simeon<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Keritot 9a" href="/Keritot.9a">Babli <i>Keritut</i>9a</a>. The ruling refers to all of R. Simeon’s statements in this paragraph.</i>.
